Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi
Biographical introduction of Imam al-Sanusi's names, titles, and nisbahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity, lineage, and key attributes of Imam al-Sanusi as presented in his biographical introduction.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography reveals his intellectual and spiritual heritage.

This passage provides a detailed introduction to Imam al-Sanusi, a towering figure in Islamic theology. It lists his many titles, his full name, and explains the origins of his nisbahs (attributions), clarifying that 'al-Sanusi' refers to a Berber tribe and 'al-Tawhidi' indicates his specialization in the science of tawhid. The biography establishes his authority and context for his theological works.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical introduction
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: a heading followed by a list of honorifics, the full name, and then explanations of the nisbahs.
The passage is dense with titles; don't worry about memorizing all now.
2
Identify the epithets and full name
Find the list of attributes (e.g., 'master of theologians', 'Imam', 'hadith scholar') and the complete name 'Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf... al-Tawhidi'. Understand that these titles show his expertise across sciences.
The full name includes geographic and school affiliations: al-Tilimsani, al-Maliki, al-Ash'ari.
3
Understand the nisbah 'al-Sanusi'
The passage explains that 'al-Sanusi' is a tribal nisbah from the Berber tribe Sanusa, not a place name. This corrects a common misunderstanding.
Also note that his mother was a Hasanid noblewoman, indicating sharifian lineage.
4
Examine additional nisbahs
The passage mentions other nisbahs written in his own hand: al-'Aysi, al-Sharif, al-Qurashi, al-Qassar. Understand what they signify, especially 'al-Tawhidi' meaning devotion to tawhid.
These nisbahs reflect both lineage and scholarly focus.
5
Reflect on the purpose of the biography
Consider why a biographical introduction is placed at the start of a theological work: it establishes the author's credibility and situates his thought within Islamic scholarly tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي

شيخ متكلمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصـوفـي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي

والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في ) تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية(۱) ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية »(۲) ووجد بخطّهِ على « شرح الآجرومية » له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي

(۱) لعله أراد جدته أم أبيه كما سترى (۲) المَلالي : نسبة إلى مَلالة بوزان جَبَّانة ؛ قرية قرب بجاية، و«المواهب القدسية» : كذا في المخطوط الذي بين أيدينا ، وطبع باسم : المواهب القدوسية، والله أعلم . (۳) تاج العروس ( س ن س ) ، وانظر ( البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » ( ص ۲۳۷ )
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi

The master of the theologians of his time and his region, the Imam, the all-knowing, the versatile, the hadith scholar, the reciter, the jurist, the thorough fundamentalist, the Sufi, the pious, the abstinent: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu’ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash’ari al-Tawhidi.

And al-Sanusi: a relative attribution to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in 'Taj al-‘Arus': 'And to them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu’ayb al-Sanusi because he settled among them, and it is said: rather he is from them.' And his mother was a Hasanid noblewoman (1). Thus it was verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Mallali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (2). And found in his handwriting on his 'Sharh al-Ajurrumiyya': 'al-Sanusi al-‘Aysi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I say: al-‘Aysi: from the house of ‘Isa, and al-Tawhidi: a relative attribution to occupying oneself with the science of tawhid. Thus mentioned by al-Hifnawi.

(1) Perhaps he meant his grandmother, his father’s mother, as you will see. (2) al-Mallali: relative attribution to Mallala, on the weight of Jabbanah, a village near Bijaya. And 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' is as in the manuscript we have, and it was printed as 'al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya'. And Allah knows best. (3) Taj al-‘Arus (s-n-s), and see 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya’ wa al-‘Ulama’ bi Tilimsan' (p. 237).
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction. It begins with the heading 'Biography of Imam al-Sanusi'. Then it lists his epithets: master of theologians of his time and region, the Imam, the all-knowing, the versatile, hadith scholar, Quran reciter, jurist, thorough fundamentalist, Sufi, pious, abstinent. Then it gives his full name: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu’ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash’ari al-Tawhidi. Next, it explains his nisbah 'al-Sanusi' by attributing it to the tribe of Sanusa in the Maghreb, quoting al-Zabidi's 'Taj al-‘Arus' that he either settled among them or was from them, and notes his mother was a Hasanid noblewoman. It then mentions verification by Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Mallali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya'. It also reports that in his own handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya, he wrote additional nisbahs: al-‘Aysi, al-Sharif, al-Qurashi, al-Qassar. The author comments that al-‘Aysi means from the house of ‘Isa, and al-Tawhidi means devoted to the science of tawhid (monotheism), as al-Hifnawi mentioned. Finally, footnotes clarify possible errors and references.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think 'al-Sanusi' is a place name.
Correction: The passage explains it is a tribal nisbah from the Berber tribe Sanusa, not a location.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of the nisbah 'al-Tawhidi' according to the passage?
A) It means he is from the town of Tawhid.
B) It is a relative attribution to occupying oneself with the science of tawhid.
C) It indicates he was a follower of a specific theological school.
D) It is a family name from his grandfather.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi is introduced with his full lineage, titles, and the meaning of his key nisbahs, establishing his scholarly authority and background.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi was known by multiple noble lineages, but his true legacy came from his mastery of tawhid and piety. What one defining characteristic do you want to be known for in your life, and what specific action will you take today to move toward that identity?
?
He had titles like 'master of theologians' and 'the all-knowing', yet he remained devoted to the science of tawhid. Is there an area of your deen where you have become complacent or distracted, and what can you do this week to reorient your focus toward cultivating sincere knowledge and devotion?
?
His lineage includes both scholarly and noble blood, but the passage emphasizes his personal achievements. Are you relying on your family background or social status for your sense of worth, or are you actively building your own legacy of faith and learning? What is one step you can take to invest in your own spiritual growth today?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

Imam al-Sanusi's Biography and Scholarly Lineage
Introduces Imam al-Sanusi's name, titles, and nisbas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details and nisbas of Imam al-Sanusi that establish his scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A scholar’s nisbas tell the story of his tradition, tribe, and specialization.

This lesson introduces Imam al-Sanusi, a towering figure in Ash'ari theology and Islamic sciences. Before we study his arguments, it is essential to know who he was, his lineage, and the scholarly heritage he carried. The passage presents his honorifics, full name, and multiple nisbas that connect him to a Berber tribe, Tlemcen, Maliki school, Ash'ari school, and the science of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the full name and titles.
Notice the chain of nisbas.
2
Identify the main nisbas
List all the nisbas mentioned: al-Sanusi, al-Tilmisani, al-Maliki, al-Ash'ari, al-Tawhidi, al-'Isi, al-Sharif, al-Qurashi, al-Qassar.
Each nisba tells something about his origin or expertise.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on why scholars recorded these nisbas and what they indicate about authority.
This builds trust in the teacher.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي
شيخ متكلمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي
والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في « تاج العروس » : وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية » ووجد بخطه على « شرح الآجرومية » له : السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi: The master of the theologians of his age and his country, the imam, the most learned, the participant (in many sciences), the hadith specialist, the reciter, the jurist, the foundational scholar, the investigator, the Sufi, the pious, the abstinent; Abu ‘Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn ‘Umar ibn Shu‘ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilmisani al-Maliki al-Ash‘ari al-Tawhidi. And al-Sanusi is a nisba to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in Taj al-‘Arus: 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu ‘Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn ‘Umar ibn Shu‘ayb al-Sanusi because he stayed among them, and it is said he is from them. His mother was a sharifa from the Hasani line.' Thus verified by Sayyidi Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Malali in al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya. And it is found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-‘Isi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I say: al-‘Isi is from the house of ‘Isa, and al-Tawhidi is a nisba to engagement in the science of tawhid (divine unity), as mentioned by al-Hafnawi.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by listing his honorific titles, indicating his mastery across various Islamic sciences: theology (متكلم), hadith (محدث), Quran recitation (مقرئ), jurisprudence (فقيه), usul (أصولي), and spiritual discipline (صوفي). Then it gives his full name and multiple nisbas: al-Sanusi (from the Sanusa Berber tribe), al-Tilmisani (from Tlemcen), al-Maliki (legal school), al-Ash‘ari (theological school), and al-Tawhidi (specialist in tawhid). The passage explains the origin of 'al-Sanusi' through al-Zabidi's statement: either he stayed with the tribe or was from them, and his mother was a Hasanid sharifa. It also reports an annotation in the Imam's own hand on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya, giving additional nisbas: al-‘Isi (from the house of ‘Isa), al-Sharif, al-Qurashi, and al-Qassar. Finally, it clarifies that 'al-‘Isi' refers to a family lineage and 'al-Tawhidi' indicates his specialization in theology, as mentioned by al-Hafnawi. The passage thus establishes the Imam's scholarly and genealogical credentials.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'al-Sanusi' refers to a place name.
Correction: The text clarifies it is a nisba to a Berber tribe called Sanusa.

Checkpoint
What is the origin of the nisba 'al-Sanusi'?
A) It refers to a city in Morocco.
B) It refers to a Berber tribe called Sanusa.
C) It refers to a Sufi order.
D) It refers to a profession.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's many nisbas reflect his deep roots in scholarship, spirituality, and a Berber lineage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What are the 'nisbas' of your own faith journey? Which communities, teachers, or schools have shaped you, and do you honor them in your identity today?
?
Imam al-Sanusi carried both Berber and Sharifian lineage. How do you reconcile seemingly different aspects of your own background that others might view as contradictory? Can you find unity in them?
?
Your name might not reveal your scholarly lineage, but you do carry a tradition. Will you take a moment today to learn more about one of your own teachers or forebears in faith, so that you can be more aware of the chain that brought you here?

Dispute Over Imam al-Sanusi's Birth Year
Examines multiple reports on Imam al-Sanusi's birth year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars resolve conflicting reports about a historical figure's birth year, using Imam al-Sanusi as a case study.

Core Idea
Historical precision requires reconciling contradictory sources — even from the same student.

Imam al-Sanusi's birth year is not certain because neither he nor his student gave consistent information. This passage shows how later scholars handled the discrepancy, offering multiple estimates and leaving the matter to Allah. This lesson teaches you to read such historical evidence critically.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the different numbers mentioned: 63, 55, and 56 years.
Focus on how each number gives a different birth year when subtracted from his death year (895 AH).
2
Identify the two main narrations from al-Malali
The passage presents two reports from al-Malali via al-Tunbukti. One gives age at death as 63, the other gives age a year before death as 55. Calculate the birth years: 832 AH and 840 AH.
3
Understand the scholarly response
Notice how Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti refrained from giving a precise year, saying only 'after 830 AH'. Also note the third report from al-Balawi (56 at death). This shows careful handling of conflicting evidence.
The phrase 'wa Allah a‘lam' indicates humility before uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مولده ونشأته
اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي ؛ وسبب يرجع لعدم نصه هو على ذلك ، واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً ، قال العلامة التُنْبُكْتي في نيل الابتهاج : ( رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء : أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ ، فقال له : مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة )
فعلى هذه الرواية : تكون السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام السنوسي هي ( ٨٣٢هـ )
وفي نيل الابتهاج أيضاً نقل قول الملالي : ( وأخبرني قبل موته بنحو عام أنَّ سنه خمس وخمسون سنة ) ، فتكون سنة ولادته على هذا ( ٨٤٠هـ ) ، والله أعلم ، ولهذا اكتفى ابن مريم والتنبكتي بقولهما : ( مولده بعد الثلاثين وثمان مئة ) ، وانظر البستان ( ص ٢٤٤ ) ، وعندما ذكر العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي خبر وفاته في ثبته ( ص ٤٣٨ ) قال : ( وكانت سنه يومئذ ستاً وخمسين سنة )
His Birth and Upbringing: There is disagreement regarding the year of birth of Imam al-Sanusi; the reason being his lack of specifying it himself, and the inconsistency of the transmission of his student al-Malali concerning that as well. The scholar al-Tunbukti said in Nayl al-Ibtihaj: 'I saw a notation from some scholars: he asked al-Malali aforementioned about the age of the shaykh, and he said to him: He died at sixty-three years.' According to this narration, the year in which Imam al-Sanusi was born is 832 AH. And in Nayl al-Ibtihaj also, there is a transmission of al-Malali's statement: 'He informed me about a year before his death that his age was fifty-five years.' So his year of birth according to this is 840 AH. And Allah knows best. For this reason, Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti sufficed by saying: 'His birth was after thirty and eight hundred [i.e., after 830 AH].' And refer to al-Bustan (p. 244). And when the scholar Abu Ja‘far al-Balawi mentioned the news of his death in his Thabat (p. 438), he said: 'His age at that time was fifty-six years.'
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses the controversy over Imam al-Sanusi's birth year. The author attributes the disagreement to two factors: first, the Imam himself did not record his birth year; second, his student al-Malali gave inconsistent reports. The passage presents two specific narrations from al-Malali via al-Tunbukti's book Nayl al-Ibtihaj. The first report states that the Imam died at age 63, which would place his birth around 832 AH. The second report, also from al-Malali, says that about a year before his death, the Imam was 55 years old, implying a birth year of 840 AH. The passage then notes that later scholars like Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti preferred a more general statement: 'his birth was after thirty and eight hundred' (i.e., after 830 AH). It also references al-Bustan and a third report from Abu Ja‘far al-Balawi in his Thabat, which states that at the time of death the Imam was 56 years old. The passage thus systematically presents the conflicting evidence without resolving it, leaving the matter open with 'wa Allah a‘lam'.

Key Terms
مولده
ولادة
نيل الابتهاج
التنبكتي
الملالي
ابن مريم
البستان
ثبت البلوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think there is a single agreed-upon birth year for Imam al-Sanusi.
Correction: The passage shows multiple conflicting reports (832, 840, or simply after 830 AH), indicating uncertainty.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what years are suggested as possible birth years for Imam al-Sanusi?
A) 832 AH and 840 AH
B) 830 AH and 845 AH
C) 838 AH and 842 AH
D) 825 AH and 835 AH

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's birth year is uncertain, with reports ranging from 832 to 840 AH, and scholars expressed caution by giving a broader range.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When faced with conflicting information about something that matters to you, do you rush to pick a comfortable answer, or do you, like these scholars, patiently hold to a cautious range? What would it look like for you to say 'Allahu a'lam' in a situation where you don't know?
?
Imam al-Sanusi himself did not record his birth year—his focus was elsewhere. What do you spend time recording and preserving? Is it centered on what truly endures, or on things that will be forgotten?
?
The contradiction in al-Malali's testimony could have been ignored or smoothed over, but the scholars transmitted it openly. Are you honest about your own inconsistencies and uncertainties, or do you present a polished version of yourself? What would change if you embraced the messiness of your own history?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Imam Sanusi's Upbringing and Family Background
Describes Sanusi's upbringing, his father's virtues, and his teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the formative environment of Imam al-Sanusi, including his family's piety and scholarship, and the influence of his father and teachers.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's upbringing in a household of virtue and knowledge shaped his spiritual and intellectual path.

Imam al-Sanusi did not emerge from a vacuum. His deep scholarship and spirituality were nurtured in a home steeped in piety and learning, and under the guidance of righteous teachers. This lesson explores the family background and early education that prepared him for his monumental role in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read about his family home and father's qualities
Read the passage carefully, noting the description of Sanusi's father as a righteous, ascetic scholar. Consider how this environment influenced Sanusi.
2
Note his grandmother's lineage and al-Mallali's testimony
The passage mentions that Sanusi's paternal grandmother was Hasaniyya, linking him to the Prophet's lineage through al-Hasan. Also, read al-Mallali's detailed praise of the father's character.
3
Consider the role of Tlemcen and his teachers
Reflect on why Tlemcen is described as a 'capital of knowledge' and how studying under major scholars and receiving attention from saints contributed to Sanusi's development.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم ؛ فوالده هو الشيخ الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب(۱)، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم ، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها ، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنيّة النسب ، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه (۲) ، وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام : ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه . . رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً ، خاشعاً الله تعالى زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها ، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى ، سالم الصدر ، حسن الأخلاق ، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه ، حسن المعاشرة ، كريم الطبع )(٣) وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب ، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أن عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته ، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته. شيوخ. أخذ الإمام السنوسي العلم عن جلة علماء عصره ، ونالته عناية ولحظات الأولياء والصالحين
Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge. His father was the righteous, ascetic, humble, accomplished teacher Yusuf Abu Ya'qub (1). From him the Imam took the principles of knowledge. That was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge in its day, the clay of the saints and righteous. The maternal grandmother of Imam al-Sanusi on his father's side was Hasaniyya in lineage, therefore Imam al-Sanusi may be called al-Hasani on account of his father's mother (2). And Shaykh al-Mallali said describing the Imam's father: 'Sayyidi Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son... was a righteous, devout man, humble before Allah, ascetic in this world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience of Allah, pure of heart, good of character, smiling in the face of everyone he met, good in companionship, generous in nature' (3). And the profession of this blessed father was teaching the Qur'an to children in the maktab. And it appears from the words of Shaykh al-Mallali that divine care accompanied him from his childhood, so Allah brought about miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight. Teachers. Imam al-Sanusi took knowledge from the great scholars of his time, and he received the attention and glances of the saints and righteous.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage describes Imam Sanusi's upbringing and education. It begins by stating he grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge. His father was Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, a pious, ascetic, and accomplished scholar. From him, the Imam learned the fundamentals of knowledge. This took place in Tlemcen, then a center of learning and a city of saints and righteous people. His paternal grandmother was Hasaniyya in lineage, so the Imam is sometimes called al-Hasani through her. Then the passage quotes al-Mallali's description of the father: a righteous, God-fearing, ascetic man, turning away from the world, devoted to obedience, pure-hearted, good-natured, smiling at everyone, generous. His profession was teaching the Quran to children in a maktab. Al-Mallali indicates that divine care accompanied him from childhood, and God granted him miracles and insight. Then the passage mentions his teachers: he studied under the major scholars of his time and received the attention and blessings of the awliya and righteous.

Correction: The passage shows that his father was a saintly figure, described as righteous, ascetic, and possessed of miracles, and he was an accomplished teacher from whom Sanusi learned the principles of knowledge.

Sanusi describes his noble lineage and his father's pious character.

Learning Objective

Imam al-Sanusi begins his work by establishing his own credentials through his lineage and upbringing. Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a house of virtue and knowledge; his father was the righteous, ascetic, humble, verifying teacher Yusuf Abu Ya'qub(1), and from him the Imam took the principles of the sciences. That was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge in its day, the clay of saints and righteous ones. The Imam's paternal grandmother was of Hasani lineage, so the Imam may be called al-Hasani through his father's mother(2). Shaykh al-Mallali said describing the Imam's father: 'My master Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son... was a righteous, pious man, humble before Allah, ascetic in the world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to Allah, pure of heart, good of character, smiling in the face of everyone he met, good in companionship, noble in nature(3).' Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Sanusi. It first states that he grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge, identifying his father as the righteous, ascetic, and verifying teacher Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, from whom he learned the foundational sciences. The location is Tlemcen, described as the center of learning and the abode of saints. It then mentions that his paternal grandmother was of Hasani lineage (descendant of Imam Hasan), explaining why al-Sanusi is sometimes called al-Hasani. The author then quotes Shaykh al-Mallali's description of the father, emphasizing his piety, asceticism, humility, good character, and his profession of teaching the Quran to children. It notes that from childhood, Allah granted him miracles and spiritual insight. The passage concludes by stating that al-Sanusi studied under the leading scholars of his era and received divine attention through the saints.

Sanusi's Chain in the Seven Qira'at
Al-Balawi reports Sanusi's study of the seven qira'at.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly authority of Imam al-Sanusi in the seven qira'at and the structure of his transmission chain.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's ijaza in qira'at connects him through a verified chain to the masters.

This passage from al-Balawi's work documents Imam al-Sanusi's direct study and ijaza in the seven canonical Quranic recitations. It reveals the rigorous process of oral transmission and the high standing of his teachers. As you read, notice the detailed descriptions of each teacher and the precise method of recitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand the overall report.
The passage is a quote from al-Balawi.
2
Identify the main teachers
Find the names of the teachers al-Sanusi studied under: Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani, al-Yaznasni, and al-Luja'i. Note their descriptions.
Each teacher is described with multiple honorifics.
3
Understand the method of study
Notice the terms: khatma (complete reading), ijaza (license), and the books al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. This shows the formal process.
4
Trace the chain of transmission
Observe that al-Sanusi's teachers themselves received from earlier authorities (al-Qaysi and Ibn Makhkhut). This establishes a continuous isnad.
The chain is important for authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن ( التيسير ) و ( الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة البقرة ) ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي ، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما )(۱) ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر (۱) انظر « ثبت أبي جعفر البلوي الوادي آشي » ( ص ٤٣٨ ) .
And the Imam al-Sanusi had a high standing in the compilation of the qira'at (modes of recitation). For al-Allama Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven qira'at from the faqih, teacher, scholar, practitioner, verifier, reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete readings (khatmat). He said: I added from a third a good amount whose limit I have not verified now, as a compilation of the seven according to the contents of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he granted him a general absolute ijaza in the seven modes of recitation and in other of his narrations. And he narrated the seven to him from the two imam scholars teachers: the venerable, most renowned, verifier reciter, the perceiving, humble teacher Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi Imran Musa al-Yaznasni; and the venerable, exalted, famous, verifier, precise, accurate, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, most pure teacher Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn al-faqih al-alim al-mutafannin Abi Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Isa al-Luja'i. He recited to the first as a compilation in one complete reading of the seven; he said: I added three ahzab from Surat al-Baqara. And to the second for Surat al-Fatiha, al-Baqara, and the beginnings of Al Imran, as a compilation of the seven, and he granted ijaza for what he recited and for the remainder. Both of them narrated together that from the two teachers: Abu Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut with their chains.' And among the scholars from whom he read was: Shaykh al-Allama Nasr. (1) See 'Thabit Abi Ja'far al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashi' (p. 438).
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a proof of Imam al-Sanusi's scholarly authority in the field of qira'at. It begins by stating his high rank in compiling the modes of Quranic recitation. The main evidence is a direct quotation from the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, who relates that al-Sanusi studied the seven qira'at under several teachers. First, he recited to Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani in two complete recitations and added a third partial one, mastering the seven according to the famous texts al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya, and received a general ijaza. Then, the text lists two other teachers: al-Yaznasni and al-Luja'i, each described with numerous laudatory epithets emphasizing their authority. For the first, al-Sanusi recited a complete compilation of the seven qira'at and added three ahzab from Sura al-Baqara. For the second, he recited a compilation of the seven for specific surahs and received ijaza. Both teachers transmitted from two earlier authorities, establishing a continuous chain of transmission. Finally, the passage mentions another teacher, Shaykh al-Allama Nasr, though the footnote refers to additional source documentation.

Al-Sanusi's Mastery of the Seven Qira'at
al-Balawi reports al-Sanusi's qira'at education in detail.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed chain of transmission through which al-Sanusi mastered the seven modes of Qur'anic recitation (al-qira'at al-sab').

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's qira'at training connected him to a living chain of masters.

In this lesson, we examine the specific report of Abu Ja'far al-Balawi detailing how al-Sanusi studied the seven qira'at. The passage reveals the rigorous method of multiple recitations (khatmat) and the formal authorization (ijaza) he received. This illustrates the traditional pathway of mastering Qur'anic recitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from al-Balawi
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'أخذ القراءات السبع' and ends with 'بسندهما'. Then read the English translation. Notice the technical terms.
Focus on the names and the phrases 'ختمتين', 'جمعاً للسبعة', 'إجازة مطلقة'.
2
Identify the three teachers mentioned in the chain
Find the names of the teachers from whom al-Sanusi directly or indirectly learned the qira'at. List them in order: Abu al-Hajjaj, al-Yaznasani, al-Laja'i.
3
Understand the teaching method
Note the process: al-Sanusi recited to them in complete recitations (khatmat). He compiled all seven qira'at according to two famous texts (al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya). He received a general ijaza.
This shows the importance of oral transmission and authorization.
4
Recognize the chain's significance
Reflect on the fact that al-Sanusi's chain goes back through multiple verifiers. This placed him in a direct line of authoritative transmission.
This is a key part of his scholarly identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن ( التيسير ) و ( الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة البقرة ) ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي ، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما)(۱) ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر أحمد الزواوي ، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ( الإرشاد » لإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد
And the Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the compilation of the Qira'at ; for the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: (He took the seven Qira'at from the jurist, the master, the scholar, the worker, the verifier, the reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: And I added from the third a suitable amount whose limit I have not verified now, compiling the seven according to the content of (al-Taysir) and (al-Shatibiyya), and he authorized him in the seven recitations and in other of his transmitted works with an absolute general authorization. And he narrated to him by the seven from the two venerable teaching imams: the eminent, most renowned, well-known reciter, verifier, perceptive, humble master Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasani, and the eminent, magnified, famous, verifier, precise, accurate, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, most pious master Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn the jurist, erudite scholar Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Laja'i, reading to the first a compilation in one complete recitation for the seven. He said: And I added three parts from Surat al-Baqara), and to the second for (Surat al-Fatiha) and (al-Baqara) and the beginnings of (Al 'Imran) as a compilation for the seven, and an authorization for what he read and for what remained. Both of them narrated to him together that from the two masters: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi, and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhkut, with their chains of transmission.)(1) And among the scholars under whom he studied: the shaykh, the scholar Nasr Ahmad al-Zawawi, and the shaykh, the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sinhaji al-Sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, he took from him the seven Qira'at, and the shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Maghili known as al-Jallab, he took from him jurisprudence, and the just scholar Abu 'Abd Allah al-Habbak, he took from him the science of the astrolabe, and the imam Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-Tilimsani, he read to him usul (principles), logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence, and the memorizer Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother, he read to him (al-Risala), and he and his brother both read to the pious, righteous imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi (al-Irshad) of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This is a biographical passage that first reports, through a quote from Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, the details of Imam al-Sanusi's education in the seven modes of Qur'anic recitation (al-qira'at al-sab'). The quote explains that al-Sanusi recited the seven qira'at to Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani in two complete readings (khatmatayn), and added a third partial reading. He also received authorization (ijaza) from him. Al-Balawi also narrates that al-Sanusi heard the seven from two other teachers, al-Yaznasani and al-Laja'i, with additional details about what was read to each. Then the passage lists other scholars under whom al-Sanusi studied various sciences: Nasr al-Zawawi and Muhammad ibn Tumart for qira'at, al-Jallab for fiqh, al-Habbak for astronomy, al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh, and his maternal brother al-Taluti for al-Risala of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani. Finally, he and his brother studied al-Irshad of al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi. The passage demonstrates al-Sanusi's wide-ranging education across transmitted and rational sciences.

Al-Balawi's quote ends; then the author lists other teachers.

وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن ( التيسير ) و ( الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة البقرة ) ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي ، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما)(۱) ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر أحمد الزواوي ، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ( الإرشاد » لإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد
And the Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the compilation of the Qira'at ; for the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: (He took the seven Qira'at from the jurist, the master, the scholar, the worker, the verifier, the reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: And I added from the third a suitable amount whose limit I have not verified now, compiling the seven according to the content of (al-Taysir) and (al-Shatibiyya), and he authorized him in the seven recitations and in other of his transmitted works with an absolute general authorization. And he narrated to him by the seven from the two venerable teaching imams: the eminent, most renowned, well-known reciter, verifier, perceptive, humble master Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasani, and the eminent, magnified, famous, verifier, precise, accurate, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, most pious master Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn the jurist, erudite scholar Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Laja'i, reading to the first a compilation in one complete recitation for the seven. He said: And I added three parts from Surat al-Baqara), and to the second for (Surat al-Fatiha) and (al-Baqara) and the beginnings of (Al 'Imran) as a compilation for the seven, and an authorization for what he read and for what remained. Both of them narrated to him together that from the two masters: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi, and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhkut, with their chains of transmission.)(1) And among the scholars under whom he studied: the shaykh, the scholar Nasr Ahmad al-Zawawi, and the shaykh, the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sinhaji al-Sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, he took from him the seven Qira'at, and the shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Maghili known as al-Jallab, he took from him jurisprudence, and the just scholar Abu 'Abd Allah al-Habbak, he took from him the science of the astrolabe, and the imam Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-Tilimsani, he read to him usul (principles), logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence, and the memorizer Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother, he read to him (al-Risala), and he and his brother both read to the pious, righteous imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi (al-Irshad) of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This is a biographical passage that first reports, through a quote from Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, the details of Imam al-Sanusi's education in the seven modes of Qur'anic recitation (al-qira'at al-sab'). The quote explains that al-Sanusi recited the seven qira'at to Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani in two complete readings (khatmatayn), and added a third partial reading. He also received authorization (ijaza) from him. Al-Balawi also narrates that al-Sanusi heard the seven from two other teachers, al-Yaznasani and al-Laja'i, with additional details about what was read to each. Then the passage lists other scholars under whom al-Sanusi studied various sciences: Nasr al-Zawawi and Muhammad ibn Tumart for qira'at, al-Jallab for fiqh, al-Habbak for astronomy, al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh, and his maternal brother al-Taluti for al-Risala of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani. Finally, he and his brother studied al-Irshad of al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid with Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi. The passage demonstrates al-Sanusi's wide-ranging education across transmitted and rational sciences.

Al-Sanusi's Teachers in Hadith and Inheritance
Al-Sanusi's study of hadith, fara'id, and ijazat from scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key teachers from whom al-Sanusi studied hadith sciences and the laws of inheritance, and the significance of the ijazat he received.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's education combined sacred hadith transmission with precise inheritance law from multiple masters.

This passage from al-Sanusi's biography highlights his dedicated study of two essential Islamic sciences: hadith and fara'id (inheritance law). It names the prominent scholars he learned from and describes the authorizations (ijazat) he earned. As you read, notice how his training in both transmitted and rational sciences reflects the comprehensive scholarship of his time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith teacher
Locate the name of the scholar under whom al-Sanusi studied hadith transmission. Note what he narrated and the type of authorization given.
The teacher is Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi.
2
Examine the fara'id teacher
Find the scholar who taught al-Sanusi the laws of inheritance and arithmetic. Note the scope of the ijaza granted.
The teacher is Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi.
3
Notice additional authorizations
The passage mentions a third scholar, Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif, who also authorized al-Sanusi. Understand that multiple ijazat were common for comprehensive training.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ) الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد (۲)
And he occupied himself with transmission and the sciences of tradition under the pious, righteous imam Abu Zayd 'Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, and he narrated from him (al-Sahihan) and other books of hadith and tradition, and he authorized him with what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat and others. And he read the laws of inheritance and arithmetic under the eminent scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he authorized him with all that he narrates, as also authorized him Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid (2).
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage continues the biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's education, focusing on his studies in hadith and related sciences. It states that he engaged in riwaya (transmission) and 'ulum al-athar (sciences of tradition, i.e., hadith) under Abu Zayd 'Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi. From him, al-Sanusi narrated the two authentic collections (al-Sahihan of Bukhari and Muslim) and other books of hadith and tradition. Al-Tha'alibi granted him a general authorization (ijaza) and made him hear (asma'ahu) the musalsalat (chains of transmission with a particular feature) and other works. Then the passage mentions that al-Sanusi studied fara'id (laws of inheritance) and hisab (arithmetic) under Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, who also authorized him with all that he narrates. Additionally, Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif authorized him on the authority of his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. This shows al-Sanusi's comprehensive studies in both transmitted and rational sciences, with formal authorizations from multiple scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'المسلسلات' is a book title or a specific genre of hadith collection.
Correction: Musalsalat refers to hadiths with a distinctive feature in their chain of transmission, such as all narrators shaking hands, not a specific book.

D) Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Sanusi sought out multiple specialized teachers for different sciences. In your own pursuit of knowledge, do you have real teachers who hold chains of transmission (sanad)? If not, what is stopping you from seeking them, and how long will you let that excuse remain?
?
He studied both transmitted knowledge (hadith) and rational sciences (arithmetic). Which of these two domains do you neglect? What concrete change will you make today to restore balance in your learning?
?
Receiving ijaza meant al-Sanusi was authorized to teach. You consume Islamic content daily, but who has authorized your teachers? And more importantly, who will authorize you to pass on what you learn? What will you do about that accountability?

Ahmad (1) 6 And al-Shaykh al-Zawawi, and the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji al-Sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani; he learned the seven qira'at from him. And al-Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Bu Isa al-Maghili known as al-Jallab; he learned fiqh from him. And the just scholar Abu Abd Allah al-Habbak; he learned the science of the astrolabe from him. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani; he read usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh to him. And the hadith master Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother; he read 'al-Risala' to him, and he and his brother read 'al-Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid to the pious and righteous Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi. And he occupied himself with hadith transmission and the sciences of athar under the pious and righteous Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi; so he narrated from him the two Sahihs and other books of hadith and athar, and he granted him ijaza for what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him listen to the musalsalat and others. And he read fara'id and arithmetic under the illustrious scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him ijaza for everything he narrates, as also granted him ijaza Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. (1) And it is said: 'Tuzat' instead of 'Tumart', and he is not Ibn Tumart the Mahdi of the Almohads, as is not hidden. (2) That was mentioned by the scholar Muhammad Makhluf in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). = 15. The scholar al-Balawi said: 'And he learned from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their great ones: the saint of Allah, the Imam, the scholar, the righteous Abu Ali al-Ahsin known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas (but he did not take much from him) and others. And he also studied under our shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn Marzuq, and our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the furu' faqih Abu Abd Allah al-Jallab, and the illustrious faqih Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabili, author of the versification of 'al-Mukhtasar'; I think he studied under him. 'And he learned the science of arithmetic and fara'id from the outstanding faqih in them, Abu Abd Allah ibn Tumart, and he also learned from his brother mentioned earlier, and from those whom his student, our companion, the distinguished, accomplished, blessed faqih Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in his book 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.' His Sufism and moral training: There are great spiritual personalities by whom Imam al-Sanusi was influenced, but it appears that the shaykh, the saint, the gnostic, the righteous Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran... was the one with the greatest impact on Imam al-Sanusi from this aspect. And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fihris al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi and Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi and from others. He said: 'And he has a small register (thabt) in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of 'al-Awwaliyya' and the hadith of 'al-Diyafa 'ala al-Aswadayn' and al-Musafaha and al-Mushabaka and wearing the khirqa and handing the subha and talqin al-dhikr by way of his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Sanusi's education and spiritual training. It begins by listing his teachers in various Islamic sciences: he studied the seven modes of Quranic recitation (qira'at) under al-Shaykh al-Zawawi and Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji. He learned fiqh under al-Maghili (al-Jallab). He studied the science of the astrolabe under al-Habbak. He read principles (usul), logic, rhetoric, and fiqh under Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani. Under his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti, he read the Risala (likely of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani), and together they read al-Juwayni's al-Irshad and the science of tawhid under al-Kanabishi. For hadith and athar, he studied under al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and received ijaza. He studied fara'id and arithmetic under al-Qalasadi and received ijaza from him and from Ibn Marzuq. The passage then includes a footnote clarifying that Ibn Tumart is not the Mahdi of the Almohads. Next, a quotation from al-Balawi adds more teachers from his town, including 'Abarkan', Ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Jallab, al-Ghurabili, and Ibn Tumart (the arithmetic teacher). The second major section focuses on his Sufi and moral training (tasawwuf wa tarbiyatuhu al-akhlaqiyya). It notes that many spiritual figures influenced him, but the greatest was Ibrahim al-Tazi, a saintly gnostic resident of Oran. Finally, al-Kattani reports that al-Sanusi had a general ijaza from al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and that he possessed a small thabt (register) containing chains of transmission for specific hadith and Sufi practices like musafaha (shaking hands), mushabaka (interlacing fingers), wearing the khirqa (Sufi cloak), handling the subha (prayer beads), and talqin al-dhikr (teaching the remembrance), all from his shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi. This demonstrates the integration of hadith scholarship with Sufi practices.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Ibn Tumart mentioned here is the founder of the Almohad movement.
Correction: The footnote explicitly states that this Ibn Tumart is not the Mahdi of the Almohads; it is a different person, possibly with a different name (Tuzat).

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi received a comprehensive education in both transmitted and rational sciences from a wide network of scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about Imam al-Sanusi's dedication to learning from many teachers across diverse sciences. How many teachers have you sought out for your own religious knowledge? Are you satisfied with acquiring knowledge from a single source, or do you actively seek multiple scholars to broaden your understanding? What steps will you take this week to find a teacher for a subject you have neglected?
?
Al-Sanusi mastered both transmitted and rational sciences. Do you have any area of Islamic knowledge that you have ignored because it seemed difficult or irrelevant? What is one 'astrolabe' or 'arithmetic' of Islamic learning that you have been avoiding? Will you commit to learning it, even if it requires effort?
?
Notice how al-Sanusi received ijazas from his teachers, ensuring connected chains of transmission. Do you care about the chains of transmission for the knowledge you consume? How can you verify that what you learn is authentically transmitted from reliable sources? What is one step you can take today to ensure the knowledge you rely on is sound?

Imam al-Sanusi's Sufi Training and Spiritual Influence
Description of Sufi influence and a thabt containing chains for practices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Sufi influence on Imam al-Sanusi, especially through Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi, and the nature of his spiritual practices as recorded in his thabt.

Core Idea
The greatest spiritual influence on Imam al-Sanusi came from Ibrahim al-Tazi of Oran.

This lesson focuses on Imam al-Sanusi's Sufi training and moral upbringing. While many spiritual figures influenced him, the passage highlights Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi as having the greatest impact. It also describes a small register (thabt) containing chains for Sufi practices like wearing the khirqa and talqin al-dhikr, showing how al-Sanusi integrated hadith transmission with Sufi discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key spiritual influence
Read the first part of the passage which states that there were many spiritual personalities, but the one with the greatest impact was Ibrahim al-Tazi.
Notice the emphasis on 'al-athar al-akbar' (the greatest impact).
2
Understand the thabt
The passage mentions a small register (thabt) by al-Sanusi that contains chains for specific hadith and Sufi practices. Read the list: hadith al-awwaliyya, hadith al-diyafa, musafaha, mushabaka, wearing khirqa, handing subha, and talqin al-dhikr.
This shows how al-Sanusi preserved chains for Sufi transmission.
3
Note the chain of transmission
All these practices are traced back to his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi. Reflect on the importance of isnad in both hadith and Sufi traditions.

Ahmad (1) 6 And al-Shaykh al-Zawawi, and the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji al-Sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani; he learned the seven qira'at from him. And al-Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Bu Isa al-Maghili known as al-Jallab; he learned fiqh from him. And the just scholar Abu Abd Allah al-Habbak; he learned the science of the astrolabe from him. And Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani; he read usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh to him. And the hadith master Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother; he read 'al-Risala' to him, and he and his brother read 'al-Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid to the pious and righteous Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi. And he occupied himself with hadith transmission and the sciences of athar under the pious and righteous Imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi; so he narrated from him the two Sahihs and other books of hadith and athar, and he granted him ijaza for what is permissible for him and from him, and he made him listen to the musalsalat and others. And he read fara'id and arithmetic under the illustrious scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him ijaza for everything he narrates, as also granted him ijaza Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid. (1) And it is said: 'Tuzat' instead of 'Tumart', and he is not Ibn Tumart the Mahdi of the Almohads, as is not hidden. (2) That was mentioned by the scholar Muhammad Makhluf in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). = 15. The scholar al-Balawi said: 'And he learned from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their great ones: the saint of Allah, the Imam, the scholar, the righteous Abu Ali al-Ahsin known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas (but he did not take much from him) and others. And he also studied under our shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn Marzuq, and our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the furu' faqih Abu Abd Allah al-Jallab, and the illustrious faqih Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabili, author of the versification of 'al-Mukhtasar'; I think he studied under him. 'And he learned the science of arithmetic and fara'id from the outstanding faqih in them, Abu Abd Allah ibn Tumart, and he also learned from his brother mentioned earlier, and from those whom his student, our companion, the distinguished, accomplished, blessed faqih Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in his book 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.' His Sufism and moral training: There are great spiritual personalities by whom Imam al-Sanusi was influenced, but it appears that the shaykh, the saint, the gnostic, the righteous Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran... was the one with the greatest impact on Imam al-Sanusi from this aspect. And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fihris al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general ijaza from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi and Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi and from others. He said: 'And he has a small register (thabt) in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of 'al-Awwaliyya' and the hadith of 'al-Diyafa 'ala al-Aswadayn' and al-Musafaha and al-Mushabaka and wearing the khirqa and handing the subha and talqin al-dhikr by way of his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.'

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Sanusi's education and spiritual training. It begins by listing his teachers in various Islamic sciences: he studied the seven modes of Quranic recitation (qira'at) under al-Shaykh al-Zawawi and Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji. For hadith and athar, he studied under al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and received ijaza. He studied fara'id and arithmetic under al-Qalasadi and received ijaza from him and from Ibn Marzuq. The passage then includes a footnote clarifying that Ibn Tumart is not the Mahdi of the Almohads. The second major section focuses on his Sufi and moral training (tasawwuf wa tarbiyatuhu al-akhlaqiyya). Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Sanusi's Teachers: The Chain of Knowledge
Al-Balawi enumerates Sanusi's teachers in various fields.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of the teacher-student chain (isnad) in Islamic scholarship through the example of Imam Sanusi's teachers.

Core Idea
The chain of teachers connects every scholar to the Prophet.

This passage from al-Balawi lists the distinguished scholars from whom Imam Sanusi acquired knowledge. It highlights the traditional Islamic emphasis on personal transmission from teacher to student. By examining this list, we see the breadth of Sanusi's education and the network of scholars that shaped him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the names and the fields of knowledge mentioned.
Pay attention to phrases like 'وأخذ من شيوخ بلده' (he took from the scholars of his town).
2
Identify the types of teachers
Note that some teachers are described as spiritual figures (ولي الله), others as jurists (فقيه), and one as a specialist in arithmetic and inheritance.
The variety shows the comprehensive scope of Sanusi's education.
3
Reflect on the significance of the list
Think about why al-Balawi and later scholars compiled such lists. How does this practice preserve the authenticity of knowledge?
In Islamic tradition, knowing the chain of transmission (isnad) is crucial for verifying knowledge.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم، ومن أكابرهم : ولي الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبـركـان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، « وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به )
Al-Allamah al-Balawi said: (He took from the scholars of his town from a group of our shuyukh and others, and among their most senior: the saint of Allah, the imam, the scholar, the righteous Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him, and others. And he also took from our shaykh Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq, and our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the jurisprudential faqih Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the noble faqih Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of the versification of al-Mukhtasar — I think he took from him. And he took the knowledge of arithmetic and inheritance shares from the distinguished faqih in them Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his brother mentioned previously, and from these (he took) as his student, our companion the noble and accomplished blessed faqih Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in the book 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list of the teachers from whom Imam Sanusi studied. Al-Allamah al-Balawi is the source. The list includes scholars from various fields: spiritual figures, hadith scholars, jurists, and specialists in arithmetic and inheritance. The passage notes that Sanusi studied with these shuyukh either directly or through others, and that his student al-Mallali recorded these teachers in a work titled 'al-Ta'rif bihi' (the introduction to him). The enumeration follows the author's own order, first mentioning the most senior, then others, and finally specialists in specific sciences.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi studied under a diverse group of scholars, emphasizing the traditional Islamic model of knowledge transmission through personal chains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that Sanusi studied under multiple teachers from different fields. Are you content with learning from only one source or method, or do you actively seek diverse teachers and subjects? What is one specific area of Islamic knowledge you have neglected that you can begin learning this week?
?
Sanusi's student al-Mallali recorded his teacher's teachers in a book. Do you know the names of the scholars you have learned from? Take a moment to write down at least three teachers—living or deceased—whom you owe a debt of knowledge. Have you ever thanked them or prayed for them?
?
The passage includes a phrase 'I think he took from him,' showing scholarly caution. When you transmit knowledge, are you careful to attribute it correctly, or do you speak without verifying? Commit today to only share what you have learned from reliable teachers and to be honest about uncertainty.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

The Spiritual Influence of Ibrahim al-Tazi on Imam Sanusi
Describes Sanusi's Sufi training and the impact of Ibrahim al-Tazi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Sanusi's spiritual and ethical formation was shaped by the saintly scholar Ibrahim al-Tazi, and how this relationship is reflected in chains of transmission.

Core Idea
Sanusi's spiritual training was anchored in a living saint who embodied knowledge and virtue.

This passage reveals a crucial dimension of Imam Sanusi's formation: his Sufi training under the guidance of Ibrahim al-Tazi. While Sanusi was influenced by many, al-Tazi stands out for his combination of deep scholarship and saintly character. The passage also shows how Sanusi preserved this spiritual connection through a small thabt listing specific hadiths and practices he received from al-Tazi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the heading about his 'Sufism and ethical upbringing' and how the passage focuses on one key figure.
This is a biographical and hagiographical account, not a theological argument.
2
Identify al-Tazi's qualities
From the description, list the scholarly and saintly attributes of Ibrahim al-Tazi. How does the author combine his knowledge with his spiritual rank?
Look for phrases like 'imamate in Quran' and 'manners of the saints'.
3
Examine the long quotation
The quote from al-Tanbakti paints a vivid picture of al-Tazi's reputation. What does it tell us about how he was perceived by others?
Proverbs were made of his intellect and forbearance—this shows his iconic status.
4
Analyze the thabt
The second part mentions a small thabt containing chains for specific hadiths and practices. What does this list (khirqa, subha, talqin dhikr) indicate about the nature of transmission?
These are not just texts but lived practices passed from master to disciple.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Reflect on how the two parts of the passage together show the integration of scholarly and spiritual transmission in Sanusi's education.
This challenges the idea that Sufi training is separate from formal scholarship.

تصوفة وتربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من هذا الجانب؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه .. كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في «نيل الابتهاج ) عن ابن صعد صاحب ( النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من جلالته وسعادته : أنَّ المثل ضرب بعقله وحلمه ، واشتهر في الآفاق ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن ؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال : كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي ، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال : لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا ؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق ، والصبر على المكاره ، واصطناع المعروف للناس والمداراة ، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه ، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته ، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة ، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة ؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة ، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار ((۱)
وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ( فهرس الفهارس ) ( ۲/ ۹۹۹ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي )
His Sufism and his ethical upbringing. There are great spiritual personalities by whom Imam Sanusi was influenced, but what appears is that the shaykh, the saint, the gnostic, the righteous Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran, was the one with the greatest impact on Imam Sanusi from this aspect. For in addition to his imamate in the sciences of the Quran and linguistics, and his memorization of hadiths, and his extensive knowledge of fiqh and its principles, and his sharp insight and understanding, he was endowed with the manners of the saints and the perfect ones. Al-Allamah al-Tanbakti narrated in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' from Ibn Sa'd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thaqib': (Sufficient for you regarding his majesty and blessedness is that proverbs were made of his intellect and forbearance, and mention of his virtue and knowledge became famous in the horizons until now. If someone exaggerated in describing a man, he said: 'He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi.' And if one of them became filled with rage, he said: 'If I were in the station of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have endured this,' because of what he used to endure from harm of people, and patience in hardships, and doing good to people, and showing leniency. So he is one whom Allah manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller for the spread of his miracles, clothed in the garment of love and awe, along with his acceptance in the hearts of the elite and the common. So he called them to Allah with insight, and guided them to His servitude through the beliefs of tawhid and the functions of dhikr.) And al-Allamah al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fahras al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam Sanusi used to narrate by general ijazah from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi and Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi and others. He said: (He has a small thabt in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of al-Awwaliyya and the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, and the handshake and interlocking of fingers, and wearing the khirqa, and handing the subha, and talqin of dhikr via the route of his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage combines biographical and hagiographical material about Imam Sanusi's spiritual training. It begins with a heading 'His Sufism and his ethical upbringing', then states that while many spiritual figures influenced Sanusi, the most significant was Ibrahim al-Tazi. The author describes al-Tazi's scholarly accomplishments (Quran, linguistics, hadith, fiqh) and his saintly character. Then a long quote from al-Tanbakti's 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' praises al-Tazi's wisdom, patience, and role as a spiritual guide. Finally, a quote from al-Kattani's 'Fahras al-Faharis' notes that Sanusi had a small thabt (a list of chains) that included specific hadiths and practices (like wearing the khirqa, using a subha, and talqin of dhikr) transmitted from al-Tazi. The passage shows the integration of scholarly and spiritual transmission.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sufi training has no connection to hadith transmission or scholarly credentials.
Correction: This passage shows that Sanusi's spiritual guide, al-Tazi, was both a scholar and a saint, and Sanusi preserved transmissions of rituals like dhikr and khirqa through a thabt, showing integration.

Checkpoint

D) He wrote a book called 'al-Najm al-Thaqib'

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's spiritual formation was inseparable from his scholarly training; his relationship with Ibrahim al-Tazi exemplifies the integration of knowledge and piety in Islamic tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibrahim al-Tazi's forbearance was so legendary that people said, 'If I were in his station, I would not have endured this.' Think of a person or situation that has tested your patience recently. What would change if you saw that person or situation as an opportunity to embody the patience of a saint? Will you ask Allah tonight for a portion of that forbearance, starting with that specific situation?
?
The passage says al-Tazi was 'clothed in the garment of love and awe.' When you interact with others—especially those who irritate you or are hard to love—do you wear that garment? Reflect on one relationship where you have been more harsh than merciful. How would the way you speak and act tomorrow be different if you truly felt the shaykh's combination of rahma (mercy) and haya (awe) toward that person?
?
Imam Sanusi preserved concrete practices like dhikr and the handshake from his shaykh. What is one specific spiritual practice you have learned from a teacher but have not implemented consistently? What is the real reason—lack of discipline, doubt in its benefit, or attachment to convenience? If you died tonight, would that practice be missing from your account? What will you do before this day ends to revive it?

Names al-Tazi's students and quotes Ibn Maryam.

Sanusi's blessing was to study with al-Tazi alongside other great scholars.

It names three other notable students who shared this privilege, and it quotes a historical source to confirm al-Tazi's scholarly stature. وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي : صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل وانتسابه له ، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام ؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي ، والحافظ التنسي، والإمام أحمد زروق

And it was among the blessings of Imam Sanusi: his companionship with this noble gnostic and his affiliation with him. And he was shared in this by notables such as his maternal brother Shaykh Ali al-Taluti, and al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq. Commentary
This passage concludes the biographical sketch of Ibrahim al-Tazi's influence. It states that Imam Sanusi was blessed to have accompanied this noble gnostic and to be affiliated with him. It then lists other notable figures who also studied with al-Tazi: Sanusi's maternal brother Shaykh Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq. Finally, a quote from Ibn Maryam al-Maliti's 'al-Bustan' confirms that these figures took from al-Tazi, and includes a footnote referring to another source and noting al-Tazi's death year (866 AH) and that the Taziyya order is attributed to him.

The Sufi Khirqa Transmission to Sanusi
Describes Ibrahim al-Tazi giving the khirqa to Sanusi and the chain of transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Sanusi received the Sufi khirqa and the chain of transmission back to the famous gnostic Abu Madyan.

Core Idea
The khirqa links Sanusi to a spiritual lineage through Ibrahim al-Tazi and Abu Madyan.

This brief passage records a key moment in Imam Sanusi's spiritual formation: his receipt of the Sufi khirqa from Ibrahim al-Tazi. The khirqa is a symbol of spiritual blessing and authority, and the text also traces its chain back to the famous gnostic Abu Madyan. Understanding this transmission helps situate Sanusi within the Sufi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the basic facts.
Notice the concise style of the biographical note.
2
Identify the key actors
Note who gave the khirqa to whom and through which chain. Identify each person mentioned: Sanusi, Ibrahim al-Tazi, Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, Salih al-Zawawi, and Abu Madyan.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the transmission of the khirqa and the chain (silsila) are important in Sufi tradition. The chain authenticates spiritual authority and blessing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران؛ ألبسه الخرقة، وحدثه بها عن شيوخه، وبصق في فيه، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة. والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير.
Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Oran, clothed him with the khirqa, and narrated to him about his shaykhs, and spat into his mouth, and narrated many things from him. And the gnostic al-Tazi had worn the khirqa according to the way of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and he wore it from Shaykh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi by his chain to Abu Madyan, the famous gnostic and the great pole.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note about the transmission of the Sufi khirqa to Imam Sanusi. It first describes how Ibrahim al-Tazi, a resident of Oran, gave Sanusi the khirqa, narrated to him about his shaykhs, spat into his mouth (a traditional blessing), and narrated many things from him. The second sentence explains that al-Tazi himself had received the khirqa through a chain: from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, from Shaykh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi, back to the famous gnostic and great pole Abu Madyan. This shows the spiritual lineage of Sanusi.

Key Terms
خرقة (khirqa)
شيخ (shaykh)
سند (sanad/chain)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The spitting was an act of impurity or disrespect.
Correction: It was a traditional blessing practice transferring baraka (spiritual energy).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi received the Sufi khirqa from Ibrahim al-Tazi, whose own chain of transmission goes back to the great gnostic Abu Madyan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Consider your own spiritual lineage: who are the teachers that have passed on their faith to you? Have you actively sought their blessings or taken their teachings for granted? What will you do today to honor that lineage?
