Compassion for Animals and Children
Quotes the saint's teachings on kindness to animals and forbidding the beating of children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the saint's teachings on compassion for animals and children, and the theological basis for mercy toward all creation.

Core Idea
Mercy to all creation is the key to receiving God's hundred mercies.

This passage from the saint's biography highlights his deep compassion for even the smallest creatures and for children. Through three sayings, he connects human mercy to divine mercy, teaching that one cannot hope for God's mercy without being merciful to all creation. Let us explore these sayings and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the saint's own words settle before analyzing.
Notice the gentle tone of the saint's rebuke.
2
Identify the three teachings
Look for the three distinct sayings: about walking gently, reacting to animal cruelty, and forbidding beating children.
Each saying builds on the theme of mercy.
3
Understand the theological link
Focus on the last saying. Why does the saint mention God's hundred mercies? How does he connect human mercy to divine mercy?
This is the key doctrinal point.
4
Reflect on application
Consider how these teachings apply to your own life. How can you show mercy to animals and children today?
Compassion is a practical virtue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان يقول : ( ينبغي للإنسان أن يمشي برفق وينظر أمامه ؛ لئلا يقتل دابة في الأرض. وإذا رأى من يضرب دابة ضرباً عنيفاً .. تغيَّرَ ، وقال لضاربها : ارفق يا مبارك ! وكان ينهى مؤدِّبي الكُتاب عن ضرب الصبيان ، ويقول : ( الله تعالى مئة رحمة ، لا مطمع فيها إلا لمن اتسم برحمة جميع الخلق وأشفق عليهم )
And he used to say: 'It is incumbent upon a person to walk gently and look ahead, lest he kill an animal on the ground.' And if he saw someone striking an animal violently, he would change (expression) and say to the striker: 'Be gentle, O blessed one!' And he used to forbid the teachers of the writing school (kuttāb) from striking the boys, and he would say: 'God Most High has a hundred mercies; there is no hope for them except for one who is characterized by mercy for all creation and is compassionate towards them.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage records three sayings of the saint regarding compassion. First, he advised people to walk gently and look ahead to avoid accidentally stepping on and killing a small animal (dābbah). This shows a consideration for even the smallest creatures. Second, if he saw someone beating an animal violently, his expression would change and he would gently rebuke the striker, calling him 'blessed one' and asking him to be gentle. This reflects his immediate reaction to cruelty. Third, he forbade teachers (muʼaddibī al-kuttāb) from beating the boys (ṣibyān) who studied under them, and he gave a theological reason: God has a hundred mercies, and no one can hope for them except those who are characterized by mercy for all creation and are compassionate. This links human mercy to divine mercy, indicating that to receive God's mercy one must show mercy to all beings, including children and animals.

Key Terms
رفق
رحمة
دابة
صبيان
مؤدبي الكتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The saint forbids all forms of discipline for children.
Correction: The saint specifically forbids harsh beating by teachers, not all correction or discipline.

Checkpoint

A) It causes them to hate learning
B) God's hundred mercies are only for those merciful to all creation
C) The teacher might be punished
D) Children are too young to understand

Key Takeaway
The saint teaches that mercy to all creation, including animals and children, is the path to receiving God's abundant mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you walk, do you ever consider the small creatures under your feet? How would your daily life change if you truly saw each step as an act that could harm a creature? What is one small habit you can change today to walk with more care?
?
The saint's expression changed when he saw animal cruelty. When was the last time your heart was moved by suffering you witnessed? Do you think our numbness to suffering is a barrier to receiving God's mercy? Ask yourself: will I speak up the next time I see cruelty, or will I remain silent?
?
The saint forbade harsh beating of children and linked mercy to God's hundred mercies. Is there a child in your life—your own, a relative, or a student—toward whom you have been harsh? How can you replace that with gentleness this week? What one concrete step will you take to show more mercy to that child?

The Saint's Virtues: Forgiveness, Charity, Solitude, and Hidden Fear
Relates anecdotes of the saint's virtues with a concluding saying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the saint's exemplary character in forgiveness, charity, solitude, and hidden fear of God, and how these reflect the state of the true knowers.

Core Idea
The true knower laughs with people but weeps inwardly from fear of God.

This lesson presents four aspects of the saint's inner and outer life: his forgiveness of those who wronged him, his emphasis on charity particularly in hardship, his love of solitude for reflection, and his description of the hidden fear that characterizes the true knowers (al-ʻārifīn). Each anecdote offers a practical model for the seeker on the path.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the sequence of events and sayings.
Notice the shift from narrated actions to direct quotes.
2
Identify the four vignettes
The passage contains four distinct elements: the forgiveness story, the charity instruction, the solitude and reflection practice, and the saying about hidden fear. Mark each in the text.
Each vignette reveals a different virtue.
3
Reflect on the inner state
The final saying contrasts outward appearance with inner reality. Consider how this relates to the saint's own practice: he forgave openly but feared inwardly.
The phrase 'هذا شأن العارفين' ties the vignettes together.
4
Apply the lesson
Ask yourself: How can I embody these virtues in my own life? What does 'hidden fear' mean for my worship and interactions?

وزاره في مرض موته بعض العلماء وكان قد أساء إليه ، فطلب منه السماح ، فغفر له ودعا له بالخير ، ولما مات الإمام بكى عليه هذا العالم وتألم جدّاً وقال : فقدت الدنيا بفقده وكان يتصدَّق ويأمر أهله بالصدقة ، لا سيما أيام الشدة والجوع ويقول : ( من أحب الجنة فليكثر الصدقة خصوصاً في الغلاء ) وكان يؤثر الخلوات ، ويزور المواضع الخربة للاعتبار ، ويقول : أين سُكَّانُها ؟ وكيف يتنعمون ؟ وكان يقول : ( كم من ضاحك مع الناس وقلبه يبكي خوف ربه فهذا شأن العارفين )
And a scholar visited him during his terminal illness, and that scholar had wronged him before, so he asked him for forgiveness, and he forgave him and prayed for good for him. And when the Imām died, this scholar wept over him and was very pained and said: 'The world has been lost by his loss.' And he used to give charity and command his family to give charity, especially in times of hardship and hunger, and he said: 'Whoever loves Paradise, let him give charity frequently, particularly during high prices.' And he preferred seclusion, and visited ruined places for reflection, and said: 'Where are its inhabitants? And how do they enjoy themselves?' And he used to say: 'How many a laugher with people while his heart weeps from fear of his Lord—this is the state of the knowers (al-ʻārifīn).'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents several aspects of the saint's inner life. First, an anecdote of forgiveness: a scholar who had wronged him visited during his illness, sought forgiveness, and the saint forgave him and prayed for his good. After the saint's death, that same scholar wept deeply and declared that the world was lost by his loss, showing the impact of the saint's character. Second, the saint was generous in charity, especially during hard times, and urged his family to do the same. He linked charity to love of Paradise, emphasizing giving during inflation. Third, he loved seclusion and would visit ruined places to reflect, asking where the previous inhabitants were and how they now enjoy themselves—a reminder of the transience of worldly life. Finally, he described the state of the true knowers (ʻārifīn): outwardly laughing with people, but inwardly weeping from fear of God. This highlights the inner spiritual reality hidden behind a cheerful exterior.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the saint's outward laughter and social interaction contradict true piety, or that such behavior indicates hypocrisy.
Correction: The saint clarifies that the true knowers maintain a cheerful exterior with people while their hearts are in a state of fear of God. This is not hypocrisy but a concealment of their inner state to avoid ostentation and to fulfill social duties.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you give charity, do you give most when it is easy, or do you give more when times are hard? The saint commanded charity 'especially in times of hardship and hunger.' Examine your own giving: Does your charity reflect your love for Paradise?
?
Look at your own heart when you laugh with friends or family. Is there a hidden fear of God behind your smile, or is your laughter empty of reverence? The true knowers weep inside while laughing outside. How can you cultivate that inner fear without losing outward cheerfulness?

His Compassion Towards Animals and Children
Biographical anecdotes showing his mercy to animals and children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Islamic tradition, mercy towards animals and children is not merely social etiquette but a reflection of divine mercy and a means to attain God's compassion.

Core Idea
Mercy to creatures is the path to God’s one hundred mercies.

This lesson presents a biographical glimpse into the character of a great Islamic scholar. Through his actions and sayings, we see how he embodied compassion in everyday life—walking gently to avoid harming an animal, correcting harsh treatment of animals, and forbidding the beating of children. His teachings connect these acts of kindness directly to the hope of receiving God's vast mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text aloud or silently. Notice the key terms: الرفق, الرحمة, الصبيان, الدابة. These words set the theme of gentleness and mercy.
2
Understand each instruction
The passage contains three teachings: walking gently, correcting animal abuse, and forbidding beating boys. Identify each and reflect on the context of each.
The Imam's reaction to seeing an animal beaten is particularly vivid.
3
Grasp the theological link
The Imam connects mercy to creatures with God's one hundred mercies. This shows that such behavior is not just polite but a religious duty and a means of drawing closer to God.
This link is the core idea of the lesson.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to reinforce what you have learned. Then consider the common misunderstanding that this is mere etiquette.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان يقول : ( ينبغي للإنسان أن يمشي برفق وينظر أمامه ؛ لئلا يقتل دابة في الأرض. وإذا رأى من يضرب دابة ضرباً عنيفاً .. تغيَّرَ ، وقال لضاربها : ارفق يا مبارك ! وكان ينهى مؤدِّبي الكُتاب عن ضرب الصبيان ، ويقول : ( الله تعالى مئة رحمة ، لا مطمع فيها إلا لمن اتسم برحمة جميع الخلق وأشفق عليهم
He used to say: 'It is befitting for a person to walk gently and look ahead, lest he kill an animal on the ground.' And when he saw someone striking an animal violently, he would become upset and say to the striker: 'Be gentle, O blessed one!' And he would forbid the tutors of the school from beating boys, and he would say: 'God Almighty has one hundred mercies; there is no hope in them except for one who is characterized by mercy for all creatures and shows compassion to them.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents a biographical anecdote illustrating the Imam's profound compassion. It first describes his instruction to walk gently and watch the ground to avoid harming an animal, showing his concern for even unintentional harm. Then it narrates his reaction upon seeing someone beating an animal violently: he would change expression and tell the striker to be gentle, calling him 'blessed'. Finally, it mentions that he forbade teachers (mu'addibi al-kuttāb) from beating boys, and he connected this to divine mercy: God has one hundred mercies, and only those who are merciful to all creatures can hope for them. This indicates his view that mercy towards animals and children is a sign of true faith and a means to obtain God's mercy.

Correction: The Imam explicitly links mercy to creatures with God's mercy, showing it is a religious principle with eternal consequences.

Key Takeaway
Mercy towards all creatures is a key to attaining God's abundant mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you saw someone striking an animal violently, would you have the courage to gently rebuke them as the Imam did? What fear holds you back, and how can you overcome it for the sake of God’s mercy?

Forgiveness and Charity in Hardship
Biographical incidents showing his forgiveness of a wrongdoer and his emphasis on charity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Imam's forgiveness and commitment to charity exemplify Islamic virtues, and why charity during hardship is especially valued.

Core Idea
Forgiveness and charity in hardship are hallmarks of true piety.

This biographical passage presents two beautiful incidents from the life of the Imam: his gracious forgiveness of a scholar who wronged him, and his emphasis on charity, especially during times of scarcity. Through these, we see how the Imam lived the teachings of Islam at the highest level.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

The passage is short but packed with meaning.

Forgiveness is a sign of strength, not weakness.
3

The Imam commands charity, especially in hardship and high prices. Why is charity during difficulty so emphasized?
Linking charity to love of Paradise motivates action.
4

It transformed an enemy into a mourner.

He linked charity to love of Paradise, and emphasized giving when prices are high (i.e., when it is most difficult), indicating that the best charity is that given in hardship.

The Imam's Spiritual Solitude and Fear of God
Biographical description of his preference for solitude and inner fear of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Imam's practice of solitude and reflection reflects the inner state of the true knowers of Allah.

Core Idea
True piety combines outward joy with inward tears of fear.

This passage offers a glimpse into the spiritual practices of Imam Sanusi. It describes his preference for solitude in desolate places for reflection, and his teaching that the genuine state of the knowers (al-ʿārifīn) is one where the heart weeps from fear of God even while outwardly appearing joyful. This lesson explores the deeper significance of these practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the gist of the Imam's actions and sayings.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question he asks about the former inhabitants.
2
Understand the practice of iʿtibār
The Imam visited ruined places for 'reflection' (iʿtibār). Consider how this practice connects to the Quranic call to learn from past nations.
Iʿtibār means deriving lessons from observations.
3
Analyze the aphorism about laughter and weeping
The Imam contrasts outward laughter with inner weeping out of fear of Allah. This is the sign of the true knowers. Reflect on why this combination is praised.
This highlights that fear of God is compatible with social cheerfulness.
4
Consider common misunderstandings
Some might think his solitude was antisocial or that outward laughter indicates negligence. The passage corrects that; the knowers maintain inner reverence while engaging with people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary

He deliberately sought out ruined places to contemplate the transience of the world, asking rhetorically about the former inhabitants and their current state. This was a means of deriving lessons (iʿtibār). He also stated that many people outwardly laugh with others while inwardly their hearts weep from fear of God, and he identified this as the characteristic of the 'knowers' (al-ʿārifīn), those who have true gnosis. This highlights that true piety involves inner fear of God even when appearing joyful.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
You have passed by graveyards and ruins countless times. Did you ever stop to ask, 'Where are its inhabitants?' as the Imam did? How will you make i'tibar a real practice in your life starting this week?

His Asceticism and Detachment from the World
Biographical description of his ascetic state, sleep, fasting, and inner reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Imam's ascetic practices reflected his inner tawḥīd and his role as a guide for spiritual seekers.

Core Idea
His detachment from the world was the outward expression of deep inner tawḥīd.

This passage paints a vivid picture of the Imam's spiritual discipline, likening his worldly state to that of a prisoner. It details his minimal sleep, prolonged fasting, and the visible impact on his face. The description culminates in a profound summary of his inner and outer reality, showing that his asceticism was rooted in tawḥīd and aimed at guiding others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the imagery and rhythm of the description sink in before analyzing.
Notice the strong metaphor 'prisoner'—it sets the tone.
2
Identify the specific practices
Note the details: little sleep, long fasting, sleeping early and waking up, commitment to fast if he returns to sleep. These show his extreme discipline.
3
Connect inner and outer
Reflect on the saying: 'His inner is realities of tawḥīd, his outer is asceticism and stripping away.' How do his practices express inner tawḥīd? How does this guide seekers?
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكان حاله مع الدنيا حال المسجون ، فقل نومه وطال صومه ، ينام أول الليل ويحيي سائره ، مع التزام الصوم عاماً إن هو رجع إلى النوم متى استيقظ ، وهذا ما قد أثر في وجهه وصدق فيه ما قيل : ( باطنه حقائق التوحيد ، وظاهره زهد وتجريد ، وكلامه هداية لكل مريد
His state with the world was that of a prisoner. Little was his sleep and long was his fasting. He would sleep at the beginning of the night and keep awake the rest of it, with the commitment to fast throughout the year if he returned to sleep whenever he woke up. And this had affected his face. And what was said about him was true: 'His inner being is realities of tawḥīd, his outer is asceticism and stripping away, and his speech is guidance for every seeker.'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage describes the Imam's extreme asceticism. It likens his relationship with the world to that of a prisoner, indicating complete detachment. His sleep was minimal, his fasting long. He would sleep early in the night and then stay awake for the remainder, and if he returned to sleep after waking, he would commit to fasting for a whole year, showing his discipline. This austerity left visible marks on his face. The passage then quotes a saying that sums up his character: inwardly he embodied the realities of tawḥīd (divine unity), outwardly he practiced asceticism and stripping away of worldly attachments, and his words provided guidance for every spiritual seeker (murīd).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

His Intense Shyness and Reluctance to Refuse
Biographical anecdote about his extreme shyness and its consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Imam's extreme shyness as described in this anecdote and his willingness to accept its consequences.

Core Idea
Shyness so powerful it made him comply with requests he would rather refuse.

This passage gives us a vivid glimpse into the personal character of the Imam. Despite his high station, he struggled with an overwhelming sense of shyness that prevented him from refusing requests, even from sultans. His brother once confronted him about this, and his response reveals the depth of his trait.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full story.
Notice the emotional intensity.
2
Understand the conflict
Identify why the Imam's brother criticized him and how the Imam justified his actions.
3
Reflect on the Imam's response
Consider the Imam's willingness to accept the Fire if shyness leads there. What does this tell you about his character?
This shows his inability to overcome this trait.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو مع هذا كله شديد الحياء ، حتى إنه كان يكتب الشفاعات للسلاطين حياءً ممن يسأله ذلك ، فلامه على ذلك أخوه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي يوماً ، فقال له الإمام : والله يا أخي ؛ يمنعني منه غلبة الحياء ، ولا أقدر أن أقول : لا أكتب ، إذا كان الحياء يدخل صاحبه النار فأنا أدخلها
And despite all this, he was extremely shy, so much so that he would write intercessions for the sultans out of shyness from the one who asked him that. His maternal brother, Shaykh ʿAlī al-Tālūtī, once reproached him for that. The Imam said to him: 'By God, O my brother, what prevents me from it is the overwhelming shyness, and I am not able to say: I will not write. If shyness admits its possessor to the Fire, then I will enter it.'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage highlights the Imam's extreme shyness (al-ḥayāʾ). It gives an example: he would write letters of recommendation (shafāʿāt) for rulers out of shyness towards the person asking him, even though he may have preferred not to. His maternal brother criticized him for this, but the Imam explained that overwhelming shyness prevented him from refusing. He then made a striking statement: if shyness were to lead its possessor to Hellfire, then he would still enter it rather than refuse out of shyness. This shows that he considered shyness a dominant trait that he could not overcome, and he was willing to accept its consequences.

Key Terms
الحياء
الشفاعات
السلاطين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He would avoid it.
B) He said he would enter it.
C) He said it is not possible.
D) He said it is a sin.

Key Takeaway
The Imam's extreme shyness was so overpowering that he could not refuse requests, even if it meant potentially incurring divine punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Fasting Like Prophet David
Biographical description of his fasting routine and detachment from food.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific fasting practice of the Imam modeled on Prophet David, and how his detachment from food reflected his spiritual state.

Core Idea
The Imam's fasting practice was not just a routine but a sign of complete detachment from worldly concerns.

This passage gives us a glimpse into the personal devotional life of the Imam. He adopted the fast of Prophet David—fasting every other day—but his practice went beyond mere ritual. His minimal concern for food, sometimes going days without eating, and his enigmatic response when asked about his fast, all point to a soul absorbed in the spiritual rather than the material.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the fasting pattern
Note the specific rhythm: one day fast, one day break. This is the fast of Prophet David, considered the best voluntary fast.
2
Observe his detachment from food
He wouldn't seek food; ate only what was available; sometimes went three days without eating. Reflect on the spiritual discipline behind this.
3
Interpret his ambiguous answer
When asked if breaking fast, he said 'Neither fasting nor breaking fast.' Understand this as a reflection of his state: so detached that he didn't label himself.
He smiled to avoid drawing attention.

Source Text

كان رحمه الله يصوم يوماً بيوم صوم سيدنا داود على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام ، ويفطر على يسير الطعام ، ولا يبحث يوم فطره عما يأكل ، وربما بقي ثلاثة أيام أو أزيد لا يأكل ولا يشرب ، إن أُتِيَ بطعام أكل ، وإلا بقي كذلك وربما سألوه بعد مضي جلّ النهار : هل مفطر هو ؟ فيقول : لا مفطر ولا صائم ، فيقال له : لِمَ لا تعلمنا بفطرك ؟! فيبتسم .
He, may God have mercy on him, used to fast one day and break one day, the fast of our master David (peace be upon our Prophet and upon him), and he would break his fast with little food, and on the day of his breaking the fast he would not search for what to eat. Sometimes he would remain three days or more without eating or drinking. If food was brought to him, he would eat; otherwise he would remain as he was. Sometimes they would ask him after most of the day had passed: 'Are you breaking the fast?' He would say: 'Neither breaking the fast nor fasting.' It would be said to him: 'Why do you not inform us of your breaking the fast?' He would smile.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage details the Imam's specific fasting practice. He followed the fast of Prophet David, which is to fast every other day. His ifṭār (breaking of fast) was minimal; he would not seek out food but simply eat whatever was available. Sometimes he would go three days or more without eating or drinking altogether, showing extreme asceticism. He would not announce whether he was fasting or not; when asked late in the day, he would give an ambiguous answer: 'Neither breaking the fast nor fasting.' This likely indicates that he considered his state between fasting and not, perhaps because he was so detached from food. When asked why he did not inform them of his ifṭār, he would simply smile, showing his humility and reluctance to draw attention to his worship.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Imam's answer 'neither fasting nor breaking fast' shows he was uncertain about his own state.
Correction: It actually reflects his detachment; he was so unconcerned with worldly categories that he did not label himself.

Checkpoint
How did the Imam respond when asked if he was breaking his fast?
A) He said 'Yes'.
B) He said 'No'.
C) He said 'Neither breaking the fast nor fasting'.
D) He remained silent.

Key Takeaway
The Imam's fasting practice exemplified extreme detachment from worldly concerns, even to the point of not identifying as fasting or breaking fast.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How attached are you to knowing when and what you will eat? Could you go three days without any food or drink if none was brought to you, trusting that Allah will provide? What would that reveal about your level of reliance on Him?
?
When was the last time you were so absorbed in worship or remembrance of Allah that you lost all track of time and worldly concerns? Would your answer have been 'neither fasting nor not fasting' because your focus was on something higher?
?
Are you hiding your good deeds out of humility, or out of fear of others' opinions? The Imam smiled when asked about his fasting practice. Can you imagine yourself smiling when your worship is questioned, without irritation or pride? What would that require from you?

The Daily Routine of Imam al-Sanusi
Describes Imam al-Sanusi's daily routine and character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the holistic daily routine of Imam al-Sanusi, which integrates social etiquette, worship, teaching, and personal devotion as a model of pious living.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's day was a seamless blend of worship, teaching, and service.

This passage offers a window into the daily life of a great scholar and saint. Imam al-Sanusi's routine shows how he balanced social interaction, scholarly teaching, and intensive worship from dawn to dawn. As you read, consider how each part of his day reflects his spiritual priorities and how you might draw inspiration from his example.

Guided Path
1
Observe his social character
Notice how he interacted with companions: joking kindly, moderate voice, shaking hands, allowing hand-kissing, and dressing like common people. What does this teach about humility and approachability?
2
Trace his prayer and worship schedule
Follow the timeline from after fajr to before fajr the next day. Note his specific practices: delaying takbir, praying duha for ten hizbs, six rak'as after maghrib, seclusion, litanies, and night prayer.
The passage gives precise times and durations.
3
Reflect on his teaching and service
He taught after fajr until breakfast and also greeted people at his door. This shows his commitment to spreading knowledge and being accessible to the community.
4
Appreciate the eulogy
The passage ends with praise of his lofty spiritual states. Consider why his routine is presented as a model for seekers of guidance.
The author uses this as inspiration for the reader.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما مازح بعض أصحابه ، فلا تجد أحسن منه حينئذ ، ولا يرفع صوته ، بل يعتدل فيه ، ويصافح الناس ولا يمنع من قبل يده ، ولا يلبس لباساً مخصوصاً يعرف به ، بل ثوبه ما اعتاده الناس كان يكره الكلام بعد الصبح والعصر ، ويتراخي في صلاته بتكبيرة الإحرام بعد الإقامة ، ولا يكبر إلا بعد حين ، وكان بعد صلاة الصبح في مسجده يقرأ أوراده ، ثم يباشر بإقراء العلم إلى وقت الفطور المعتاد ، ثم يقف ساعة مع الناس على باب داره ، ثم يدخل ويصلي الضحى قدر قراءة عشرة أحزاب ، ثم يشتغل بالمطالعة نهاراً . وكان بعد الزوال يخرج لخلواته إلى الغروب ، وأحياناً يصلي الظهر مع الناس ثم يجلس يصلي ويتنفل ويقرأ إلى العصر ، ثم يشتغل بورده إلى الغروب ، فإذا صلى المغرب صلى ست ركعات ، وبقي في مسجده حتى يصلي العشاء ، ويقرأ ما تيسر • ثم يرجع إلى داره وينام ساعة ، ثم يشتغل بالنظر أو النسخ ساعة ، ثم يصلي إلى طلوع الفجر (1) فيا لها من أحوال شريفة ، نال صاحبها المقامات المنيفة ! فأكرم به من عالم عامل ، ومنارة هدي تتلمحها أعين القُصَّاد ، وسالكي سبل الرشاد ! (۱) انظر ( البستان » ( ص ٢٤٤ ) ، و ( نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٥٧٠ ).
And perhaps he would joke with some of his companions, and you would not find anyone better than him at that time. He would not raise his voice but would be moderate in it. He would shake hands with people and would not prevent anyone from kissing his hand. He would not wear a specific garment by which he would be known, but his clothing was what people were accustomed to. He disliked talking after dawn and afternoon prayers. He would delay in his prayer by the takbir of ihram after the iqama, and would not say the takbir except after a while. After the dawn prayer, he would remain in his mosque reading his litanies, then he would directly begin teaching knowledge until the usual breakfast time. Then he would stand for an hour with the people at the door of his house, then enter and pray the forenoon prayer (al-duha) equal to the recitation of ten hizbs, then occupy himself with reading during the day. After noon, he would go out to his seclusions until sunset, and sometimes he would pray the noon prayer with the people, then sit praying, performing voluntary prayers, and reciting until the afternoon prayer. Then he would occupy himself with his litany until sunset. When he prayed the sunset prayer, he would pray six rak'as, and remain in his mosque until he prayed the evening prayer, and he would recite whatever was easy. Then he would return to his house and sleep for an hour, then occupy himself with study or copying for an hour, then pray until dawn. (1) What noble states they are! Their possessor has attained lofty stations! How excellent he is, a knowledgeable and practicing scholar, a beacon of guidance glimpsed by the eyes of seekers and those on the paths of right guidance! (1) See 'al-Bustan' p. 244 and 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' p. 570.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage describes the daily routine of Imam al-Sanusi. It begins with his social behavior: he joked with companions, was pleasant, moderate in voice, shook hands, allowed kissing of hand (a sign of respect), and dressed modestly like ordinary people. Then it details his prayer habits: he disliked talking after fajr and asr, delayed the takbir of ihram after iqama, and had a fixed schedule after fajr: reading litanies, teaching until breakfast, greeting people at the door, praying duha (which he measured by reciting ten hizbs), then studying during the day. After noon, he would go into seclusion until sunset, sometimes praying zuhr with people and doing extra prayers until asr. After asr he would do his litany until sunset. After maghrib he would pray six rak'as, remain in mosque until isha, recite, then go home, sleep an hour, study or copy for an hour, then pray until fajr. The passage ends with a eulogy: what noble states he achieved! He is a knowledgeable and practicing scholar, a beacon of guidance.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's daily routine exemplifies a balanced life of worship, teaching, and social engagement, showing that spiritual excellence permeates every moment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at your own daily schedule. Where is the space for consistent worship, learning, and service? Imam al-Sanusi's day was filled with these. What specific activity are you going to add or adjust this week to bring more balance?
?
Imam al-Sanusi avoided distinctive clothing and did not seek recognition. Are there any outward displays of piety you rely on for validation? How can you detach from that and focus purely on Allah's pleasure?
?
He combined social affability (joking, handshakes) with deep devotion. Which aspect do you lean too much toward—neglecting people for worship, or neglecting worship for people? What one change will you make tomorrow to restore balance?

The Karama of His Father's Vision
Relates a karama where al-Sanusi's father credits his son's reflection for his own forgiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of a karama involving Imam al-Sanusi's reflection on creation and how it relates to his scholarly rank and the science of kalam.

Core Idea
A saint's reflection on God's creation can be a means of divine forgiveness.

This passage introduces a delightful miracle that shows the deep connection between Imam al-Sanusi's theological reflection and his spiritual state. The story demonstrates how even a moment of pondering God's creation can have profound effects, as seen in the forgiveness granted to his father. The author frames this karama as an additional honor that complements Sanusi's high scholarly station.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's preface about karamat before the story.
2
Understand the author's introductory remarks
The author states that Sanusi's status is not magnified by miracles, but recounting them is a form of veneration. Identify the key phrase: 'من باب زيادة العناية والتعظيم'.
3
Follow the dream narrative
A saint sees Sanusi's father in a dream and learns he was forgiven due to Sanusi's reflection on a mountain. Trace the dialogue and Sanusi's confirmation.
Notice the phrase 'بتفكر ولدي' which directly links the reflection to forgiveness.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how deep thought on creation (tafakkur) is tied to kalam and brings one closer to God. The karama is 'mixed with kalam' (ممزوجة بعلم الكلام).
This shows that theological reflection is not just intellectual but spiritually transformative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طرف من كراماته مثل الإمام السنوسي لا يعظم شأنه بحكاية كرامة له ؛ إذ حسبنا ما أكرمه الله به حين بوأه هذه المنزلة العلمية الرفيعة ، وأقامه عَلَمَ هدى لإرشاد الخلق ، واستنقذ بما أجراه الله على يراعه كثيراً من التائهين المتحيّرين ، ولكن حكاية ذلك من باب زيادة العناية والتعظيم ومن اللطيف أن ترى له بعض الكرامات ممزوجةً بعلم الكلام ! وهذا دال على صدق حال الإمام مع هذا العلم المقرب من الله تعالى ؛ فقد حكى العلامة الشفشاوني عن بعض الأولياء أنه رأى والد الشيخ السنوسي بعد موته في المنام ، فقال له : ما فعل الله بك ؟ فقال : غفر لي ، فقال : بم ؟ قال : بتفكر ولدي في الجبل ساعة دفني ! فلمَّا سُئل الإمام السنوسي عن ذلك قال : نعم ؛ كنت أتفكّر الجبل الذي كان أمامي ؛ وهو المطل على تلمسان ، وكم فيه من جواهر ، وكيف ركبه الحكيم بقدرته وحكمته
A Sampling of His Miracles (Karamat). Like Imam al-Sanusi, his status is not magnified by recounting a miracle for him; for sufficient for us is what God honored him with when He established him in this high scholarly station, and set him up as a beacon of guidance for directing creation, and through what God caused to flow from his pen, He rescued many of those who were wandering lost. But recounting that is by way of increasing care and veneration. And it is delightful that you see for him some miracles mixed with the science of kalam! This indicates the sincerity of the Imam's state with this science that brings one near to God Almighty. For the scholar al-Shafshawani narrated from one of the saints that he saw the father of Shaykh al-Sanusi after his death in a dream, and he said to him: 'What did God do with you?' He said: 'He forgave me.' He said: 'By what?' He said: 'By the reflection of my son concerning the mountain for an hour at my burial.' When Imam al-Sanusi was asked about that, he said: 'Yes, I was reflecting on the mountain that was in front of me, which overlooks Tlemcen, and how many gems are in it, and how the Wise One composed it by His power and wisdom.'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a combination of an introductory comment on the nature of miracles (karamat) and a specific story. The author begins by stating that a scholar like Sanusi does not need miracles to magnify him; his honor comes from God giving him high scholarly rank and using him to guide others. Yet recounting miracles is permissible as additional respect. The specific miracle is delightful because it is mixed with kalam (theology). A saint saw Sanusi's father in a dream and learned that he was forgiven because of Sanusi's reflection on a mountain for an hour at the time of his burial. When asked, Sanusi confirmed that he was reflecting on the mountain overlooking Tlemcen, pondering its gems and how God composed it with power and wisdom. This shows that deep reflection on creation can be a means of forgiveness.

Key Terms

القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a saint's miracle (karama) is the primary proof of his spiritual rank, or that another person's reflection can directly earn forgiveness for someone else without divine will.
Correction: The passage clarifies that al-Sanusi's rank is not based on miracles but on his scholarly station and guidance. The forgiveness granted to his father is a specific divine favor, not a mechanical cause-and-effect from the son's reflection. It is a karama that highlights the spiritual benefit of tafakkur.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in God as the wise and powerful Creator, but when was the last time you actually stopped to reflect on a mountain, a leaf, or your own fingers? Your neglect of tafakkur suggests your faith is lazy. Will you today discard your distraction and spend an hour in genuine contemplation of God's handiwork?
?
This karama shows that even a saint's reflection can be a means of forgiveness for a deceased parent. How often do you ponder the universe with the intention of drawing closer to God? If your reflections are rare or superficial, what does that say about the depth of your connection to your Creator? Commit now to a specific time for tafakkur this week.
?
Imam al-Sanusi's reflection was so sincere that it became a source of mercy for his father. Do you consider that your own spiritual practices—your salah, dhikr, or study—could have an impact on those you love beyond the grave? Or are you only concerned with your own salvation? Repent of your selfishness and begin to see your acts of worship as acts of intercession.

The Miracle of the Uncooked Meat
A story where meat remained raw after prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this story illustrates a miracle of Sanusi and the lesson of prioritizing prayer over worldly concerns.

Core Idea
Devotion in prayer can bring divine intervention in daily life.

This short story recounts a remarkable miracle associated with Imam Sanusi. It shows how a man's decision to prioritize prayer over his meat purchase led to a supernatural preservation of his food. The narrative underscores the blessings of putting worship first.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage

The story is concise but rich in implication.

Understand the sequence of events

The meat did not cook despite prolonged cooking.
3
Reflect on the lesson

Divine intervention preserved the meat.
4
Complete the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to test your understanding of the event.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كراماته : أنَّ رجلاً اشترى لحماً من السوق ، فسمع الإقامة في المسجد ، فدخل واللحم معه يحمله ، فخاف من طرحه فوات ركعة ، وكبر على هذه الحال ، فلما سلَّم وعاد إلى أهله طبخ أهله اللحم إلى صلاة العشاء فلم ينضج ، فأرادوا طرحه فإذا هو على حاله بدمه ،
Among his miracles: that a man bought meat from the market, and he heard the iqama in the mosque, so he entered carrying the meat with him, and he feared that discarding it would cause him to miss a rak'a, so he said the takbir in this state. When he said the salutation (taslim) and returned to his family, his family cooked the meat until the evening prayer, but it did not cook. They wanted to throw it away, and behold, it was in its state with its blood.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage recounts another miracle of Sanusi. A man bought meat and heard the iqama for prayer. He entered the mosque carrying the meat, not wanting to miss a rak'a by putting it down. He prayed in that state. After prayer, he returned home, and his family cooked the meat until isha, but it did not cook. They were about to discard it, but it remained raw and bloody. The story implies that the meat's uncooked state was a miracle, perhaps a sign of the man's devotion or a lesson about prioritizing prayer.

Why Mention Miracles? The Purpose of Karamat
Sanusi introduces the section on his karamat and justifies their mention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author mentions Imam Sanusi's miracles despite his already high rank, and how they serve to confirm his sincerity in the science of kalam.

Core Idea
Miracles confirm sincerity, not elevate rank.

This passage introduces the section on Imam Sanusi's extraordinary acts, known as karamat. The author makes a careful theological point: these miracles are not meant to embellish his status but to highlight his sincerity and devotion to Islamic theology, especially the science of kalam. Understanding this helps us appreciate the proper role of miracles in Islamic spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words and rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's apologetic tone—he is defending the mention of miracles.
2
Identify the author's main argument
The author states that recounting a miracle does not magnify the Imam's rank because Allah already honored him with high rank and guidance. Find this statement and reflect on why the author feels the need to say it.
Think: Why might some think miracles are needed to magnify a saint's status?
3
Reflect on the connection between karamat and kalam
The author notes that some of the Imam's miracles are mixed with the science of kalam. Consider how this indicates sincerity and closeness to Allah. This step connects the lesson to the broader theme of the course.
The term 'kalam' here refers to theological reasoning, not just speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طرف من كراماته مثل الإمام السنوسي لا يعظم شأنه بحكاية كرامة له؛ إذ حسبنا ما أكرمه الله به حين بوأه هذه المنزلة العلمية الرفيعة، وأقامه عَلَمَ هدى لإرشاد الخلق، واستنقذ بما أجراه الله على يراعه كثيراً من التائهين المتحيّرين، ولكن حكاية ذلك من باب زيادة العناية والتعظيم. ومن اللطيف أن ترى له بعض الكرامات ممزوجةً بعلم الكلام! الله وهذا دال على صدق حال الإمام مع هذا العلم المقرب من تعالى.
A portion of his miracles: such as Imam Sanusi, his station is not magnified by recounting a miracle for him; for sufficient is what Allah honored him with when He granted him this high scholarly rank, and made him a banner of guidance for directing creation, and saved through what Allah caused to flow from his pen many of the lost and bewildered. But recounting that is from the door of increasing care and veneration. And it is subtle that you see some of his miracles mixed with the science of kalam! By Allah, this indicates the truthfulness of the Imam's state with this science that draws near to the Most High.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage serves as an introduction to the section on the karamat (miracles) of Imam Sanusi. The author begins by stating that Imam Sanusi's rank is not enhanced by narrating a miracle for him, because Allah has already honored him sufficiently by granting him a high scholarly position and making him a guide. However, recounting these miracles is a way of increasing care and veneration for him. Then the author notes the subtlety that some of his miracles are mixed with the science of kalam (theology). Finally, he emphasizes that this indicates the sincerity of the Imam with this science that draws one near to Allah.

Key Terms
كرامة
علم الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karamat are meant to prove that a saint is superior to others or to magnify his rank beyond what his knowledge provides.
Correction: The author clarifies that karamat do not elevate rank; rather, they are recounted to increase care and veneration. The Imam's high rank comes from Allah's gift of knowledge and guidance.

Checkpoint
Why does the author mention the karamat of Imam Sanusi?
A) To prove that he is a prophet
B) To increase care and veneration for him
C) To show that he is better than other scholars
D) To entertain the reader

Key Takeaway
Karamat are not to elevate a saint's rank but to confirm his sincerity and to increase veneration, especially when they are linked to sacred knowledge like kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn about scholars and saints, do you find yourself more impressed by their miracles or by the knowledge and guidance they conveyed? Which do you think truly testifies to their sincerity before Allah?
?
If your own devotion to sacred knowledge were to be 'mixed' with something miraculous, what would that miracle be? Is there any area of your life where you need to seek sincerity (ṣidq) more than spectacular signs?
?
The author says sufficient honor is the scholarly rank Allah granted. Are you content with the 'ordinary' blessings of knowledge and guidance in your life, or do you secretly wish for a sign to confirm your worth? What does that longing reveal about your trust in Allah's wisdom?

Dream of Forgiveness Through Contemplation
Sanusi recounts a dream vision showing his father's forgiveness due to his contemplation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream vision illustrates the spiritual power of contemplation (tafakkur) and its benefit for the deceased.

Core Idea
A son's contemplation can bring forgiveness to his father.

This passage recounts a remarkable dream vision involving Imam Sanusi's father. It shows the profound effect of contemplative reflection (tafakkur) on creation. Through this story, we see how the spiritual state of a righteous child can benefit his parents even after death.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the chain of narration: a saint sees the father in a dream, then Sanusi confirms.

Look for the word 'تفكر' (contemplation).

Sanusi mentions jewels and the Wise Creator's power and wisdom.

Contemplation of Allah's creation is a spiritually powerful act.

He said: 'He forgave me.' He said: 'By what?' He said: 'By my son's contemplation of the mountain for an hour at my burial!' When Imam al-Sanusi was asked about that, he said: 'Yes; I was contemplating the mountain that was in front of me, which overlooks Tlemcen, and how many jewels are in it, and how the Wise One composed it with His power and wisdom.'

Commentary
This passage is a narrative of a karamah related to Imam Sanusi. A saint sees Sanusi's deceased father in a dream and asks about his fate. The father reveals he was forgiven because of his son's contemplation of a mountain for one hour at the time of his burial. When Imam Sanusi is questioned, he confirms the event, explaining that he was indeed contemplating the mountain overlooking Tlemcen, reflecting on its composition and the divine wisdom and power behind it. This highlights the spiritual benefit of tafakkur (contemplation) and the intercession of righteous children.

The Miracle of the Uncooked Meat
Sanusi relates a miracle where meat carried through prayer would not cook.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the miracle of the uncooked meat as a sign of the barakah of praying behind a righteous imam.

Core Idea
Barakah from righteous prayer can even protect meat from fire.

This lesson presents a remarkable story from the life of Imam Sanusi. A man enters the mosque during prayer carrying raw meat, and after praying behind the Imam, the meat miraculously refuses to cook. Through this event, Sanusi teaches a profound lesson about the spiritual protection granted to those who follow true guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the story
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the sequence of events: buying meat, entering mosque, praying, cooking failure.
The story is simple but carries deep meaning.
2
Understand the miracle
The meat does not cook despite prolonged heating. Reflect on why this is considered a miracle (karama) of the Imam.
3
Examine the Imam's explanation
Sanusi links the miracle to the barakah of his prayer, hoping that those who pray behind him will be protected from Hellfire.
The meat's condition is a physical sign of spiritual protection.
4
Consider the request for secrecy
Sanusi asks the man to keep the event secret. This reflects the humility of saints who avoid fame.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كراماته: أنَّ رجلاً اشترى لحماً من السوق، فسمع الإقامة في المسجد، فدخل واللحم معه يحمله، فخاف من طرحه فوات ركعة، وكبر على هذه الحال، فلما سلَّم وعاد إلى أهله طبخ أهله اللحم إلى صلاة العشاء فلم ينضج، فأرادوا طرحه فإذا هو على حاله بدمه، فقالوا: لعله لحم شارف، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح، فلم يتغيَّر حاله! عن فذكر الرجل، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك، فقال له: يا بني؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي، ولكن اكتم ذلك.
And among his miracles: a man bought meat from the market, and heard the iqama in the mosque, so he entered while carrying the meat. He feared that putting it down would cause him to miss a rak'ah, so he said the takbir in that state. When he finished the prayer and returned to his family, his family cooked the meat until the evening prayer but it did not cook. They wanted to throw it away, but it was still raw with its blood. They said: Perhaps it is old meat. So they kept kindling fire under it until morning, but its condition did not change. Then the man remembered, so he went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son, I hope from Allah that whoever prays behind me, the Fire will not harm him. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep this secret.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage narrates a miracle associated with Imam Sanusi's prayer. A man enters the mosque during iqama carrying raw meat, prays without putting it down, and after prayer the meat refuses to cook even after prolonged cooking. The Imam explains that his prayer has such barakah that whoever prays behind him will be protected from Hellfire, and the meat's state may be due to being present during that prayer. The Imam asks the man to keep the event secret, a common practice among saints to avoid fame.

كرامة
بركة
صلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the miracle is about the meat itself having special properties.
Correction: The miracle is a sign of the barakah of praying behind a righteous imam; the meat's resistance to fire symbolizes protection from Hellfire.

Checkpoint

A) They will become wealthy
B) The Fire will not harm them
C) Their meat will always cook
D) They will never sin

Key Takeaway
The miracle of the uncooked meat demonstrates the spiritual barakah of praying behind a righteous imam and the importance of humility in concealing one's virtues.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in a hurry, do you still prioritize your prayer over worldly tasks, or do you carry your 'meat' into the prayer? What would it take for you to trust that Allah's barakah is more important than punctuality?
?
If you witnessed a clear sign of Allah's favor in your life, would you be able to keep it secret as Sanusi instructed, or would you feel compelled to share it for recognition? What does your answer reveal about your intentions?
?
The family tried everything to cook the meat but failed. When your own efforts repeatedly fail, do you ever pause to consider that a spiritual cause—such as a hidden blessing or trial—might be at work? How often do you seek the spiritual explanation before the natural one?

The Miracle of the Lost Key and Tawassul
Sanusi encourages tawassul and a woman's key is recovered through his intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practice of tawassul through a historical account of Imam Sanusi and a miraculous event.

Core Idea
Tawassul through awliya is effective, as shown by Sanusi's intercession opening a locked door.

This lesson presents a story from the life of Imam Sanusi that illustrates the concept of tawassul—seeking intercession through a righteous person. The story shows how a woman, unable to open her door after losing the key, turned to Sanusi and his status with Allah, and the door miraculously opened. This account reinforces the belief that tawassul is a permissible and powerful practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the key terms: tawassul and jah.
2
Identify the saying
Find Sanusi's direct statement: 'Whoever has a need to Allah, let him seek intercession through us...'
3
Understand the miracle
Focus on the sequence: woman loses key, tries everything, fails, then uses tawassul, and the door opens.
This demonstrates the efficacy of tawassul.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this story supports the doctrine of tawassul and intercession of awliya. Note the common misconception that tawassul is shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك: أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه: (من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا)، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه، ففُتح الباب وانحلَّ القفل.
And among that: he used to say, trusting in his Lord: 'Whoever has a need to Allah, let him seek intercession through us and let him put us forward.' And it is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house and tried every trick to open it but failed, so she sought intercession through the Shaykh and his status with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock was loosened.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a saying of Imam Sanusi on tawassul (seeking intercession) followed by a miraculous event confirming its efficacy. The Imam encourages people to use him as a means (wasila) to Allah for their needs. A woman, unable to open her door after losing the key, seeks intercession through the Imam and his status (jah) with Allah, and the door opens miraculously. This underscores the belief that awliya can intercede and that tawassul is a legitimate practice.

Key Terms
توسل
جاه
ولاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawassul is shirk (associating partners with Allah).
Correction: The author presents tawassul as a permissible and effective practice endorsed by the saint, relying on Allah's power.

Checkpoint

A) She found the key
B) The lock opened by itself

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

If so, why do you not actively seek their intercession in your daily supplications? Commit to one specific way you will incorporate tawassul into your prayers this week.

Protecting Scholarship from the Evil Eye
A biographical account of Sanusi's hidden commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Sanusi's precocious commentary was hidden to protect it from the evil eye, illustrating the tradition's belief in spiritual protection.

Core Idea
Even great works need protection from envy.

This short passage from Sanusi's biography reveals a remarkable act of spiritual prudence. At just nineteen, Sanusi authored a major commentary that amazed a saintly figure, who then ordered it hidden until the author turned forty. This story highlights the Islamic tradition's serious regard for the evil eye and the measures taken to safeguard blessings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the key details: the age of authorship, the saint's reaction, and the command to hide the work.
The ellipsis in the Arabic indicates a pause in the narrative.
2
Identify the key figures and actions
Identify Imam Sanusi (author), Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan (the saint), and the actions: writing, seeing, ordering to hide, and praying.
3
Understand the rationale
Reflect on why the saint ordered the commentary hidden. The reason is explicit: 'lest it be struck by the evil eye.' This connects to the belief that envy can harm people and objects.
The evil eye (al-ayn) is a recognized concept in Islamic theology.
4
Consider the lesson for today
Think about how this story teaches humility and the importance of seeking protection from envy, even for one's good works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك: تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ (الحوفية)، الذي سماه: ألَّفه المقرب المستوفي وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان . . تعجب منه، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مؤلّفه أربعين سنة؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين، ويقول له: لا نظير له فيما أعلم، ودعا لمؤلفه.
And among that: his authorship of the great commentary on al-Hawfiyya, which he named 'Al-Muqarrat al-Mustawfi'; he wrote it when he was nineteen years old. When Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan saw it, he was amazed by it and ordered that it be hidden until its author completes forty years, lest it be struck by the evil eye, and said to him: 'There is nothing like it to my knowledge,' and he made du'a for its author.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage relates a miracle of precocious scholarship and divine protection. Imam Sanusi wrote a major commentary at the age of nineteen. A prominent saint, al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan, saw it, admired it greatly, but ordered it to be hidden until Sanusi reached forty years of age to protect it and him from the evil eye (al-ayn). The saint praised it as unparalleled and made supplication for its author. This highlights the belief in the evil eye and the need for spiritual protection.

Key Terms
شرح
عين
قطب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The commentary was hidden because it contained errors or was not good enough.
Correction: The text clearly states it was hidden to protect it from the evil eye due to its excellence, not because of flaws.

Checkpoint

B) To protect it from being stolen
C) To protect it and its author from the evil eye
D) Because the author was too young

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's commentary was hidden on saintly advice to shield it from the evil eye, reflecting the Islamic emphasis on spiritual protection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The saint ordered the commentary hidden because he feared the evil eye. In your life, what good thing (knowledge, deed, talent) are you sharing too openly that might be vulnerable to envy? How will you change that today?
?

?
Sanusi patiently accepted the saint's order to hide his work until age 40. Is there a good deed or project in your life that you need to conceal for a time to seek Allah's protection? What is holding you back from that patience?

The Imam's Distress and Hidden Knowledge
Sanusi appears distressed and reveals that Allah informed him of something secret.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
The Imam's distress was a sign of divine disclosure, not worldly worry.

This brief anecdote offers a glimpse into the spiritual state of Imam Sanusi. When questioned about his visible distress, he only revealed its cause on condition of secrecy. The passage highlights the profound nature of spiritual unveilings (mukashafat) and the trust placed in the Imam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

Notice the words 'انقباض' (dejection) and 'متغير اللون' (changed color).

This suggests the knowledge was of a sensitive or sacred nature.
3
Connect to the broader theme of hidden knowledge
Consider how this incident relates to the concept of 'ilm al-batin' (hidden knowledge) in Islamic tradition.
Sanusi is known for his deep spiritual insights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك: أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون، فسُئل عن ذلك، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر، فقال: أطلعني الله تعالى
And among that: one day he was seen very dejected, his color changed. He was asked about that, and after insistence and on condition of keeping the matter secret, he said: 'Allah the Most High informed me'

The story is incomplete in this excerpt, but it shows the Imam had access to spiritual unveilings (mukashafat) and was entrusted with secret knowledge. The insistence on secrecy indicates the gravity of the matter.

The Meat That Wouldn't Burn: A Karama of Protection
A story of a meat that would not burn despite prolonged fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Sanusi's prayer protected his followers from fire, and how this story illustrates the concept of karamat.

Core Idea
The Imam's prayer shields his followers from fire.

This first story from the life of Imam Sanusi shows a miraculous incident involving meat that would not burn. It reveals the spiritual power of the Imam and his intercession. Let's read the account.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of the meat
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the narrative.
Notice the detail that the meat was from a worn-out camel.
2
Understand the Imam's statement
The Imam expresses hope that those who pray behind him are protected from fire. Reflect on the connection between prayer and protection.
3
Reflect on the concept of karamat
This is a manifest karama. Why is it done secretly? Consider the principle of hiding karamat.
The Imam says 'but keep that secret'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقالوا : لعله لحم شارف ، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح ، فلم يتغيَّر حاله ! عن فَتذكر الرجل ، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك ، فقال له : يا بني ؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار ، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي ، ولكن اكتم ذلك
ومن ذلك : أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه : من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا ، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح ، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه ، ففُتح الباب وانحلَّ القفل
ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ الحوفية ، الذي سماه : ألفه المقرب المستوفي وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة ، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان تعجب منه ، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مؤلّفه أربعين سنة ؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين ، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم ، ودعا لمؤلفه
ومن ذلك : أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون ، فسُئل عن ذلك ، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر ، فقال : أطلعني الله تعالى على رؤية جهنم وما فيها ، نعوذ بالله منها ، فمن حينئذ صرت أتغير وأحزن إلى الآن ، فهذا سبب تغيري
They said: Perhaps it is meat of a worn-out camel, so they spent the night kindling fire on it until morning, but its condition did not change. Then the man remembered, and went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son; I hope from Allah the Exalted that everyone who prays behind me will not be overtaken by fire. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. And among that: He used to say, trusting in his Master: 'Whoever has a need to Allah should seek intercession through us and put us forward.' So it is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but did not succeed. She sought intercession through the Sheikh and his status with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock was unlocked. And among that: His authorship of the great commentary on al-Hawfi, which he named: 'The Nearness-seeker, the Enough' while he was nineteen years old. When the great pole al-Hasan Abarkan came across it, he was amazed, and ordered that it be hidden until its author completes forty years; so that he not be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no equal to it as far as I know, and he prayed for its author. And among that: He was seen one day very depressed, with changed color. He was asked about that, and after insistence and a condition of secrecy, he replied: Allah the Exalted showed me the vision of Hell and what is in it, we seek refuge in Allah from it. From then on I have been changing and grieving until now, and this is the reason for my change.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a collection of anecdotes illustrating the karamat (miracles of saints) of Imam Sanusi. The first story tells of a man who had meat that would not cook, and the Imam assures him that whoever prays behind him will be protected from fire, implying the meat was blessed. The second story involves a woman who lost her key and used tawassul (intercession) through the Imam, resulting in the door opening. The third story describes how the Imam wrote a major commentary at a young age, and a saintly figure ordered it hidden until he was forty to protect him from the evil eye. The fourth story has the Imam seeing a vision of Hell, causing him lasting sorrow. These stories highlight the Imam's spiritual station and the reality of karamat.

Key Terms
كرامة
صلاة
بركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karamat are performed by the saints themselves independently of Allah.
Correction: Karamat are granted by Allah as a sign of His approval of the saint's obedience, not as independent power.

Checkpoint
What did Imam Sanusi say about those who pray behind him?
A) They will never get sick
B) They will not be overtaken by fire
C) They will become wealthy
D) They will see angels

Key Takeaway
The Imam's spiritual connection through prayer can result in tangible protection from fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the prayer of a righteous person can protect you from harm? How does this story challenge your reliance on material means alone?
?
The Imam kept the miracle secret. Is there a spiritual experience or blessing in your life that you have shared too openly, perhaps seeking recognition rather than protecting its sanctity?
?
The man's meat was preserved because he had prayed behind the Imam. What does this teach you about the importance of seeking out and connecting with righteous teachers? Are you actively seeking such connections?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
The Lost Key: Tawassul Through the Imam
A story of a woman opening a locked door through tawassul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practice of tawassul (seeking intercession) through saints as illustrated by this story.

Core Idea
Seeking intercession through the awliya opens doors.

The second story demonstrates the power of tawassul — asking a saint to intercede with Allah. A woman unable to open her lock turns to Imam Sanusi, and the problem is solved miraculously.

Guided Path
1
Read the story
Read the Arabic passage and translation.
Note the Imam's general statement before the anecdote.
2
Understand the Imam's teaching on tawassul
The Imam invites people to use him as a means to Allah. Reflect on the legitimacy of tawassul.
3
Note the result
The door opens immediately after tawassul. This shows the effectiveness of seeking intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقالوا : لعله لحم شارف ، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح ، فلم يتغيَّر حاله ! عن فَتذكر الرجل ، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك ، فقال له : يا بني ؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار ، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي ، ولكن اكتم ذلك
ومن ذلك : أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه : من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا ، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح ، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه ، ففُتح الباب وانحلَّ القفل
ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ الحوفية ، الذي سماه : ألفه المقرب المستوفي وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة ، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان تعجب منه ، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مؤلّفه أربعين سنة ؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين ، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم ، ودعا لمؤلفه
ومن ذلك : أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون ، فسُئل عن ذلك ، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر ، فقال : أطلعني الله تعالى على رؤية جهنم وما فيها ، نعوذ بالله منها ، فمن حينئذ صرت أتغير وأحزن إلى الآن ، فهذا سبب تغيري
They said: Perhaps it is meat of a worn-out camel, so they spent the night kindling fire on it until morning, but its condition did not change. Then the man remembered, and went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son; I hope from Allah the Exalted that everyone who prays behind me will not be overtaken by fire. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. And among that: He used to say, trusting in his Master: 'Whoever has a need to Allah should seek intercession through us and put us forward.' So it is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but did not succeed. She sought intercession through the Sheikh and his status with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock was unlocked. And among that: His authorship of the great commentary on al-Hawfi, which he named: 'The Nearness-seeker, the Enough' while he was nineteen years old. When the great pole al-Hasan Abarkan came across it, he was amazed, and ordered that it be hidden until its author completes forty years; so that he not be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no equal to it as far as I know, and he prayed for its author. And among that: He was seen one day very depressed, with changed color. He was asked about that, and after insistence and a condition of secrecy, he replied: Allah the Exalted showed me the vision of Hell and what is in it, we seek refuge in Allah from it. From then on I have been changing and grieving until now, and this is the reason for my change.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a collection of anecdotes illustrating the karamat (miracles of saints) of Imam Sanusi. The first story tells of a man who had meat that would not cook, and the Imam assures him that whoever prays behind him will be protected from fire, implying the meat was blessed. The second story involves a woman who lost her key and used tawassul (intercession) through the Imam, resulting in the door opening. The third story describes how the Imam wrote a major commentary at a young age, and a saintly figure ordered it hidden until he was forty to protect him from the evil eye. The fourth story has the Imam seeing a vision of Hell, causing him lasting sorrow. These stories highlight the Imam's spiritual station and the reality of karamat.

Key Terms
توسل
جاه
ولاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawassul means worshipping the saint instead of Allah.
Correction: Tawassul is asking the saint to supplicate to Allah on one's behalf, not worshipping the saint.

Checkpoint
What did the woman do when she couldn't open the lock?
A) Called a locksmith
B) Broke the door
C) Sought intercession through the Imam
D) Gave up

Key Takeaway
Tawassul through the awliya is a recognized practice that brings about divine assistance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an impossible situation like the woman’s locked door, do you exhaust every worldly means before even considering tawassul? What would it take for you to put the Imam forward from the very start, trusting that his status with Allah is the key?
?
The woman had to reach a point of complete helplessness before she sought intercession. Are there areas in your life where you are still trying to open the door yourself, refusing to ask for help from those whom Allah has honored? What is the cost of that pride?
?
If you truly believed that the awliya can open doors for you—not as a superstition but as a reality witnessed in this story—would you face your current struggles with more hope? Commit to one specific situation this week where you will practice tawassul with full conviction.

The Great Commentary Written at Nineteen
A story about the Imam's early scholarly accomplishment and its protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Sanusi's early authorship of a major commentary was a karama protected from the evil eye.

Core Idea
Youthful mastery blessed by Allah through karamat.

This story highlights a different kind of karama: extraordinary knowledge and wisdom at a young age. Imam Sanusi authored a significant commentary at nineteen, and a saintly figure ordered it hidden to protect him from envy.

Guided Path
1
Read about the commentary
Read the Arabic and translation about the authorship.
Notice the title he gave.
2
Notice the reaction of the saint
Shaykh al-Hasan Abarkan was amazed and acknowledged its uniqueness.
3
Understand the wisdom of hiding it
The order to hide until age forty was to protect from the evil eye. Reflect on the reality of envy.

Source Text

Misconception & Correction

A) It was not good enough

Extraordinary knowledge at a young age can be a karama, and protection from envy is wise.

?
Have you ever achieved something impressive and felt the urge to broadcast it? How does the saint's order to hide this work until age forty challenge your desire for recognition?
?
Think of a blessing Allah has given you that might be envied. Are you guarding it wisely, or exposing it to harm? What concrete step can you take today to protect it?
?
The saint saw this young scholar's work as unique and prayed for him. Is there a young person in your life whose spiritual or intellectual gifts you have overlooked? What will you do to recognize and support them?

The Vision of Hell
A story of the Imam seeing a vision of Hell and its effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Sanusi's vision of Hell affected his demeanor and deepened his spirituality.

Core Idea
A glimpse of Hell transforms the soul forever.

The final story reveals a profound spiritual experience: Imam Sanusi was shown a vision of Hell, which caused him lasting sorrow and change. This demonstrates the seriousness of the afterlife in the lives of the awliya.

Guided Path
1
Read the story
Read the Arabic and translation.
Notice the external signs of his state.
2
Note the Imam's condition
He was depressed and his color changed. This shows the impact of the vision.
3
Understand the cause
The vision of Hell was shown by Allah. This is a type of unveiling (mukashafa).
He keeps it secret except under duress.

Source Text

What did Imam Sanusi see that caused his change?

?
If you were shown a vision of Hell right now, would your life change as dramatically as the Imam's? What is holding you back from taking the reality of Hell as seriously as he did? What one concrete change will you make today because of this lesson?
?
The Imam's transformation was visible to others—his depression and changed color were noticed. Is your inner spiritual state reflected in your outward appearance and behavior? What would those closest to you say about the impact of your faith on your daily life?
?
You have just read that a single glimpse of Hell permanently altered the Imam's soul. You already know about Hell from the Quran and Sunnah. Why hasn't this knowledge had the same effect on you? What deep-seated resistance or distraction do you need to remove to let the truth of the Hereafter truly penetrate your heart?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
