Imam Sanusi's Final Days and Last Prayer
Al-Malali narrates the imam's withdrawal and his final prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circumstances of Imam Sanusi's final days and the depth of his concern for the community's spiritual well-being.

Core Idea
Even in his final weakness, Imam Sanusi prioritized the people's hearts over his own comfort.

This lesson presents a moving biographical account from Imam Sanusi's last days. It shows how his withdrawal from social engagement was followed by a heroic effort to lead the community in prayer despite severe illness. The narrative reveals the imam's deep sense of responsibility and compassion.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative of withdrawal
Begin by reading the full passage. Notice how the imam gradually withdrew from people and found going to the mosque difficult.
2
Understand the community's distress
Identify the community's reaction to his absence—they became distressed. This sets the stage for his sacrifice.
3
Witness the imam's sacrifice
Focus on the final Friday: he could barely ascend the mosque but forced himself for the people, completing Asr prayer with great difficulty.
This was his last prayer.
4
Reflect on the lesson of selfless leadership
Consider the moral: true leaders put others' needs before their own, even in extreme weakness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان رضي الله عنه في أواخر عمره كثير الانقباض عن الخلق، لا يكاد ينبسط مع أحد كما كانت عادته قبل ذلك، ويشق عليه الخروج إلى المسجد للإقراء والصلاة، ولا يخرج إليه في بعض الأيام إلا حياءً من الناس الذين ينتظرونه في المسجد للصلاة. ولمَّا أحس رضي الله تعالى عنه بألم مرضه الذي توفي منه.. انقطع عن المسجد، فسمع الناس بمرضه، فصاروا يأتون إلى المسجد فلا يجدونه، فتتغير قلوبهم من فقدان الشيخ وعدم رؤيته لهم، فأخبر الشيخ بذلك، فصار يتكلف الخروج إلى المسجد للصلاة لأجل الناس، فإذا رأوه فرحوا وسُرُّوا بخروجه ورؤيته. فخرج يوماً وأتى لباب المسجد، وأراد الصعود إليه، فلم يقدر، فقال: كيف أطلع إلى المسجد يا ربِّ؛ أو كما قال، فهم بالرجوع إلى داره فبدا له خوفاً من أن يدخل على الناس حزناً برجوعه، فتكلف الصعود إلى المسجد، وصلى بالناس صلاة، وصلى بالناس صلاة عصر يوم الجمعة، ولم يكمل الصلاة إلا بشق النفس، وهذه آخر صلاة صلاها.
He, may God be pleased with him, in the last part of his life was greatly withdrawn from people, hardly opening up to anyone as was his custom before that, and going out to the mosque for teaching and prayer became difficult for him, and he would not go out on some days except out of shyness from the people who were waiting for him in the mosque for prayer. And when he, may God be pleased with him, felt the pain of the illness from which he died, he stopped going to the mosque. The people heard of his illness, and they would come to the mosque and not find him, and their hearts would become distressed from the loss of the Shaykh and not seeing him. So the Shaykh was informed of that, and he began to force himself to go out to the mosque for prayer for the sake of the people, and when they saw him they rejoiced and were delighted by his coming out and seeing him. So one day he went out and came to the door of the mosque, and wanted to ascend to it, but he could not, so he said: 'How can I ascend to the mosque, O Lord?' or as he said, and he intended to return to his home, but it occurred to him out of fear that he would cause grief to the people by his return, so he forced himself to ascend to the mosque, and led the people in prayer, and led the people in the Asr prayer on Friday, and he did not complete the prayer except with great difficulty, and this was the last prayer he prayed.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing Imam Sanusi's final days. It relates how in his old age he became withdrawn and found it hard to go to the mosque. When his illness intensified, he stopped going, which distressed the community. To alleviate their sorrow, he forced himself to go out and pray with them. On one Friday, he could barely ascend to the mosque, but fearing to disappoint the people, he managed to lead the Asr prayer with great difficulty—this was his last prayer.

Key Terms
الانقباض عن الخلق
شق النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Sanusi force himself to go to the mosque even when he could barely ascend?
A) To teach a lesson about patience
B) For the sake of the people who were distressed by his absence
C) Because it was a religious obligation that could not be missed
D) To show his devotion despite illness

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's last actions teach us that true leadership is marked by compassion and sacrifice for the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you chose to endure physical or emotional pain for the sake of others' hearts? What held you back?
?
Imam Sanusi could not even climb the mosque steps, yet he pushed himself because people's joy mattered more than his comfort. Is there a relationship, community, or duty you have been avoiding because of your own weakness? What would it cost you to show up for them—and what would it cost them if you don't?
?
If you knew today were your last chance to serve others in worship, would you force yourself to join them despite every excuse not to? What excuse are you hiding behind right now?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
Imam Sanusi's Final Days: A Lesson in Patience and Faith
Al-Malali recounts the imam's final conversation and his death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the events of Imam Sanusi's final illness and death, and the lessons of patience and trust in Allah demonstrated by his response.

Core Idea
Even in death's throes, the imam's faith never wavered.

The passage narrates the last days of Imam Sanusi. After a vision where he was told his death was near, he showed remarkable patience and clarity. His story teaches us about the reality of death and the importance of maintaining faith and composure even in the most difficult moments.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the Arabic passage once and then its English translation. Notice the sequence of events from his return home to his death.
Pay attention to the details of his vision and his conversation with his wife.
2
Identify the key events
List the main events: returning home, refusing food, losing consciousness, the vision, the conversation about the endowment, the ten-day illness, patient suffering, and the death throes.
3
Reflect on the imam's response
Consider how he remained calm, did not complain, and continued to interact with others despite intense pain.
He did not moan until the last three days.
4
Understand the significance of the vision
The vision of angels ascending him to heaven and the command to leave the endowment shows his spiritual state and that such experiences are possible for saints.
This guards against the misconception that only prophets receive such visions.
5
Learn from his example
Apply the lessons of patience and trust in Allah during trials. Reflect on how the imam's conduct can inspire your own faith.

فرجع إلى داره، فبقي إلى صبيحة يوم السبت من الغد، فقربت إليه زوجته طعاماً، فقال لها: لا أقدر على شيء، فقالت له: وأيُّ شيء بك؟ فقال لها: أنا تخلفت، ثم غاب عن حسّه، فبقي على تلك الحالة النهار كله. ثم كلمته زوجته وقالت له: ما الذي غيّبك عن حِسّكَ؟ أو قريباً من هذا، فقال لها: إنَّ الملائكة قد صعدت بي إلى السماء الدنيا، فسمعت قائلاً يقول لي: اترك ما أنت عليه فقد قَرُبَ أَجلُكَ، ثم قال: لا أستطيع أن أفسِّرَ لك بقية ما رأيت، أو كما قال. فقالت له زوجته: وما الذي أُمرت بتركه؟ قال لها: قد تركت ذلك المحبس لا آخذ منه شيئاً أبداً. ثم إنه لازم الفراش من حينئذ إلى أن توفي، ومدة مرضه عشرة أيام، وفي كل ساعة يتقوّى مرضه وتضاعف ألمه وتضعف قوته وحركته، ويثقل لسانه، وهو مع ذلك ثابت العقل لم يتأوَّه ولا أنَّ بالكلية، ثم تجده مع ذلك يكلّم من كلمه، ويسلم على من سلَّم عليه أو يشير له. فلمَّا قَرُب أجله بثلاثة أيام دخلته سكرات الموت، فرجع يتأوه.
So he returned to his home, and remained until the morning of Saturday the following day. His wife brought food to him, and he said to her: 'I cannot do anything.' She said to him: 'What is the matter with you?' He said to her: 'I have fallen behind.' Then he lost consciousness, and remained in that state the entire day. Then his wife spoke to him and said: 'What has taken away your consciousness?' or something close to this. He said to her: 'The angels have ascended with me to the nearest heaven, and I heard a speaker saying to me: Leave what you are doing, for your term has drawn near.' Then he said: 'I cannot explain to you the rest of what I saw,' or as he said. His wife said to him: 'What have you been commanded to leave?' He said to her: 'I have left that endowment (ḥabs); I will never take anything from it.' Then he took to bed from then until he died. The duration of his illness was ten days. Every hour his illness grew stronger, his pain doubled, his strength and movement weakened, and his tongue became heavy, yet he remained of sound mind, not groaning nor moaning at all. Moreover, he would speak to whoever spoke to him, and greet whoever greeted him or gesture to him. When his term drew near by three days, the throes of death came upon him, and he began to groan.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative of the imam's final days. After his last prayer, he returned home. The next day, he could not eat, saying 'I have fallen behind' (likely meaning he felt his death approaching). He then lost consciousness for a day. When he regained awareness, he told his wife that angels had taken him to the lowest heaven, where he heard a voice telling him to leave what he was doing, as his death was near. He refused to explain more. His wife asked what he was commanded to leave; he said he had left an endowment (ḥabs) and would never take from it. He then remained bedridden for ten days, his condition worsening, but he stayed fully conscious, patient, and responsive, neither moaning nor complaining until the last three days, when death throes began and he groaned.

المحبس
سكرات الموت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The imam's vision of angels contradicts Islamic belief because only prophets receive such experiences.
Correction: In Sunni Islam, saints (awliya') can experience visions and spiritual states, including seeing angels and being transported. This is not exclusive to prophets.

Checkpoint

A) His teaching
B) His family
C) A particular endowment (ḥabs)
D) His prayers

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's final days demonstrate profound patience, spiritual awareness, and unwavering faith in the face of death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a serious illness or hardship, do you react with the same patience as the imam, or do you complain and lose hope? What would need to change in your heart to reflect his trust in Allah?
?
The imam was commanded to leave his endowment and obeyed immediately. What worldly attachment do you find hardest to let go of, and how can you start detaching from it today for the sake of your Hereafter?
?
If you were told your death was near, as the imam was, would your inner state be one of peace or fear? What can you do right now to prepare your soul for that moment?

The Saint’s Death and Steadfast Faith
Biographical account of a saint's final days, illness, and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the signs of a good death as exemplified by the saint's unwavering faith, stable mind, and hopeful response to loved ones during his final illness.

Core Idea
A true saint's death is marked by unwavering faith, stable mind, and hope in Allah's mercy.

This passage presents a moving account of a saint's final days, demonstrating how deep faith manifests even in the throes of death. It is not merely a biography but a spiritual lesson on how to face the end with patience, presence of heart, and trust in Allah's promise. As you read, notice the saint's reactions to various events—his vision, his weakness, his family's questions—and how each reveals his steadfastness.

Guided Path
1
Witness the initial signs of departure
Read about the saint's last prayer, his feeling of 'falling behind', and the vision of angels commanding him to leave his ascetic prison. Notice how he immediately obeys and explains his state to his wife.
This shows his sensitivity to spiritual reality even before physical decline.
2
Observe the ten-day illness
The passage describes his physical deterioration over ten days, yet emphasizes that his mind remained stable (thabit al-'aql). He did not groan or complain, and continued to respond to others.
Stable mind in severe illness is a key sign of sainthood.
3
Reflect on the death throes and shahada
When the agonies of death intensify, his nephew prompts him with the shahada. The saint's reply—'Is there anything else?'—shows his heart is already absorbed in remembrance, even if his tongue cannot utter it.
This guards against the misconception that a struggling death indicates lack of faith.
4
Contemplate the falling prayer bead and final prayer
When his prayer bead falls, he says 'Worship has gone, O Muhammad,' acknowledging the end of physical devotion. Yet he ends with a prayer to die uttering the shahada with knowledge, reaffirming his hope.
The falling bead symbolizes the end of physical acts; the heart remains connected.

يكمل الصلاة إلا بشق النفس، وهذه آخر صلاة صلاها الغد، فقربت فرجع إلى داره، فبقي إلى صبيحة يوم السبت من إليه زوجته طعاماً، فقال لها: لا أقدر على شيء فقال لها: لا أقدر على شيء(۱)، فقالت له: وأيُّ شيء بك؟ فقال لها: أنا تخلفت، ثم غاب عن حسّه، فبقي على تلك الحالة النهار كله من ثم كلمته زوجته وقالت له: ما الذي غيبك عن حِسّكَ؟ أو قريباً بي إلى السماء الدنيا، هذا، فقال لها: إنَّ الملائكة قد صعدت فسمعت قائلاً يقول لي: اترك ما أنت عليه فقد قَرُبَ أَجلُكَ، ثم قال: لا أستطيع أن أفسِّرَ لك بقية ما رأيت، أو كما قال فقالت له زوجته: وما الذي أُمرت بتركه؟ قال لها: قد تركت ذلك المحبس لا آخذ منه شيئاً أبداً. حبس ثم إنه لازم الفراش من حينئذ إلى أن توفي، ومدة مرضه عشرة أيام، وفي كل ساعة يتقوّى مرضه وتضاعف ألمه وتضعف قوته وحركته، ويثقل لسانه، وهو مع ذلك ثابت العقل [لم] يتأوَّه ولا أنَّ بالكلية، ثم تجده مع ذلك يكلّم من كلمه، ويسلم على من سلَّم عليه أو يشير له فلمَّا قَرُب أجله بثلاثة أيام دخلته سكرات الموت، فرجع يتأوه (۱) وقد ذكر الملالي في المواهب القدسية » ( ق ۱۳ ) أنه بلغ به الجهد حتى عجز عن التيمم وأركان الصلاة، فقال: ( رحم الله تعالى أبا حنيفة حيث قال بسقوطها ) يعني: الصلاة ٤٨ بالقهر ويميل يميناً وشمالاً، فنظرت إليه وقد احمرت وجنتاه وأرخيت عيناه وشفتاه (۱)، واشتدَّ نَفَسُهُ، وتقوى صعوده وهبوطه، فلم أملك صبراً على البكاء بما عاينت من شدة مقاساته وعظيم صبره على ذلك، ففارقته وظننتُ أنه لا يبقى تلك الليلة، وكانت ليلة السبت، فبقي في النزع تلك الليلة والأحد إلى بعد العصر، فكان ابن أخيه حينئذ يلقنه الشهادة مرة بعد مرة، فالتفت الشيخ له وقال بكلام ضعيف جداً: وهل ثَمَّ غيرها؟ ! يعني: أنه رضي الله تعالى عنه ليس بغافل عنها بقلبه في هذا الوقت، وإن كنت لم نطق بها اللسان فحينئذ استبشروا بذلك، وعرف الحاضرون أنه ثابت العقل، ليس بغافل عن الله سبحانه هو و وكانت بنته رضي الله عنها تقول له حينئذٍ: تمشي وتتركني؟! فقال لها: الجنة تجمعنا عن قريب إن شاء الله تعالى وكانت في يده رضي الله تعالى عنه سبحة، فلما اشتدَّ مرضه سقطت السبحة من يده، فبقي كذلك ما شاء الله، ثم التفت إلى السبحة فلم يجدها في يده، فقال: مشت العبادة يا محمد؛ يعني: نفسه وكان رضي الله عنه يقول عند موته: نسأله سبحانه أن يجعلنا وأحبتنا عند الموت ناطقين بكلمتي الشهادة عالمين بها (۱) وانظر هنا » المواهب القدسية » ( ق ۹۳ ) .
He completed the prayer except with difficulty, and this was the last prayer he prayed the next day [?], so he returned to his house and remained until the morning of Saturday. His wife brought food to him [?] and he said to her: 'I am not able to do anything.' He said to her: 'I am not able to do anything(1).' She said to him: 'What is the matter with you?' He said to her: 'I have fallen behind.' Then he lost consciousness and remained in that state the whole day. Then his wife spoke to him and said: 'What has made you lose your senses? Or near to me, to the lowest heaven, this.' He said to her: 'Indeed, the angels ascended and I heard a speaker saying to me: Leave what you are upon, for your term has drawn near.' Then he said: 'I cannot explain to you the rest of what I saw,' or as he said. His wife asked him: 'What were you commanded to leave?' He said to her: 'I have left that prison; I will never take anything from it.' A prison. Then he took to bed from then until he died. The duration of his illness was ten days. Every hour his illness grew stronger, his pain multiplied, his strength and movement weakened, his tongue became heavy, yet with all that he was of stable mind; he did not groan nor sigh at all. Moreover, he would speak to whoever spoke to him and greet whoever greeted him or gesture to him. When his term drew near by three days, the agonies of death came upon him, so he began to groan involuntarily (1). Al-Malali mentioned in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (fol. 13) that the effort reached such a point that he was incapable of tayammum and the pillars of prayer, so he said: 'May Allah have mercy on Abu Hanifa, for he allowed its omission' meaning prayer. Page 48. By force he would sway left and right. I looked at him and his cheeks had reddened, his eyes and lips had slackened (1), his breathing became intense, his rising and falling became strong. I could not bear to cry at what I witnessed of the severity of his struggles and the greatness of his patience in that. So I left him and thought he would not survive that night. It was Saturday night. He remained in the death throes that night and Sunday until after 'Asr. His nephew was then prompting him with the shahada repeatedly. The shaykh turned to him and said with very weak speech: 'Is there anything else?' Meaning: that he, may Allah be pleased with him, was not heedless of it in his heart at that time, even if I did not utter it with the tongue. So then they rejoiced at that, and those present knew that he was of stable mind, not heedless of Allah Almighty. He also said to his daughter, may Allah be pleased with her, who was saying to him at that time: 'Will you walk away and leave me?' He said to her: 'Paradise will gather us soon, Allah willing.' He had a prayer bead (subha) in his hand. When his illness intensified, the prayer bead fell from his hand. He remained like that as Allah willed. Then he turned to the prayer bead and did not find it in his hand, so he said: 'Worship has gone, O Muhammad,' meaning himself. He, may Allah be pleased with him, used to say at his death: 'We ask Him, glorified, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the two words of shahada, knowledgeable of them.' (1) See here 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (fol. 93).
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing the final days and death of a saint. It begins with his last prayer and his feeling of being 'fallen behind' (takhalluftu). He loses consciousness and then reports a vision: angels ascended and a voice told him to leave what he was doing because his time was near. When asked what he was commanded to leave, he says he abandoned a prison (al-mahbas), likely a place of ascetic confinement. The narrative then details his ten-day illness, emphasizing his steadfastness: though his body weakened, his mind remained stable (thabit al-'aql). He did not groan or complain. As death approached, the agonies (sakarat al-mawt) intensified, yet he still responded to others. His nephew prompted him with the shahada, and the saint's response—'Is there anything else?'—shows he was already mindful of it. His daughter's question about leaving her is met with an assurance of reunion in Paradise. Even his fallen prayer bead becomes a lesson: he says 'Worship has gone,' meaning that as the bead drops, the act of dhikr has ended, but his heart remains connected. Finally, he prays to die uttering the shahada with knowledge. The passage serves as a model of a good death, demonstrating perfect faith, patience, and presence of mind.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person who experiences severe physical struggles and groaning at death is likely unaware or in despair, indicating weak faith.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that despite intense agonies and involuntary groaning, the saint was of stable mind (thabit al-'aql) and not heedless of Allah. His response to the shahada — 'Is there anything else?' — shows his heart was fully present, even if his tongue could not utter the words.

Key Takeaway
The saint's death teaches that true faith remains constant even when the body fails; steadfastness and hope in Allah are the hallmarks of a blessed end.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the saint heard 'Leave what you are upon,' he immediately abandoned his cherished ascetic practice. What attachment in your life would be most painful for you to leave if Allah called you today? Are you ready to release it now, or will you wait until the angel speaks?
?
The saint's body failed—he could not pray, could not hold the prayer beads, could not even speak clearly—yet his heart was fully with Allah. Is your connection to Allah strong enough to survive when your health, abilities, and routines are stripped away? What are you building to last beyond your strength?
?
His daughter wept and asked why he would 'walk away and leave her,' and he promised reunion in Paradise. Who are you leaving behind, and have you given them hope and faith that will sustain them in your absence—or only grief? What are you doing today to ensure your farewell leads them toward Jannah?

The Death of a Saint: Lessons in Faith and Mindfulness
Describes the shaykh's final illness, death, and burial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exemplary death of a saintly scholar and the importance of maintaining consciousness of Allah even in the throes of death.

Core Idea
A saint's death is a mirror of his life: fully aware of Allah until the last breath.

This passage recounts the final moments of a revered shaykh, revealing profound spiritual realities. Beyond the historical narrative, it offers timeless lessons about faith, presence of heart, and the tranquility of believers facing death. Let us witness how the shaykh's entire life culminates in this sacred departure.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative of the deathbed
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then the translation. Observe the details: physical suffering, reactions of those present, and the shaykh's responses.
Notice that the shaykh is in severe pain yet remains composed.
2
Analyze the shahada prompting
Focus on the exchange with the nephew. The shaykh says 'Is there anything else?' Why is this significant? It shows his heart was already engaged with the shahada, even if his tongue could not utter it.
This distinguishes between 'ilm al-yaqin (knowledge of the heart) and utterance with the tongue.
3
Reflect on the daughter's question
Consider the daughter's plea and the shaykh's reassuring response about Paradise. What does this teach about a believer's outlook at death?
The shaykh replaces worldly attachment with hope in divine reunion.
4
Examine the rosary incident
When the rosary slips from his hand, he says 'Worship has gone.' What does this reveal about his constant awareness of worship?
Even in severe illness, his focus remains on 'ibadah.

فنظرت إليه وقد احمرت وجنتاه وأرخيت عيناه وشفتاه (۱) ، واشتدَّ نَفَسُهُ ، وتقوى صعوده وهبوطه ، فلم أملك صبراً على البكاء بما عاينت من شدة مقاساته وعظيم صبره على ذلك ، ففارقته وظننتُ أنه لا يبقى تلك الليلة ، وكانت ليلة السبت ، فبقي في النزع تلك الليلة والأحد إلى بعد العصر ، فكان ابن أخيه حينئذ يلقنه الشهادة مرة بعد مرة ، فالتفت الشيخ له وقال بكلام ضعيف جداً : وهل ثَمَّ غيرها ؟ ! يعني : أنه رضي الله تعالى عنه ليس بغافل عنها بقلبه في هذا الوقت ، وإن كنت لم أنطق بها اللسان

وأخبرتني والدتي رحمها الله تعالى عن بنت الشيخ رضي الله عنها أنها شمت رائحة المسك في البيت بنَفَس موت أبيها ، وشمَّته أيضاً في جسده ، والله تعالى أعلم
نسأله سبحانه أن يُقدِّس روحه ، وأن يسكنه في أعالي الفردوس فسيحه ، وأن يجعله ممَّن يتنعم في كل لحظة برؤية ذاته العلية العديمة النظير والمثال ، وأن ينفعنا به في الدنيا والآخرة ، وأن يجمعنا معه بفضله وكرمه في أعلى المنازل الفاخرة ، بجاه سيدنا ونبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وعلى آله عدد خلقه ، ورضا نفسه ، ووزنة عرشه ، ومداد كلماته

I looked at him and his cheeks had reddened, his eyes and lips relaxed, his breathing intensified, and his rising and falling became strong. I could not bear to cry because of what I witnessed of his severe suffering and his great patience with that. So I left him and thought that he would not survive that night. It was Saturday night. He remained in agony that night and Sunday until after 'Asr. His nephew was then prompting him with the shahada repeatedly. The shaykh turned to him and said with very weak speech: 'Is there anything else?' Meaning: that he, may Allah be pleased with him, was not heedless of it in his heart at this time, even if I did not utter it with the tongue. Then they rejoiced at that, and those present knew that he was of sound mind, not heedless of Allah, exalted is He. His daughter, may Allah be pleased with her, was saying to him then: 'You are walking and leaving me?!' He said to her: 'Paradise will gather us soon, if Allah wills.' He had a rosary in his hand, may Allah be pleased with him. When his illness intensified, the rosary fell from his hand. He remained like that for as long as Allah willed. Then he turned to the rosary and did not find it in his hand. He said: 'Worship has gone, O Muhammad'; meaning his self. He, may Allah be pleased with him, used to say at the time of death: 'We ask Him, exalted is He, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the two words of shahada, knowing them.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, on Sunday after 'Asr, the eighteenth of Jumada al-Akhira, in the year eight hundred and ninety-five. My mother, may Allah have mercy on her, told me about the daughter of the shaykh, may Allah be pleased with her, that she smelled the scent of musk in the house during her father's death pangs, and she also smelled it on his body. And Allah knows best. We ask Him, exalted is He, to sanctify his soul, to settle him in the highest expanses of Paradise, to make him among those who delight every moment in the vision of His lofty essence, without peer or likeness, to benefit us through him in this world and the Hereafter, and to gather us with him by His favor and generosity in the highest noble stations, for the sake of our master, our Prophet, and our patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and his family as number of His creatures, His own pleasure, the weight of His Throne, and the ink of His words. The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He was buried during the midday of Monday after it, alongside the grave of his righteous brother, the scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Tanluti, may Allah sanctify his soul, at 'Ayn Wanwata outside Bab al-Jiyad. We attended his funeral, and it was extremely crowded; the streets were filled with people. The sultan and those below him attended, and he offered eulogy befitting him. The people regretted his loss, and rightly so. His age that day was fifty-six years. May Allah benefit us through him and gather us with him in...'

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the death of a revered shaykh, likely the author's teacher or a saintly figure. It begins with a description of his physical state during his final illness: his cheeks reddened, eyes and lips relaxed, breathing labored, and his body rising and falling with effort. The narrator is overcome with emotion and leaves, assuming he will not survive the night (Saturday). However, he lingers in agony through Sunday until after 'Asr. His nephew prompts him with the shahada repeatedly, but the shaykh responds with weak speech: 'Is there anything else?' This indicates he was already mindful of the shahada in his heart, even if his tongue could not utter it. Those present take comfort that he is of sound mind and not heedless of Allah. His daughter asks him not to leave her, and he reassures her that Paradise will reunite them soon. At one point his prayer beads (subha) fall from his hand; he later notices their absence and says, 'Worship has gone, O Muhammad,' referring to himself, showing his constant awareness of devotion. His customary prayer at death is recorded: asking Allah to make him and his loved ones utter the shahada knowingly at death. The date of death is given: Sunday after 'Asr, 18 Jumada al-Akhira 895 AH. A miraculous scent of musk is reported by the shaykh's daughter during his death pangs and on his body. The narrator then offers a supplication for the shaykh's soul, asking for sanctification, high rank in Paradise, enjoyment of the vision of Allah's essence, benefit through him, and reunion in noble stations, for the sake of the Prophet. Finally, Abu Ja'far al-Balawi reports the burial details: buried Monday midday beside his brother Abu al-Hasan al-Tanluti at 'Ayn Wanwata outside Bab al-Jiyad. The funeral was crowded, attended by the sultan and many people, with eulogies and universal regret. The shaykh was 56 years old. The account ends mid-sentence with the hope of gathering with him.

Key Terms
شهادة
سبحة
نزع
رؤية ذات الله
مسك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A believer who cannot speak the shahada at death is deprived of faith.
Correction: The shaykh's inability to utter the shahada aloud did not indicate heedlessness; his heart was fully aware, and that inner faith was sufficient.

Checkpoint
What did the shaykh say when his nephew prompted him with the shahada?
A) 'I testify that there is no god but Allah'
B) 'Is there anything else?'
C) 'Worship has gone'
D) 'Peace be upon you'

Key Takeaway
The shaykh's death demonstrates that true faith is a constant awareness of Allah, manifesting even in the final moments of life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The shaykh, in his final agony, could not speak but his heart was still full of shahada. If you were in his place, would your heart be so accustomed to Allah's remembrance that it would continue even when your tongue fails? What are you doing now to build that habit of heart-awareness?
?
When the shaykh's rosary fell, he said 'Worship has gone, O Muhammad.' How much of your worship is tied to external tools and routines? If they were taken away, would your inner connection to Allah remain? What step can you take today to make your worship more heart-centered?
?
The shaykh reassured his daughter with the promise of Paradise: 'Paradise will gather us soon.' Is there a worldly attachment in your life that you would struggle to release for the sake of that same promise? What would it take for you to trust Allah's promise enough to let go?

The Death and the Fragrance of Musk
Announcement of death with a miraculous sign and prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the miraculous musk fragrance as a sign of sainthood and the pious response to the scholar's death.

Core Idea
Even in death, the saint's body is honored with the scent of paradise.

The account opens with the precise date of the scholar's death, then immediately reports a miraculous sign: the fragrance of musk filled the house at the moment of passing and clung to his body. This was witnessed by the scholar's daughter, transmitted through the author's mother. Such accounts are common in hagiography, affirming the deceased's spiritual rank. We will read the passage and reflect on its devotional tone.

Guided Path
1
Read the death announcement
Locate the date and the way the author invokes mercy. Notice the precise time ('Sunday after Asr') and the Hijri date.
The year is 895 AH, which corresponds roughly to 1490 CE.
2
Identify the miracle
Find the sentence about the musk fragrance. What two specific details are given about it?
It was smelled in the house 'at the breath of death' and also on the body.
3
Examine the prayer that follows
After the miracle, the author prays for the scholar's soul. What does he ask for? List the three requests.
Sanctification of soul, highest paradise, and vision of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأحد بعد العصر ، الثامن وتوفي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه يوم عشر من جمادى الآخرة ، من عام خمسة وتسعين بعد ثمان مئة وأخبرتني والدتي رحمها الله تعالى عن بنت الشيخ رضي الله عنها أنها شمت رائحة المسك في البيت بنَفَس موت أبيها ، وشمَّته أيضاً في جسده ، والله تعالى أعلم نسأله سبحانه أن يُقدِّس روحه ، وأن يسكنه في أعالي الفردوس فسيحه ، وأن يجعله ممَّن يتنعم في كل لحظة برؤية ذات العلية العديمة النظير والمثال ، وأن ينفعنا به في الدنيا والآخرة ، وأن يجمعنا معه بفضله وكرمه في أعلى المنازل الفاخرة ، بجاه سيدنا ونبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وعلى آله عدد خلقه ، ورضا نفسه ، ومداد كلماته قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( ودفن بين ظهري يوم الاثنين بعده حذاء قبر أخيه الصالح العلامة أبي الحسن التانلوتي قدس الله تعالى روحه بعين وانزوته خارج باب الجياد ، حضرنا جنازته ، وكانت في غاية الحفول ؛ غصَّت الشوارع فيها بالناس ، وحضرها السلطان فمن دونه ، وأتبع ثناءً يليق مثله ، وتأسف الناس لفقده وبحق ، وكانت سنه يومئذٍ ستاً وخمسين سنة ، نفعنا الله تعالى به ، وجمعنا به في مستقر رحمته ، إنه ولي ذلك والقادر عليه ومما رثاه الفقيه الأجل أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الرحمن الحوضي بعد وفاته : من الكامل ما للمنازل أظلمَتْ أرجاؤُها والأرض رجتْ حِينَ خَابَ رجاؤُها هذا الذي ورثَ النبيَّ فأصبحَتْ علل الضلال به استفيد دواؤها هذا الذي تبعَ النبي وصحبَهُ فانجابَ عن سُبُلِ الهدى ظلماؤُها يا أيها النفس المقدسة التي لبقائها المحمودِ كَانَ فَناؤُها يا أوحد العلماء يا عَلَماً بهِ كلُّ العلوم بدَتْ لنا أنحاؤها يا درة الزهَّادِ یا غوثاً بهِ يُرجى لأمراض القلوب شفاؤها أخلاقُكَ التسليم يصحبها الرضا بالله منشور عليكَ لـواؤُها بلت ترابه سحب الرضوان ، وجعل الله مستقره فراديس الجنان
Sunday after the afternoon, the eighth [date?] And he died, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him and be pleased with him, on the tenth of Jumada al-Akhirah, of the year nine hundred and ninety-five. And my mother, may Allah Almighty have mercy on her, told me from the daughter of the Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with her, that she smelled the scent of musk in the house at the breath of her father's death, and she also smelled it on his body, and Allah Almighty knows best. We ask Him, Glory be to Him, to sanctify his soul, and to settle him in the highest paradises of His spacious [paradise], and to make him among those who delight at every moment in the vision of His exalted essence that has no peer or likeness, and to benefit us by him in this world and the next, and to gather us with him by His bounty and generosity in the highest of glorious abodes, for the sake of our Master, our Prophet, and our Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and his family, as many as His creation, and the pleasure of His self, and the ink of His words. The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He was buried between the noon and afternoon [prayers] on Monday afterward, opposite the grave of his righteous brother, the scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Tanlutiy (or al-Talanluti), may Allah Almighty sanctify his soul, in 'Ayn al-Wanazat outside Bab al-Jiyad. We attended his funeral, and it was extremely crowded; the streets were filled with people, and the Sultan and those below him attended, and he expressed praise befitting him, and the people regretted his loss, and rightly so. His age that day was fifty-six years. May Allah Almighty benefit us by him, and gather us with him in the abode of His mercy. Indeed, He is the Patron of that and is able to do it.' And among the elegies made for him after his death by the eminent jurist Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Hawdi: From the meter al-Kamil: 'What is with the houses, their corners darkened, and the earth quaked when its hope was disappointed? This is he who inherited the Prophet, so the diseases of misguidance found their cure through him. This is he who followed the Prophet and his companions, so the darkness of the paths of guidance cleared away. O pure soul, whose praised extinction was for its continuation? O unique of the scholars, O banner by which all the sciences became manifest to us in their aspects. O pearl of the ascetics, O succor with whom healing for the diseases of hearts is hoped. Your character is submission, accompanied by contentment with Allah. Raised over you is its banner. The clouds of divine pleasure watered his dust, and Allah made his abode the meadows of Paradise.'

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the death and burial of a revered scholar, likely the subject of the work (perhaps Imam Sanusi or a related figure). It begins by stating the exact date of death: the tenth of Jumada al-Akhirah in the year 995 AH (or 895? The text says 'five and ninety after eight hundred' which is 895? But could be 995? The translation uses 995? Actually 'خمسة وتسعين بعد ثمان مئة' is 895. Let's note that. The author then reports a miraculous sign: his mother smelled musk in the house at the moment of the scholar's death, and also on his body. This is a sign of sainthood. Then follows a prayer asking for his elevation and union with the Prophet. Next, a quote from another scholar, Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, describes the burial: it took place on Monday afternoon, opposite the grave of his brother, in a specific location outside Bab al-Jiyad. The funeral was extremely crowded, with the Sultan and many people attending. The scholar was 56 years old at death. Finally, a poetic elegy by the jurist al-Hawdi is presented. The poem praises the deceased as inheritor of the Prophet, a source of cure for misguidance, a unique scholar, a pearl of ascetics, and a succor for hearts. It ends by describing his character as submission and contentment with Allah, and concludes that divine pleasure rains on his grave and paradise is his abode.

?

?

?
The daughter perceived the musk as a sign. Are you attentive to the subtle signs of Allah's favor in your life, or are you too absorbed in your daily routines? How can you train yourself to notice and appreciate these blessings?

The Burial and the Grand Funeral
Account of the burial and the massive public funeral.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of the scholar's burial and the massive public funeral that honored him.

Core Idea
A saint's funeral draws the Sultan and the masses, reflecting his influence.

In this segment, another scholar, Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, provides a first-hand account of the burial and funeral. He describes the location, the timing, the enormous crowd, and the presence of the Sultan. It was a public outpouring of grief and honor. The passage underscores the social and spiritual stature of the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Locate the burial details
Find the day, time, and place of burial. Notice the proximity to the grave of his brother.
Buried on Monday, between noon and afternoon, opposite his brother's grave.
2
Observe the funeral crowd
The streets were filled. Who attended? What does the author emphasize about the crowd?
The Sultan attended, along with many people; the funeral was 'extremely crowded'.
3
Note the age and closing prayer
What was the scholar's age at death? How does the account end?
He was 56. The account ends with a prayer for benefit and reunion.

The Poet's Elegy for the Scholar
Poetic elegy praising the scholar's virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the virtues of the scholar as praised in the poetic elegy by al-Hawdi.

Core Idea
The scholar is celebrated as heir of the Prophet, cure for misguidance, and a source of spiritual healing.

The passage concludes with a poem composed by the jurist al-Hawdi. Written in the meter al-Kamil, it elegizes the deceased with powerful imagery. The poem highlights his role as inheritor of prophetic knowledge, a remedy for spiritual ailments, and a paragon of virtue. It is a fitting tribute that encapsulates the community's reverence.

Guided Path
1
Read the first two couplets
Notice the contrast: the darkened houses and quaking earth versus the hope restored through the scholar. What does the poet say he inherited?
He inherited from the Prophet, and through him the cure for misguidance was found.
2
Examine the middle section
The poet addresses the scholar directly with titles. List the titles used: 'O pure soul', 'O unique of the scholars', 'O pearl of the ascetics', 'O succor'. What do these indicate?
Each title highlights a different aspect of his excellence.
3
Analyze the final lines
How does the poem describe his character? What is said about his dust and abode?
His character is submission and contentment; his dust is watered by divine pleasure, and his abode is paradise.

الأحد بعد العصر ، الثامن وتوفي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه يوم عشر من جمادى الآخرة ، من عام خمسة وتسعين بعد ثمان مئة وأخبرتني والدتي رحمها الله تعالى عن بنت الشيخ رضي الله عنها أنها شمت رائحة المسك في البيت بنَفَس موت أبيها ، وشمَّته أيضاً في جسده ، والله تعالى أعلم نسأله سبحانه أن يُقدِّس روحه ، وأن يسكنه في أعالي الفردوس فسيحه ، وأن يجعله ممَّن يتنعم في كل لحظة برؤية ذات العلية العديمة النظير والمثال ، وأن ينفعنا به في الدنيا والآخرة ، وأن يجمعنا معه بفضله وكرمه في أعلى المنازل الفاخرة ، بجاه سيدنا ونبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وعلى آله عدد خلقه ، ورضا نفسه ، ومداد كلماته قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( ودفن بين ظهري يوم الاثنين بعده حذاء قبر أخيه الصالح العلامة أبي الحسن التانلوتي قدس الله تعالى روحه بعين وانزوته خارج باب الجياد ، حضرنا جنازته ، وكانت في غاية الحفول ؛ غصَّت الشوارع فيها بالناس ، وحضرها السلطان فمن دونه ، وأتبع ثناءً يليق مثله ، وتأسف الناس لفقده وبحق ، وكانت سنه يومئذٍ ستاً وخمسين سنة ، نفعنا الله تعالى به ، وجمعنا به في مستقر رحمته ، إنه ولي ذلك والقادر عليه ومما رثاه الفقيه الأجل أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الرحمن الحوضي بعد وفاته : من الكامل ما للمنازل أظلمَتْ أرجاؤُها والأرض رجتْ حِينَ خَابَ رجاؤُها هذا الذي ورثَ النبيَّ فأصبحَتْ علل الضلال به استفيد دواؤها هذا الذي تبعَ النبي وصحبَهُ فانجابَ عن سُبُلِ الهدى ظلماؤُها يا أيها النفس المقدسة التي لبقائها المحمودِ كَانَ فَناؤُها يا أوحد العلماء يا عَلَماً بهِ كلُّ العلوم بدَتْ لنا أنحاؤها يا درة الزهَّادِ یا غوثاً بهِ يُرجى لأمراض القلوب شفاؤها أخلاقُكَ التسليم يصحبها الرضا بالله منشور عليكَ لـواؤُها بلت ترابه سحب الرضوان ، وجعل الله مستقره فراديس الجنان
Sunday after the afternoon, the eighth [date?] And he died, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him and be pleased with him, on the tenth of Jumada al-Akhirah, of the year nine hundred and ninety-five. And my mother, may Allah Almighty have mercy on her, told me from the daughter of the Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with her, that she smelled the scent of musk in the house at the breath of her father's death, and she also smelled it on his body, and Allah Almighty knows best. We ask Him, Glory be to Him, to sanctify his soul, and to settle him in the highest paradises of His spacious [paradise], and to make him among those who delight at every moment in the vision of His exalted essence that has no peer or likeness, and to benefit us by him in this world and the next, and to gather us with him by His bounty and generosity in the highest of glorious abodes, for the sake of our Master, our Prophet, and our Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and his family, as many as His creation, and the pleasure of His self, and the ink of His words. The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He was buried between the noon and afternoon [prayers] on Monday afterward, opposite the grave of his righteous brother, the scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Tanlutiy (or al-Talanluti), may Allah Almighty sanctify his soul, in 'Ayn al-Wanazat outside Bab al-Jiyad. We attended his funeral, and it was extremely crowded; the streets were filled with people, and the Sultan and those below him attended, and he expressed praise befitting him, and the people regretted his loss, and rightly so. His age that day was fifty-six years. May Allah Almighty benefit us by him, and gather us with him in the abode of His mercy. Indeed, He is the Patron of that and is able to do it.' And among the elegies made for him after his death by the eminent jurist Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Hawdi: From the meter al-Kamil: 'What is with the houses, their corners darkened, and the earth quaked when its hope was disappointed? This is he who inherited the Prophet, so the diseases of misguidance found their cure through him. This is he who followed the Prophet and his companions, so the darkness of the paths of guidance cleared away. O pure soul, whose praised extinction was for its continuation? O unique of the scholars, O banner by which all the sciences became manifest to us in their aspects. O pearl of the ascetics, O succor with whom healing for the diseases of hearts is hoped. Your character is submission, accompanied by contentment with Allah. Raised over you is its banner. The clouds of divine pleasure watered his dust, and Allah made his abode the meadows of Paradise.'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the death and burial of a revered scholar, likely the subject of the work (perhaps Imam Sanusi or a related figure). It begins by stating the exact date of death: the tenth of Jumada al-Akhirah in the year 995 AH (or 895? The text says 'five and ninety after eight hundred' which is 895? But could be 995? The translation uses 995? Actually 'خمسة وتسعين بعد ثمان مئة' is 895. Let's note that. The author then reports a miraculous sign: his mother smelled musk in the house at the moment of the scholar's death, and also on his body. This is a sign of sainthood. Then follows a prayer asking for his elevation and union with the Prophet. Next, a quote from another scholar, Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, describes the burial: it took place on Monday afternoon, opposite the grave of his brother, in a specific location outside Bab al-Jiyad. The funeral was extremely crowded, with the Sultan and many people attending. The scholar was 56 years old at death. Finally, a poetic elegy by the jurist al-Hawdi is presented. The poem praises the deceased as inheritor of the Prophet, a source of cure for misguidance, a unique scholar, a pearl of ascetics, and a succor for hearts. It ends by describing his character as submission and contentment with Allah, and concludes that divine pleasure rains on his grave and paradise is his abode.

Praise of Imam Sanusi's Scholarly Precision and Status
Biographical praise of Sanusi's scholarly journey and acclaim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Sanusi's diligence and methodology in kalam earned him unparalleled scholarly recognition.

Core Idea
Sanusi's journey from taqlid to tahqiq became proverbial in kalam.

This passage opens with a vivid description of Imam al-Sanusi as a meticulous diver for knowledge, progressing from the most basic level to the highest verification. It then recounts his legendary status in kalam, illustrated by the testimony of a peer and the widespread acceptance of his works. The lesson highlights the qualities that made Sanusi a benchmark in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice the poetic opening and the anecdotal style.
Pay attention to the footnote markers.
2
Identify key descriptive phrases
Look for phrases that describe Sanusi's method: 'المدقق الحريص', 'غواص في لججه', 'من صغرى الصغرى الصغرى إلى شرح العقيدة الكبرى', 'من تقليد أعمى إلى تحقيق أسمى'. What do they convey?
These highlight his range and progressive refinement.
3
Understand the anecdote and its significance
Read Sheikh Abu Imran's statement: 'ما رأيتُ مَنْ غربلَ هذا العلم مثل هذا الرجل'. Why is the word 'غربل' (sifted) significant? How does this show Sanusi's status?
It implies he analyzed and purified the science.
4
Reflect on the impact of his works
Consider the last part: Sanusi's works were eagerly received by students and even examined by his teachers. What does this tell us about his legacy?
It shows immediate recognition and lasting influence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المدقق الحريص على نفائس العلم وحُلله ، والباحث الغواص في لججه لاستخراج درره ؛ فمن صغرى الصغرى الصغرى إلى شرح العقيدة الكبرى ومن تقليد أعمى إلى تحقيق أسمى ، فسبحان الفتاح على ما فتح ! وله الحمد تعالى على ما أعطى ومنح ومكانة الإمام في علم الكلام صارت مضرب مثل ، حتى قال الشيخ أبو عمران موسى بن عقدة الأغضاوي إذا ذُكر علم الكلام : ( ما رأيتُ مَنْ غربلَ هذا العلم مثل هذا الرجل ) يعني : السنوسي (1) وقبل رحيل إمامنا السنوسي عن هذه الدنيا الفانية . . قرت عينه حينما رأى مؤلفاته - وعلى رأسها « سنوسياته » ـ قد أقبل عليها طلبة العلم ، بل إنَّ بعض شيوخه نظر فيها واستخرج ما سُمِّي بكتاب حقائق السنوسي ) (1) نقله العلامة الشفشاوني في ( دوحة الناشر » ( ص ١٢١ - ١٢٢ ) .
The meticulous researcher eager for the jewels of knowledge and its ornaments, and the diver plunging into its depths to extract its pearls; from the smallest of the smallest of the small to the commentary on the Greatest Creed, and from blind imitation to the highest verification. So glory be to the Opener for what He has opened! And praise be to Him, exalted, for what He has given and bestowed. The status of the Imam in the science of kalam became a proverbial example, until Sheikh Abu Imran Musa ibn Uqda al-Aghdawi said, when the science of kalam was mentioned: 'I have not seen anyone who sifted this science like this man' — meaning al-Sanusi. (1) And before our Imam al-Sanusi departed from this fleeting world... his eyes were comforted when he saw his works — especially his 'Sanusiyyat' — being eagerly received by students of knowledge. Indeed, some of his teachers examined them and extracted what is called the book 'Haqa'iq al-Sanusi'. (1) Quoted by the scholar al-Shafshawani in 'Dawhat al-Nashir' (pp. 121-122).
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction praising Imam Sanusi's scholarly diligence and his high standing in the field of kalam. It begins by describing him as a meticulous researcher who carefully seeks the finest pearls of knowledge, progressing from the most elementary level (the smallest of the small) to the highest level (the commentary on the Greatest Creed), and moving from blind imitation (taqlid) to true verification (tahqiq). The author then declares that Sanusi's status in kalam became a proverb, illustrating with an anecdote from Sheikh Abu Imran, who said that when kalam was mentioned, he had never seen anyone who 'sifted' this science like Sanusi, meaning he analyzed and refined it thoroughly. The passage further notes that before his death, Sanusi was pleased to see his works, especially the 'Sanusiyyat', being embraced by students and even examined by his own teachers, who extracted a work called 'Haqa'iq al-Sanusi'. This shows the immediate recognition and impact of his scholarship. The footnote credits the anecdote to al-Shafshawani's work.

تقليد أعمى

Imam al-Sanusi's transition from taqlid to tahqiq and his meticulous sifting of kalam made him an enduring model of scholarly excellence.

Sanusi's Distinctive Method: Repetition with Novelty and Audience Diversity
Describes Sanusi's method of repetition with novelty and audience-appropriate language.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi combined repetition of core creedal content with novelty in presentation, tailoring his discourse to diverse audiences.

Core Idea
Sanusi's works balance repetition and novelty to reach every learner.

Sanusi's three creedal commentaries share core doctrines but each is uniquely presented. This passage shows how he deliberately addressed everyone from scholars to commoners, making his words sweet and effective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Sanusi's method
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noticing the description of repetition with novelty and the diversity of audiences addressed.
Pay attention to the terms 'خواص وعوام' (elite and commoners).
2
Identify the two main features
Find where the author mentions repetition with novelty and where he emphasizes audience diversity. Note the examples given.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: Why did Sanusi use such diversity? How does this approach help in teaching creed?
Consider the goal of 'استنقاذ المقلدين' (rescuing imitators).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترى فيها تكراراً في معالمها العامة ، ولكن مع جديد في أسلوب العرض ، وتنويع في الدليل والمثال ، وزيادة تنفرد بها كل « سنوسية » لا توجد في غيرها ، وكم ترى للعلماء نقولاً وتحريرات عن إمامنا السنوسي يختمونها بقولهم : كما في شرح العقيدة الكبرى » ، أو شرح العقيدة الوسطى » ، أو «شرح العقيدة الصغرى » ولا يمكنهم الاكتفاء بـ ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى » مثلاً عن غيرها وكل ناظر يعلم تنوع الخطاب الذي روعي فيه تنوع المخاطب فقد كان للسنوسي نية حسنة في استنقاذ المقلدين من جميع الشرائح ؛ فتراه يخاطب العـامـي والمختص ، والصغير والكبير ، والأمـة والصبي ، بلغة حريصة على التفهيم والبيان ، دون اشتغال بتنميق هذا كله جاءت «سنوسياته » حلوة الكلمات ، رائقة العبارات . ثم من الملامح البديعية في هذه السلسلة الموفقة : المزج الهادف والمتعمد لبعض الإشارات المعرفية على طريقة السادة الصوفية ، ولبعض الأدعية الرقيقة التي يختم بها فصوله على سبيل الإيناس والتذكير ، وشحذ الهمم واستلهام التوفيق ، ولبعض الأشعار والحكم والأقوال التي ترطب جفاف النص وتطرّي من خشونته ، وكم لهذا الملمح من أثر طيب ، وطمأنينة تسري في النفوس ، فلله دره من عالم تحریر موفق ! وقد لوّح الإمام السنوسي بوفاء هذه الطريقة في عرض الاعتقاد بالمقصود ، وبركتها وسلامتها من كدر الخوض فيما لا يعني ؛ فقد طالعة كتابه ( المنهج السديد ( المعروف بـ ( شرح الجزائرية » قال في وهو يتحدث عن ( منظومة الإمام أبي العباس الجزائري » : ( إذ هو منظوم مشتمل على طريقي هداية الخواص والعوام ؛ لأنه قد ضم فيه إلى حلاوة النظم المستميلة للطباع تقرير الأدلة البرهانية للعقائد على التمام ، ثم وشّحها بخطابات تصوفية تهزُّ النفوس النائمة لتعظيم جناب الحق ويدخل بها الضعيف مع القوي في سلك الانتظام ، وتلك سنة الله تعالى في تقرير الأدلة في كتابه العزيز ، ثم سنة مصطفاه الرسول وما أبركها من طريقة ، وأنصحها من دلالة ! لتضمنها الهداية العامة ، وإنالة البغية لكل موفق يروم إلى الحق الوصول )(۱) عصره نعم ؛ قد اشتعلت نار الغيرة والحسد في قلوب بعض علماء حينما رأوا عقائد السنوسي يُكتب لها التوفيق والمسيرة التعليمية ، ولم تلبث أن خبت ؛ رحمةً بالإمام وبهم من قبل ، قال العلامة المؤرخ الحضيكي في « طبقاته » : ( ولما ألف بعض عقائده أنكره كثير من علماء وقته ، وتكلموا بما لا يليق ، فكثر تغيره بذلك ، ثم رأى في منامه عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه واقفاً على رأسه يتهدده على الخوف من الناس ، فأصبح وقد زال حزنه ، وقوي على المنكرين فخرسوا من حينئذ ، ثم أقرُّوا بفضله ((۲)
You see in them repetition in their general features, but with novelty in the style of presentation, and variety in proof and example, and an addition unique to each 'Sanusiyya' not found in others. And how often you see scholars quoting and verifying from our Imam al-Sanusi, concluding with their saying: 'as in the commentary on the Great Creed', or 'the commentary on the Middle Creed', or 'the commentary on the Small Creed', and they cannot suffice with (the commentary on the Great Creed) for example over others. And every observer knows the diversity of discourse in which the diversity of the addressee was taken into account, for al-Sanusi had a good intention in rescuing the imitators from all segments; so you see him addressing the commoner and the specialist, the young and the old, the slave woman and the boy, with a language keen on instruction and clarification, without preoccupation with embellishment. All this made his 'Sanusiyyat' sweet in words, elegant in expressions. Then among the exquisite features in this successful series: the purposeful and deliberate mixing of some gnostic pointers according to the method of the Sufi masters, and some delicate supplications with which he concludes his chapters by way of familiarity and reminder, sharpening of ambitions and seeking inspiration for success, and some poems, wise sayings, and adages that moisten the dryness of the text and soften its roughness. And how great a pleasant effect this feature has, and tranquility that flows into souls, so how excellent is he as a successful scholar! And Imam al-Sanusi hinted at the fulfillment of this method in presenting creed as intended, and its blessing and safety from the trouble of delving into what does not matter. For I read his book 'al-Manhaj al-Sadid' known as 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya', he said, while discussing the poem of Imam Abu al-'Abbas al-Jaza'iri: 'It is a poem comprising both ways of guidance of the elite and the commoners; because he included in it, along with the sweetness of verse that attracts dispositions, the establishment of demonstrative proofs for beliefs in full, then he adorned them with Sufi discourses that shake dormant souls for the glorification of the station of Truth, and by which the weak enters with the strong into the order of discipline. And that is the way of Allah Almighty in establishing proofs in His Mighty Book, then the way of His Chosen Messenger, and how blessed is this method, and how sincere is its guidance! For it includes general guidance and attainment of the desire for every successful one who intends to reach the truth.' Yes, the fire of jealousy and envy was ignited in the hearts of some scholars of his time when they saw the creeds of al-Sanusi granted success and educational progression, but it soon subsided; out of mercy for the Imam and for them beforehand. The historian al-Hadiki said in his 'Tabaqat': 'When he authored some of his creeds, many of the scholars of his time denied it and spoke inappropriately, so his distress increased. Then he saw in his dream 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, standing at his head threatening him for fearing people, so he woke up with his grief gone, and he became strong against the deniers, so they were silenced from then on, then they acknowledged his virtue.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological description of Imam al-Sanusi's creedal works (the Sanusiyyat) and their reception. The author begins by noting that while there is repetition in general features across Sanusi's three creedal commentaries (al-Kubra, al-Wusta, al-Sughra), each has its own novelty, variety of proof and example, and unique additions. Scholars often quote them and cannot rely on only one. The key point is the diversity of discourse tailored to different audiences: Sanusi addressed the commoner and specialist, young and old, slave woman and boy, using clear, instructive language without excessive ornamentation, resulting in sweet and elegant expressions. Then the author highlights another feature: the deliberate mixing of gnostic references from the Sufi path, delicate supplications at chapter endings, and poems, wise sayings, and adages that soften the text and bring tranquility. This indicates Sanusi's method aimed at both rational proof and spiritual inspiration. The author then quotes Sanusi's own statement from his commentary on al-Jaza'iri's poem, where Sanusi praises the poem for combining the way of guidance for both elite and commoners: it includes sweet verse, demonstrative proofs for beliefs, and Sufi discourses that shake souls and include all levels. Sanusi sees this as following the divine method of the Quran and prophetic sunna, providing general guidance. Finally, the passage recounts the opposition Sanusi faced from some jealous scholars when his creeds became popular. Their fire subsided out of mercy, and the historian al-Hadiki narrates a dream in which 'Umar ibn al-Khattab appeared to Sanusi, threatening him for fearing people, after which Sanusi's grief vanished, he became strong, and his opponents were silenced and eventually acknowledged his virtue.

Key Terms
سنوسيات
خواص وعوام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi's works are mere repetitions of the same content without added value.
Correction: Each Sanusiyya has its own novelty in style, proof, and examples, and they are all valued by scholars.

Checkpoint
What did Sanusi avoid in his language according to the passage?
A) Repetition
B) Embellishment
C) Variety of proofs
D) Addressing different audiences

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's works are tailored to each audience while maintaining doctrinal core.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Sanusi wrote for both the commoner and the specialist because he wanted to rescue people from blind imitation. In which category do you fall? Do you strive to understand your creed from its sources, or are you content to follow without insight? What concrete step will you take this week to move from imitation (taqlid) to informed conviction?
?
The passage says Sanusi addressed even 'the slave woman and the boy.' Think of someone you consider beneath your attention in matters of faith—a child, a new Muslim, someone uneducated. How do you speak to them about Allah and His attributes? Is your language clear and kind, or do you use complex terms that confuse them? Will you commit to learning how to explain one creedal point simply to someone who needs it?
?
Sanusi's works are described as 'sweet in words, elegant in expressions' while being keen on instruction and clarification, not embellishment. When you speak about Islam—whether in teaching, conversation, or online—do you prioritize clarity and sincerity, or do you seek to impress others with your eloquence? What would change if you made 'instruction and clarification' your only goal?

Integrating Gnostic Pointers and Sufi Discourses in Creedal Works
Highlights Sanusi's blending of gnostic pointers and Sufi discourses with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi deliberately mixed rational proofs with spiritual elements to guide both elites and commoners.

Core Idea
Sanusi's method mirrors the Quran: proof and spiritual inspiration together.

Besides clear presentation, Sanusi enriched his works with Sufi references, supplications, and poetry. He explained this method in his commentary on al-Jaza'iri's poem, showing it as the prophetic way.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on spiritual features
Read the Arabic passage and translation focusing on the three features: gnostic pointers, supplications, and poetry.
2
Read Sanusi's own statement
Find the quote from 'al-Manhaj al-Sadid' where Sanusi praises al-Jaza'iri's poem for combining proofs and Sufi discourses.
Note how Sanusi sees this as following Allah's method in the Quran.
3
Understand the purpose
Reflect on why Sanusi included these elements: to moisten the text, bring tranquility, and guide both weak and strong.
Consider the phrase 'يدخل بها الضعيف مع القوي في سلك الانتظام'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترى فيها تكراراً في معالمها العامة ، ولكن مع جديد في أسلوب العرض ، وتنويع في الدليل والمثال ، وزيادة تنفرد بها كل « سنوسية » لا توجد في غيرها ، وكم ترى للعلماء نقولاً وتحريرات عن إمامنا السنوسي يختمونها بقولهم : كما في شرح العقيدة الكبرى » ، أو شرح العقيدة الوسطى » ، أو «شرح العقيدة الصغرى » ولا يمكنهم الاكتفاء بـ ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى » مثلاً عن غيرها وكل ناظر يعلم تنوع الخطاب الذي روعي فيه تنوع المخاطب فقد كان للسنوسي نية حسنة في استنقاذ المقلدين من جميع الشرائح ؛ فتراه يخاطب العـامـي والمختص ، والصغير والكبير ، والأمـة والصبي ، بلغة حريصة على التفهيم والبيان ، دون اشتغال بتنميق هذا كله جاءت «سنوسياته » حلوة الكلمات ، رائقة العبارات . ثم من الملامح البديعية في هذه السلسلة الموفقة : المزج الهادف والمتعمد لبعض الإشارات المعرفية على طريقة السادة الصوفية ، ولبعض الأدعية الرقيقة التي يختم بها فصوله على سبيل الإيناس والتذكير ، وشحذ الهمم واستلهام التوفيق ، ولبعض الأشعار والحكم والأقوال التي ترطب جفاف النص وتطرّي من خشونته ، وكم لهذا الملمح من أثر طيب ، وطمأنينة تسري في النفوس ، فلله دره من عالم تحریر موفق ! وقد لوّح الإمام السنوسي بوفاء هذه الطريقة في عرض الاعتقاد بالمقصود ، وبركتها وسلامتها من كدر الخوض فيما لا يعني ؛ فقد طالعة كتابه ( المنهج السديد ( المعروف بـ ( شرح الجزائرية » قال في وهو يتحدث عن ( منظومة الإمام أبي العباس الجزائري » : ( إذ هو منظوم مشتمل على طريقي هداية الخواص والعوام ؛ لأنه قد ضم فيه إلى حلاوة النظم المستميلة للطباع تقرير الأدلة البرهانية للعقائد على التمام ، ثم وشّحها بخطابات تصوفية تهزُّ النفوس النائمة لتعظيم جناب الحق ويدخل بها الضعيف مع القوي في سلك الانتظام ، وتلك سنة الله تعالى في تقرير الأدلة في كتابه العزيز ، ثم سنة مصطفاه الرسول وما أبركها من طريقة ، وأنصحها من دلالة ! لتضمنها الهداية العامة ، وإنالة البغية لكل موفق يروم إلى الحق الوصول )(۱) عصره نعم ؛ قد اشتعلت نار الغيرة والحسد في قلوب بعض علماء حينما رأوا عقائد السنوسي يُكتب لها التوفيق والمسيرة التعليمية ، ولم تلبث أن خبت ؛ رحمةً بالإمام وبهم من قبل ، قال العلامة المؤرخ الحضيكي في « طبقاته » : ( ولما ألف بعض عقائده أنكره كثير من علماء وقته ، وتكلموا بما لا يليق ، فكثر تغيره بذلك ، ثم رأى في منامه عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه واقفاً على رأسه يتهدده على الخوف من الناس ، فأصبح وقد زال حزنه ، وقوي على المنكرين فخرسوا من حينئذ ، ثم أقرُّوا بفضله ((۲)
You see in them repetition in their general features, but with novelty in the style of presentation, and variety in proof and example, and an addition unique to each 'Sanusiyya' not found in others. And how often you see scholars quoting and verifying from our Imam al-Sanusi, concluding with their saying: 'as in the commentary on the Great Creed', or 'the commentary on the Middle Creed', or 'the commentary on the Small Creed', and they cannot suffice with (the commentary on the Great Creed) for example over others. And every observer knows the diversity of discourse in which the diversity of the addressee was taken into account, for al-Sanusi had a good intention in rescuing the imitators from all segments; so you see him addressing the commoner and the specialist, the young and the old, the slave woman and the boy, with a language keen on instruction and clarification, without preoccupation with embellishment. All this made his 'Sanusiyyat' sweet in words, elegant in expressions. Then among the exquisite features in this successful series: the purposeful and deliberate mixing of some gnostic pointers according to the method of the Sufi masters, and some delicate supplications with which he concludes his chapters by way of familiarity and reminder, sharpening of ambitions and seeking inspiration for success, and some poems, wise sayings, and adages that moisten the dryness of the text and soften its roughness. And how great a pleasant effect this feature has, and tranquility that flows into souls, so how excellent is he as a successful scholar! And Imam al-Sanusi hinted at the fulfillment of this method in presenting creed as intended, and its blessing and safety from the trouble of delving into what does not matter. For I read his book 'al-Manhaj al-Sadid' known as 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya', he said, while discussing the poem of Imam Abu al-'Abbas al-Jaza'iri: 'It is a poem comprising both ways of guidance of the elite and the commoners; because he included in it, along with the sweetness of verse that attracts dispositions, the establishment of demonstrative proofs for beliefs in full, then he adorned them with Sufi discourses that shake dormant souls for the glorification of the station of Truth, and by which the weak enters with the strong into the order of discipline. And that is the way of Allah Almighty in establishing proofs in His Mighty Book, then the way of His Chosen Messenger, and how blessed is this method, and how sincere is its guidance! For it includes general guidance and attainment of the desire for every successful one who intends to reach the truth.' Yes, the fire of jealousy and envy was ignited in the hearts of some scholars of his time when they saw the creeds of al-Sanusi granted success and educational progression, but it soon subsided; out of mercy for the Imam and for them beforehand. The historian al-Hadiki said in his 'Tabaqat': 'When he authored some of his creeds, many of the scholars of his time denied it and spoke inappropriately, so his distress increased. Then he saw in his dream 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, standing at his head threatening him for fearing people, so he woke up with his grief gone, and he became strong against the deniers, so they were silenced from then on, then they acknowledged his virtue.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological description of Imam al-Sanusi's creedal works (the Sanusiyyat) and their reception. The author begins by noting that while there is repetition in general features across Sanusi's three creedal commentaries (al-Kubra, al-Wusta, al-Sughra), each has its own novelty, variety of proof and example, and unique additions. Scholars often quote them and cannot rely on only one. The key point is the diversity of discourse tailored to different audiences: Sanusi addressed the commoner and specialist, young and old, slave woman and boy, using clear, instructive language without excessive ornamentation, resulting in sweet and elegant expressions. Then the author highlights another feature: the deliberate mixing of gnostic references from the Sufi path, delicate supplications at chapter endings, and poems, wise sayings, and adages that soften the text and bring tranquility. This indicates Sanusi's method aimed at both rational proof and spiritual inspiration. The author then quotes Sanusi's own statement from his commentary on al-Jaza'iri's poem, where Sanusi praises the poem for combining the way of guidance for both elite and commoners: it includes sweet verse, demonstrative proofs for beliefs, and Sufi discourses that shake souls and include all levels. Sanusi sees this as following the divine method of the Quran and prophetic sunna, providing general guidance. Finally, the passage recounts the opposition Sanusi faced from some jealous scholars when his creeds became popular. Their fire subsided out of mercy, and the historian al-Hadiki narrates a dream in which 'Umar ibn al-Khattab appeared to Sanusi, threatening him for fearing people, after which Sanusi's grief vanished, he became strong, and his opponents were silenced and eventually acknowledged his virtue.

Key Terms
إشارات معرفية
أدلة برهانية
منهج السديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Including Sufi elements dilutes doctrinal purity or is merely decorative.
Correction: Sanusi deliberately includes them as part of a prophetic method to reach all audiences and soften hearts, as modeled in the Quran.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's quote, what does the poem of al-Jaza'iri combine?
A) Only rational proofs
B) Only Sufi discourses
C) Sweet verse, demonstrative proofs, and Sufi discourses
D) Poetry and supplications only

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's integration of spiritual elements aims for inclusive guidance for all levels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you study your creed, do you feel only intellectual satisfaction, or does it also stir your heart to love and awe of Allah? How can you seek both from this lesson's model?
?
Sanusi deliberately included spiritual elements to soften the dryness of the text. In your own journey of learning, are you reaching for the 'moistening' of your soul, or are you content with just 'dry' knowledge? What will you do today to invite spiritual nourishment?
?
The Prophet's way combined proof and inspiration. If you were to teach someone the basics of faith, would your method mirror this inclusive approach? What is holding you back from making your teaching more heartfelt?

Opposition to Sanusi and His Dream of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab
Recounts opposition to Sanusi's creeds and his prophetic dream of 'Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of opposition Sanusi faced and how a dream of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab strengthened him and silenced critics.

Core Idea
Divine support came through a dream of Umar, calming Sanusi and humbling his opponents.

Not everyone accepted Sanusi's innovative approach. Some scholars opposed him out of jealousy. The passage narrates how a dream of 'Umar transformed Sanusi's distress into strength, leading opponents to acknowledge his virtue.

Guided Path
1
Read the opposition narrative
Read the Arabic passage and translation describing the jealousy and denial faced by Sanusi.
Note the phrase 'اشتعلت نار الغيرة والحسد'.
2
Read the dream story
Read the account from al-Hadiki's Tabaqat about Sanusi's dream of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.
Note how the dream changed his state.
3
Reflect on the outcome
Consider how the dream resolved the conflict: his grief vanished, he became strong, opponents were silenced and later acknowledged his virtue.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological description of Imam al-Sanusi's creedal works (the Sanusiyyat) and their reception. The author begins by noting that while there is repetition in general features across Sanusi's three creedal commentaries (al-Kubra, al-Wusta, al-Sughra), each has its own novelty, variety of proof and example, and unique additions. Scholars often quote them and cannot rely on only one. The key point is the diversity of discourse tailored to different audiences: Sanusi addressed the commoner and specialist, young and old, slave woman and boy, using clear, instructive language without excessive ornamentation, resulting in sweet and elegant expressions. Then the author highlights another feature: the deliberate mixing of gnostic references from the Sufi path, delicate supplications at chapter endings, and poems, wise sayings, and adages that soften the text and bring tranquility. This indicates Sanusi's method aimed at both rational proof and spiritual inspiration. The author then quotes Sanusi's own statement from his commentary on al-Jaza'iri's poem, where Sanusi praises the poem for combining the way of guidance for both elite and commoners: it includes sweet verse, demonstrative proofs for beliefs, and Sufi discourses that shake souls and include all levels. Sanusi sees this as following the divine method of the Quran and prophetic sunna, providing general guidance. Finally, the passage recounts the opposition Sanusi faced from some jealous scholars when his creeds became popular. Their fire subsided out of mercy, and the historian al-Hadiki narrates a dream in which 'Umar ibn al-Khattab appeared to Sanusi, threatening him for fearing people, after which Sanusi's grief vanished, he became strong, and his opponents were silenced and eventually acknowledged his virtue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage attributes it to jealousy ('الغيرة والحسد'), not scholarly critique, and it ends with acknowledgement of his virtue.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
