The Method of al-Minhaj al-Sadid: Combining Proofs and Discourses
Praise of Sanusi's poem combining proofs and discourses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi's poem is praised for uniting demonstrative proofs and Sufi discourses to guide both the elite and the common, following the prophetic sunna.

Core Idea
Guidance combines rational proof and spiritual awakening.

This lesson presents a quotation from the commentary al-Minhaj al-Sadid, which praises Sanusi's poetic work for its unique method. The author highlights how the poem seamlessly blends rational arguments with Sufi discourses, making it accessible to both intellectuals and laypeople. This approach is presented as following the divine and prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the author's tone of praise and the key elements he highlights.
The passage is a quotation, so the 'author' here is the commentator of al-Minhaj al-Sadid.
2
Identify the two ways of guidance
The passage mentions 'the two ways of guidance for the elite and the common.' Identify what these two ways are and how they are combined.
Look for the mention of demonstrative proofs (adilla burhaniyya) and Sufi discourses (khitabat tasawwufiyya).
3
Reflect on the blessedness of the method
The author exclaims 'How blessed is this way!' Reflect on why he considers this method so praiseworthy, especially in light of the Quranic and prophetic precedent.
Consider how this method is said to follow the sunna of Allah and His Messenger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالمقصود ، وبركتها وسلامتها من كدر الخوض فيما لا يعني ؛ فقد طالعة كتابه ( المنهج السديد ( المعروف بـ ( شرح الجزائرية » قال في وهو يتحدث عن ( منظومة الإمام أبي العباس الجزائري » : ( إذ هو منظوم مشتمل على طريقي هداية الخواص والعوام ؛ لأنه قد ضم فيه إلى حلاوة النظم المستميلة للطباع تقرير الأدلة البرهانية للعقائد على التمام ، ثم وشّحها بخطابات تصوفية تهزُّ النفوس النائمة لتعظيم جناب الحق ويدخل بها الضعيف مع القوي في سلك الانتظام ، وتلك سنة الله تعالى في تقرير الأدلة في كتابه العزيز ، ثم سنة مصطفاه الرسول وما أبركها من طريقة ، وأنصحها من دلالة ! لتضمنها الهداية العامة ، وإنالة البغية لكل موفق يروم إلى الحق الوصول )(۱)
... and its blessedness and freedom from the murkiness of delving into what does not concern. He has read his book al-Minhaj al-Sadid, known as Sharh al-Jazairiyya, and he said, while speaking about the poem of Imam Abi al-Abbas al-Jazairi: 'It is a poem that includes the two ways of guidance for the elite and the common; because it combines the sweetness of poetry that attracts dispositions with the presentation of demonstrative proofs of beliefs completely, then adorned them with Sufi discourses that shake sleeping souls to glorify the side of Truth, and by it the weak enters with the strong into the order of regularity. And that is the way of Allah the Exalted in presenting proofs in His Mighty Book, and then the way of His chosen Messenger. How blessed is this way, and how sincere a guidance! For it includes general guidance and attainment of the goal for every successful one who seeks to reach the Truth.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from the author of al-Minhaj al-Sadid (a commentary on al-Jazairiyya) praising Sanusi's poem. It begins by noting the work's blessedness and its freedom from irrelevant matters. The author then describes the poem as encompassing two paths of guidance: one for the elite (khawass) through demonstrative proofs (adilla burhaniyya) and one for the common (awamm) through sweet poetry and Sufi discourses that awaken the soul. He emphasizes that this combination follows the sunna of Allah in the Qur'an and the sunna of the Prophet. The passage ends with an exclamation of how blessed and sincere this method is, as it provides general guidance and helps every seeker reach the truth.

Key Terms
المنهج السديد
طريقي هداية الخواص والعوام
الأدلة البرهانية
خطابات تصوفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think combining poetry with proofs diminishes theological rigor.
Correction: The author insists this combination actually follows the prophetic sunna and provides general guidance, strengthening rather than weakening the message.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two things does Sanusi's poem combine to achieve guidance for both elite and common?
A) Rational proofs and Sufi discourses
B) Grammar and theology
C) History and ethics
D) Fiqh and hadith

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's poem is praised for uniting demonstrative proofs and Sufi discourses, following the Quranic and prophetic model.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This method follows the Quran and the Prophet's sunna. Does your approach to learning and sharing Islam mirror this comprehensive model? What specific step will you take to combine reason and spirituality in your daily practice?

The Dream That Silenced the Critics
Story of scholars' envy and Sanusi's dream of Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of a dream in strengthening Imam al-Sanusi against his critics and how this event illustrates the psychological dimension of scholarly conflict.

Core Idea
A dream of Umar gave Sanusi the strength to overcome his critics.

This lesson recounts a famous episode from the life of Imam al-Sanusi. When his creedal works faced harsh opposition, he received divine support through a dream of Umar ibn al-Khattab. This story reminds us that scholarly authority is not just about argument but also about spiritual fortitude.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the emotional buildup: envy, distress, then the dream and resolution.
This is a biographical narrative, not a doctrinal argument.
2
Identify the key actors
Identify the deniers (scholars who opposed Sanusi) and the dream figure (Umar). Understand their roles.
Umar is known for his strength in truth.
3
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider why this story is included in a creedal work. It shows that even great scholars face opposition and find strength through divine means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعم ؛ قد اشتعلت نار الغيرة والحسد في قلوب بعض علماء حينما رأوا عقائد السنوسي يُكتب لها التوفيق والمسيرة التعليمية ، ولم تلبث أن خبت ؛ رحمةً بالإمام وبهم من قبل ، قال العلامة المؤرخ الحضيكي في « طبقاته » : ( ولما ألف بعض عقائده أنكره كثير من علماء وقته ، وتكلموا بما لا يليق ، فكثر تغيره بذلك ، ثم رأى في منامه عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه واقفاً على رأسه يتهدده على الخوف من الناس ، فأصبح وقد زال حزنه ، وقوي على المنكرين فخرسوا من حينئذ ، ثم أقرُّوا بفضله ((۲)
Yes, the fire of jealousy and envy had ignited in the hearts of some scholars when they saw the creeds of al-Sanusi being granted success and educational progress, and it did not take long until it subsided; out of mercy for the Imam and for them beforehand. The historian al-Haddayki said in his Tabaqat: 'When he authored some of his creeds, many of the scholars of his time denied him and spoke improperly, and his distress increased because of that. Then he saw in a dream Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, standing at his head threatening him regarding fearing people. So he woke up and his grief had vanished, and he became strong against the deniers, and they fell silent from that point, then they acknowledged his virtue.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage relates an episode of opposition to Sanusi's creedal works. It begins by noting the envy that arose in some scholars when they saw the success and educational spread of Sanusi's creeds. However, the fire of jealousy subsided out of mercy. The historian al-Haddayki reports that when Sanusi authored some of his creedal works, many scholars objected and spoke improperly, causing him great distress. Then Sanusi had a dream where Umar ibn al-Khattab stood over him, threatening him for fearing people instead of Allah. After this dream, Sanusi's grief lifted and he became strong against the deniers, who then fell silent and eventually acknowledged his virtue.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dream proves Sanusi's creedal works are doctrinally correct.
Correction: The dream is presented as a psychological support for Sanusi, not as a proof of doctrinal correctness. The story shows how he overcame his fear of critics.

Checkpoint

The dream of Umar ibn al-Khattab strengthened Sanusi, silencing his critics and showing the importance of trusting Allah over human opinion.

The Excellence of Tawhid and Sanusi's Leadership
Sanusi's statement on the unique role of tawhid and its fruits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Sanusi held tawhid in such high regard and how his statement links tawhid to knowledge of Allah and fear of Him.

Core Idea
Only tawhid among outward sciences yields direct knowledge and watchfulness of Allah.

This lesson introduces a passage from the biography of Imam al-Sanusi, where the author explains the driving force behind Sanusi's preeminence in kalam and tawhid. Sanusi's own words are quoted to show that tawhid is the unique science that gives knowledge of Allah and opens understanding of all other sciences. We'll explore this statement and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: the author's praise, then Sanusi's quote, then the outcome of his efforts.
Pay attention to the intensity of the phrase 'رغبة جامحة' (intense desire).
2
Identify Sanusi's claim about tawhid
Sanusi says there is no outward science that yields knowledge and watchfulness of Allah except tawhid. He also says that by tawhid, understanding of all sciences is opened.
This is a strong claim about the primacy of tawhid.
3
Reflect on the connection between knowledge and fear
Notice the causal link: according to the extent of one's knowledge of tawhid, fear of Allah increases. This shows that tawhid is not just theoretical but transformative.
4
Consider the result
Observe the outcome: Sanusi rose to become the head of this science and his works are praised as unmatched. This demonstrates the fruits of his sincere intention and high regard for tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولعل الرغبة الجامحة التي حملت إمامنا السنوسي إلى منصّة الإمامة في علم الكلام والتوحيد .. هي حسن ظنه بهذا العلم ، وصفاء نيَّته في تعلمه وتعليمه ؛ تعرف هذا من قوله رحمه الله تعالى : ( ليس علم من علوم الظاهر يورث معرفته تعالى ومراقبته غير التوحيد ، وبه يفتح فهم كل العلوم ، وبقدر معرفته يزيد خوفه منه تعالى ((۱) فحالفه التوفيق والتأييد ، فرقيَ دَرَجَ هذا العلم حتى رَأَسَ فيه وصارت تأليفه في علم التوحيد يُشار إليها بالبنان بالفضل ، حتى قيل فيها : ( وعقائده كافية فيه لا يعادلها شيء من العقائد كما أشار إليه ((٢)
And perhaps the intense desire that drove our Imam al-Sanusi to the position of imamate in the science of kalam and tawhid is his good opinion of this science and the purity of his intention in learning and teaching it. You know this from his statement, may Allah have mercy on him: 'There is no science of the apparent sciences that yields knowledge of Him, the Exalted, and watchfulness of Him except tawhid. And by it the understanding of all sciences is opened, and according to the extent of one's knowledge of it, his fear of Him increases.' So success and support were with him, and he rose in the rank of this science until he became its head, and his works in the science of tawhid were pointed to with fingers for excellence, until it was said about them: 'His creeds are sufficient in it, nothing of the creeds equals them, as his student al-Malali indicated.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage explains the driving force behind Sanusi's leadership in kalam and tawhid: his high regard for this science and his pure intention. It quotes Sanusi's own words: among all outward sciences, only tawhid produces knowledge and watchfulness of Allah, and it opens the door to understanding all other sciences; the more one knows tawhid, the more one fears Allah. As a result, Sanusi received divine support, rose to the highest rank in this science, and his works on tawhid became famously authoritative. A student remarked that his creedal works are sufficient and nothing equals them.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
التوحيد
مراقبته
خوفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It closes them off
B) It opens the understanding of all sciences
C) It replaces them
D) It has no effect

Key Takeaway
Sanusi teaches that tawhid is the unique science that directly imparts knowledge and fear of Allah, and it is the key to understanding all other sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your study of tawhid is the key to understanding all other Islamic sciences, or do you treat it as just another subject? What would change if you approached tawhid with that conviction starting today?
?
Sanusi says only tawhid gives direct watchfulness of Allah. When you recite the shahada or study attributes of Allah, do you actually feel watched by Him? If not, what is missing in your tawhid?
?
The more you know tawhid, the more your fear of Allah increases. Is your fear of Allah growing with your knowledge? If you are not more fearful, have you truly learned tawhid, or only memorized facts?

The Composition and Purpose of Sanusi's Sharh al-Wusta
Editor explains the date and rationale for Sanusi's commentary on al-Wusta.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances that led Sanusi to write his middle commentary, its place in his creedal series, and his goal of simplifying creed for beginners and intermediate students.

Core Idea
Sanusi wrote his middle commentary to bridge the gap between advanced and beginner students.

This passage from the editor introduces Imam al-Sanusi's commentary on al-ʿAqīda al-Wusṭā, explaining when and why it was written. We learn that students found his earlier commentary too lengthy, prompting a simpler intermediate work. Sanusi himself lamented the state of his time, a sentiment that further motivated his pedagogical approach. This lesson places the commentary within Sanusi's broader creedal project.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Read the passage to learn the date (875 AH) and the sequence of Sanusi's works. Note that this commentary came after both the Wusta and the Kubra commentaries.
2
Identify the motivation
Sanusi wrote this commentary at the request of students who found his longer work too difficult. Notice the preface's lament about the scarcity of good students.
3
Recognize the pedagogical purpose
Sanusi states that the aim is to simplify for beginners and intermediate learners. Consider how this intermediate commentary avoids verbosity and some debates.
This aligns with the core idea of bridging levels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك ألَّفَ إمامنا السنوسي هذا الشرح سنة ( ٨٧٥ هـ ) كما نص على خاتمة كتابه (۱) في وتأليفه قد وقع يقيناً بعدَ ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى » وتأليف « العقيدة الوسطى » بلا شكٍّ ، وكان ـ على ما يظهر من طالعته ـ بطلب ممن كان حول الإمام قد استصعب الكتاب الأول وطالت عليه أنفاسه ، تلك الطالعة التي شكى فيه الإمامُ متحسّراً أهل زمانه ، وقلة الخير فيهم ، ونُدرةَ طالب العلم الذكي الحاد الجنان ، وبسطة الدنيا واستيلاءها على قلوب البشر ، ونزارة العلماء ، فكيف به لو رأى أحوالنا وأحوال أهل زماننا ؟! فرقُ ما بين شرحي لا غرابة في توسط هاذا الشرح الذي بين أيدينا في ثنايا السلسلة العقدية السنوسية ؛ للإسهابِ الملحوظ الذي لا نراه فيما مهد به من الكتب قبله ، والإعراض عن مناقشة بعض الشُّبَهِ والآراء التي بسطَتْ العقيدة الكبرى » و « العقيدة الوسطى » : (۱) انظر ( ص ٥٧٠ ) (۲) ولذا قال : ( ولنقتصر على هذا القَدْرِ في هذا المختصر ؛ إذ الغرض منه التقريب على المبتدئ في هذا العلم والمتوسّط فيه ) ، وانظر ( ص ٢٥٨ ) .
That our Imam al-Sanusi authored this commentary in the year 875 AH as stated in the conclusion of his book (1). Its composition certainly occurred after 'Sharh al-'Aqida al-Kubra' and the composition of 'al-'Aqida al-Wusta' without doubt. And it was, as appears from its preface, by request of those around the Imam who found the first book difficult and its reading too lengthy. In that preface the Imam complainingly lamented his contemporaries, the scarcity of good among them, the rarity of the intelligent sharp-minded student, the extent of the world and its domination over hearts, and the fewness of scholars. So how would he be if he saw our conditions and the conditions of our time?! No wonder that this commentary before us is intermediate in the Sanusi creedal series due to the noticeable verbosity that we do not see in the books he prepared before it, and the avoidance of discussing some doubts and opinions that were expanded upon in 'al-'Aqida al-Kubra' and 'al-'Aqida al-Wusta': (1) See p. 570. (2) Hence he said: 'We will restrict ourselves to this extent in this abridgement, for the purpose of it is to bring close [understanding] to the beginner and intermediate in this science.' See p. 258.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note explaining the composition of Imam al-Sanusi's 'Sharh al-Wusta' (commentary on the Middle Creed). The editor states that Sanusi wrote this commentary in 875 AH, as he mentions at the end of the book. It was written after his longer commentary on the 'Kubra' (Greater Creed) and after composing the 'Wusta' (Middle Creed) itself. The motivation was a request from those around Sanusi who found the first commentary too lengthy and difficult. In the preface, Sanusi complained about his own time—lack of good people, scarcity of intelligent students, worldly distractions, and few scholars—suggesting he would be even more distressed if he saw the editor's time. The editor notes that this commentary is intermediate in length between the two others, avoiding the verbosity of the earlier works and omitting some discussions present in the 'Kubra' and 'Wusta'. He quotes Sanusi's own statement that the purpose is to simplify for beginners and intermediate students.

Key Terms
السنوسي
شرح العقيدة الوسطى
العقيدة الكبرى
المختصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sharh al-Wusta is an abridgement of Sharh al-Kubra.
Correction: Sharh al-Wusta is a separate, intermediate commentary written in response to requests for a shorter work, not an abridgement of the Kubra commentary.

Checkpoint
Why did Sanusi write his commentary on al-'Aqida al-Wusta?
A) To refute heretical innovations
B) Because students found his earlier commentary too lengthy
C) To summarize all his creedal works
D) As a response to a king's request

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's Sharh al-Wusta was written in 875 AH as an intermediate commentary to simplify creedal teachings for beginners and intermediate students, responding to their difficulties with his longer work.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi lamented the scarcity of intelligent students and the world's domination over hearts. In your own pursuit of knowledge, do you find yourself more driven by a love for the world or a love for Allah? What one change can you make today to align your priorities with true learning?
?
The commentary was written to simplify for beginners and intermediates. Have you ever taken for granted the accessibility of simplified Islamic texts, or felt impatient with beginners? How will you show gratitude for those who make knowledge easy, and how can you support others at the start of their journey?
?
Sanusi wrote this work in response to students who struggled. When you encounter difficulty in learning, do you humbly seek help, or do you give up? Commit to a specific step you will take the next time you feel overwhelmed in your studies.

The Composition of Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta: Motivation and Context
Sanusi states the date and motivation for writing his commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context and motivation behind Sanusi's commentary Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta.

Core Idea
Sanusi wrote Sharh al-Wusta to make creed accessible to students struggling with his larger work.

This lesson explores the background of Sanusi's intermediate commentary. We learn when it was written, why it was written, and how Sanusi lamented the spiritual state of his own time. This sets the stage for understanding the unique character of this work.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening lines
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning to '...إذا رأى أحوالنا وأحوال أهل زماننا؟' and review the translation. Notice the year and the context.
2
Identify the motivation
Look for the reason why Sanusi wrote this commentary. The passage mentions that people around him found the first book too difficult and lengthy.
3
Reflect on Sanusi's lament
Sanusi complains about the scarcity of good people, intelligent students, and the dominance of worldly concerns. Consider how this relates to the need for a simpler text.
This lament is a rhetorical feature that shows his concern for the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك كلمة عن كتاب شرح العقيدة الوسطى. ألَّفَ إمامنا السنوسي هذا الشرح سنة ( ٨٧٥ هـ ) كما نص على ذلك في خاتمة كتابه (1) وتأليفه قد وقع يقيناً بعد ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى ) وتأليف ( العقيدة الوسطى ) بلا شكٍّ، وكان — على ما يظهر من طالعته — بطلب ممن كان حول الإمام قد استصعب الكتاب الأول وطالت عليه أنفاسه، تلك الطالعة التي شكى فيه الإمامُ متحسّراً أهل زمانه، وقلة الخير فيهم، ونُدرةَ طالب العلم الذكي الحاد الجنان، وبسطة الدنيا واستيلاءها على قلوب البشر، ونزارة العلماء، فكيف به لو رأى أحوالنا وأحوال أهل زماننا ؟!

فرقُ ما بين شرحي ( العقيدة الكبرى ) و ( العقيدة الوسطى ): لا غرابة في توسط هذا الشرح الذي بين أيدينا في ثنايا السلسلة العقدية السنوسية؛ للإسهابِ الملحوظ الذي لا نراه فيما مهد به من الكتب قبله، والإعراض عن مناقشة بعض الشُّبَهِ والآراء التي بسطَتْ في ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى )، وخير الأمور أوساطها.

وقد نبَّه العلامة محمود بن سعيد مقديش الصفاقسي في ( حاشيته على شرح الوسطى ) إلى أنَّ مسائل (الوسطى ) نبذة من ( الكبرى )، وحواشي الكبرى تتضمَّنُ الكلام على مسائلهما معاً، لكن مسائل ( الكبرى ) ليست موافقة لها دائماً (1).

والمطالع في عقائد الإمام السنوسي يرى بجلاء انفراد كل كتاب عن غيره بجملة من المسائل والفوائد تجعله مقصوداً لذاته، وهذا من براعة التأليف التي قلّ أن تجدها عند مكثر.

ماذا في ( شرح العقيدة الوسطى ) ؟

كانت عناية الإمام السنوسي منصرفةً إلى شرح ( العقيدة الوسطى ) دون الوقوف على كل جملة من جملها أو كلمة من كلماتها، وقد انفرد هذا الشرح بإشباع مسائل عرض لها الإمام في غيره إيجازاً ولو كان هذا العرض في ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى )، وبإيراد مسائل لا تجدها في غيره؛ فمن ذلك:

- تجديد تشديده في مسألة التقليد، مع بيان خطورة الأخذ وإلحاقه برتبة النفاق؛ إذ نقل عن الإمام ابن دهاق بأنَّ النفاق نفاقان، الأول نفاق المقلَّد والثاني هو (؟) في أصول الدين، إلا أنَّه غيَّر يسيراً عما ذهب إليه في شرح العقيدة الكبرى؛ إذ جعل مذهب جمهور المتكلمين على...
That is a word about the book 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta'. Our Imam al-Sanusi authored this commentary in the year (875 AH) as he stated in the conclusion of his book (1) and its composition definitely occurred after [the composition of] 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra' and the composition of 'al-Aqida al-Wusta' without doubt, and it was — as appears from its opening — at the request of those who were around the Imam who had found the first book difficult and its subject matter lengthy for them, that opening in which the Imam complained regretfully about the people of his time, the scarcity of goodness among them, the rarity of the intelligent sharp-minded student of knowledge, the vastness of the world and its domination over the hearts of humans, and the scarcity of scholars; so how would it be if he saw our conditions and the conditions of our time?!

The difference between his two commentaries (al-Aqida al-Kubra) and (al-Aqida al-Wusta): There is no wonder in the intermediateness of this commentary which is in our hands within the midst of the Sanusi creedal series; due to the noticeable conciseness which we do not see in what he prepared from the books before it, and the turning away from discussing some of the doubts and opinions that were spread in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra), and the best of affairs is their middle course.

And the scholar Mahmud ibn Sa'id Muqdish al-Sfaqsi pointed out in (his gloss on Sharh al-Wusta) that the issues of (al-Wusta) are a sample from (al-Kubra), and the glosses of al-Kubra include discussion of both their issues together, but the issues of (al-Kubra) are not always in agreement with them (1).

And the reader in the creeds of Imam al-Sanusi sees clearly the distinctiveness of each book from others by a set of issues and benefits that make it intended for itself, and this is from the proficiency in authorship which is rarely found among prolific authors.

What is in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta)?

The attention of Imam al-Sanusi was directed to explaining (al-Aqida al-Wusta) without pausing at every sentence of its sentences or every word of its words, and this commentary is unique in expanding upon issues which the Imam presented concisely in his other works even if that presentation was in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra), and in presenting issues that you do not find in his other works; among that is:

- Renewing his emphasis on the issue of taqlid (imitation), with clarification of the danger of taking [by imitation] and attaching it to the rank of nifaq (hypocrisy); for he transmitted from Imam Ibn Dahaq that hypocrisy is two types, the first is the hypocrisy of the muqallid (one who imitates) and the second is (?) in the fundamentals of religion, except that he slightly changed what he went to in Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra; for he made the position of the majority of mutakallimin (theologians) on...
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is an editorial introduction to Sanusi's commentary on al-Aqida al-Wusta. It begins by stating the year of composition (875 AH) and confirms that this work was written after both Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra and the original al-Aqida al-Wusta. The motivation for writing is then explained: those around the Imam found the larger work (al-Kubra) too difficult and lengthy, so Sanusi composed this intermediate commentary. The opening of the work is quoted, where Sanusi laments the state of his own time — scarcity of good, of intelligent students, prevalence of worldly concerns, and few scholars — and remarks how much worse it would be if he saw our own times. The passage then compares the two commentaries, noting that the present work is intermediate in scope (tawassut), avoiding the lengthy elaboration of doubts and opinions found in al-Kubra, following the principle that 'the best of affairs is their middle course.' A comment from the scholar al-Sfaqsi is cited, indicating that al-Wusta's issues are a sample (nubdha) of al-Kubra's, though not always identical. The next paragraph emphasizes that each book in Sanusi's creedal series is independently valuable, with its own set of issues and benefits, showing his skill in authorship. The passage then poses the question 'What is in Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta?' and begins to list distinctive features, though the text cuts off mid-sentence. The first feature mentioned is a renewed emphasis on the issue of taqlid (blind imitation), where Sanusi stresses its danger, linking it to nifaq (hypocrisy), and quotes Ibn Dahaq's division of hypocrisy into two types, which he modified slightly from his earlier position in Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra. The passage ends abruptly, indicating that the enumeration continues in the original source.

العقيدة الكبرى
العقيدة الوسطى
السنوسي

Key Takeaway
Sanusi wrote Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta in 875 AH to provide a more accessible commentary for students who found his larger work too difficult.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Sanusi's lament about the scarcity of good and intelligent students, do you recognize that attitude in your own heart? Have you ever felt that 'people today' are worse, and that you are somehow better? What does that reveal about your pride? This week, will you actively seek to find goodness in those around you, especially those who struggle with learning?
?
Sanusi wrote a simpler commentary because students found the larger one difficult. Is there someone in your life who is struggling to understand Islamic creed? What are you doing to make it accessible to them, or are you content to stay in your own level of knowledge? Commit to one concrete action this week to help someone else understand a basic point of aqida.
?
The passage shows Sanusi responding to the needs of his students. Have you ever asked your teacher or scholar for clarification when you found something hard, or did you just give up? How will you change your approach to learning to be more like the students who requested this commentary? Write down one question you have been afraid to ask and promise to ask it before the week ends.

Distinctive Features of Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta Compared to Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra
Comparison of the two commentaries and enumeration of distinctive features.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta differs from Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra in scope and content, including its treatment of taqlid and hypocrisy.

Core Idea
Sharh al-Wusta is intermediate in length, avoids lengthy debates, and includes unique issues like a stricter view on taqlid.

This lesson explores the distinctive characteristics of Sanusi's intermediate commentary. We examine how it compares to his larger commentary and what unique content it contains, particularly regarding the issue of blind imitation (taqlid) and its connection to hypocrisy (nifaq).

Guided Path

2
Understand the intermediate nature
The passage says this commentary is intermediate (tawassut) in the series: it is less detailed than Kubra but more than the original text. It avoids discussing many doubts and opinions found in Kubra.
3
Identify distinctive features
Then read 'ماذا في شرح العقيدة الوسطى؟' and the beginning of the list. The passage highlights a renewed emphasis on taqlid and its danger, linking it to hypocrisy.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

Sanusi's Mission: Rescuing from Taqlid
Sanusi narrates his motivation and method for teaching creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's personal motivation for teaching creed and his approach to combating blind imitation through evidence.

Core Idea
True faith requires active evidence, not blind imitation.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi opens his heart to reveal why he devoted himself to teaching creed. He observed people clinging to corrupt beliefs and neglecting the proofs of tawhid. His response was not harsh condemnation but a gentle, persistent effort to clarify the truth with sound arguments, aiming to rescue them from the danger of taqlid (blind imitation).

Guided Path
1
Read Sanusi's narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of Sanusi's personal tone and purpose.
Notice the emotional investment: he speaks of 'rubbing the nose of Iblis' and breaking his back.
2
Identify the problems Sanusi saw
Look for the three problems Sanusi observed in people's beliefs. He mentions corruption, neglect of proofs, and abandonment of their own reasoning.
These problems motivated his teaching.
3
Understand Sanusi's method
Notice his gentle approach (التلطف) and his focus on universal teaching regardless of social status.
He didn't discriminate between lowly and noble.
4
Grasp the goal: rescuing from taqlid
Sanusi states his goal explicitly: to rescue from evil belief and the danger of taqlid. Understand why taqlid is considered dangerous in Islamic theology.
Taqlid means following without evidence; it undermines personal conviction.
5
Reflect on the imagery
The passage ends with vivid imagery of combating Iblis with brilliant proofs. Reflect on how this shows the seriousness of the task.
Sanusi sees his work as a spiritual battle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض الفسادِ في عقائدِهم ، وإعراضهم عن النظر في أدلَّةِ التوحيد وإهمالهم لكثيرٍ مِنْ مراشدهم ، فشرعتُ في إقراء هذه العقيدة وغيرها ، والتلطَّفِ في إيضاح الحقِّ بالبراهين لجميعهم ، وعدمِ الاكتراث بإبداء نفيس ذلك بين وضيعهم ورفيعهم ، قاصداً بذلك - والله سبحانه أعلم - إنقاذهم مِنْ سيَّي الاعتقادِ وخطر التقليدِ ، مُنبِّهاً لهم المرَّةَ بعد المرَّةِ على ما خَفِيَ عليهم مِنْ مهالك وقعوا فيها وقد حسبوا أنَّهم فيها على الرأي السديد وبقيت على هذا الأمرِ زماناً نُرغِمُ فيهِ أنف إبليس اللعين ، ونقطع ظهرَهُ ونكشفُ سحائبه التي يلقيها على الحقِّ بما نقدحُهُ مِنْ سواطع البراهين
[I observed] some corruption in their beliefs, and their turning away from examining the proofs of tawhid, and their neglect of many of their guides. So I began teaching this creed and others, and being gentle in clarifying the truth with evidence for all of them, and not caring about presenting its preciousness among their lowly and noble. Intending thereby - and Allah most high knows best - to rescue them from evil belief and the danger of taqlid (blind imitation), alerting them time after time to the hidden dangers in which they fell, thinking they were upon the correct opinion. And I persisted in this matter for a time, thereby rubbing the nose of the accursed Iblis in the dust, breaking his back, and unveiling the clouds he casts upon the truth by the brilliant proofs we strike.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a personal narrative in which Sanusi describes his motivation for writing and teaching the creed. He begins by noting the corruption in people's beliefs and their neglect of the proofs of tawhid and their own resources. In response, he started teaching this creed (likely referring to the Sanusiyya or similar work) and others, taking a gentle approach to clarify the truth with evidence for all people, regardless of status. His goal, as he states with humility, is to rescue them from evil belief and the danger of taqlid (blind imitation). He emphasizes that he repeatedly warned them about hidden perils they fell into while thinking they were correct. Then he describes his steadfastness in this effort, using vivid language: he rubs the nose of Iblis, breaks his back, and dispels the clouds Iblis casts over the truth with brilliant proofs. The passage underscores Sanusi's compassionate yet combative stance against ignorance and imitation.

Key Terms
التقليد
البراهين
التوحيد
الاعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Sanusi is criticizing all scholars or common Muslims as disbelievers.
Correction: Sanusi criticizes only corrupt beliefs and blind imitation, not the people themselves. He seeks to rescue them gently.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi identify as the main problem in people's beliefs that motivated him to teach?
A) Lack of knowledge altogether
B) Corruption in their beliefs and neglect of the proofs of tawhid
C) Disbelief in Allah
D) Rejection of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's motivation was to rescue people from blind imitation by gently teaching the proofs of tawhid to all, regardless of status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi observed that people had 'neglected their guides' (إهمال المراشد). What natural inclinations or intellectual tools has Allah given you to recognize truth, and how have you neglected them? What is one step you will take this week to use them again?
?
He taught 'all of them, lowly and noble.' Do you ever assume that creed is only for scholars, not for you? Today, are you willing to personally examine one proof for tawhid and commit to understanding it, not just repeating it?
?
Sanusi persisted 'for a time' rubbing Iblis's nose in the dust, breaking his back. What area of your life has Iblis clouded with doubt or indifference? Will you strike it with the brilliant proof of Allah's oneness and start a specific practice to strengthen your certainty?

Opposition and the Wisdom of Guarding Knowledge
Sanusi describes Satan's assault and quotes a poem on concealing knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi responded to opposition from Satan and ignorant followers, and why he quoted Zayn al-Abidin on concealing knowledge from the unworthy.

Core Idea
Sacred knowledge must be protected from those who would misuse it.

In this passage, Sanusi continues his narrative of the fierce opposition he faced when teaching. He describes how Satan, frustrated by the spread of truth, recruited a compound ignoramus to spread lies. Sanusi then cites a verse from the Quran and a poem by Zayn al-Abidin to explain why some knowledge must be hidden from those who cannot handle it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the vivid language describing Satan's assault.
The word 'السكوت' is likely an OCR error; the intended meaning is probably 'نقل عنا' (transmit from us).
2
Identify the opponent
The opponent is a 'compound ignoramus' (جاهل مركب) – someone ignorant of his own ignorance. How does Sanusi characterize his understanding and religion?
3
Understand the Quranic citation
Sanusi quotes Surah Al-Hujurat (49:6) commanding verification of news from a sinner. Why does he bring this verse here?
The verse warns against spreading unverified reports that cause harm.
4
Reflect on the poem
Read the poem by Zayn al-Abidin. What does it say about the consequences of revealing jewels of knowledge to fools?
The poet fears being accused of disbelief (worshipping an idol) and having his blood deemed lawful.
5
Draw the lesson
Consider Sanusi's use of this poem. What is the proper balance between spreading truth and protecting knowledge?
Sanusi is not advocating secrecy, but prudence to prevent harm.

فلمَّا أَنْ عظُمَتْ على الشيطانِ المصيبةُ ، وطالَتْ عليهِ مُدَّتها التي هي لجسمِهِ مضنيةٌ مذيبةٌ . . أجلب علينا بخيلِهِ ورَجِلِهِ ، وجرَّ إلى المجلسِ مِنْ أعوانِهِ مَنْ طُرِدَ عن فهم الحقِّ وعن معرفة أهله ، ثم هو مع ذلك جاهل بجهلِهِ ، فصار - والله سبحانه وتعالى حسيبه - ينقل [السكوت؟] عنَّا بحسَبِ فهمِهِ الأعوج ودينه الأعرج مِنَ الكلماتِ الكاذبة ما يُوجِبُ الإذايةَ في النفسِ والدينِ ، ويَقْبَلُ ذلكَ منهُ ويُشِيعُهُ مَنْ هو على شاكلتِهِ؛ ممَّنْ لم يمتثل قولَ اللهِ تعالى : يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِن جَاءَكُمْ فَاسِقُ بِنَبَاءٍ فَتَبَيَّنُوا أَن تُصِيبُوا قَوْمًا بِجَهَالَةٍ فَتُصْبِحُوا عَلَى مَا فَعَلْتُمْ نَدِمِينَ الله [الحجرات : ٦] . والله تعالى دَرُّ زين العابدين علي بن الحسين رضي الله عنهما حيثُ أنشد : إِنِّي لَأَكْتُمُ مِنْ عِلْمِي جَوَاهِرَهُ كَيْ لَا يَرَى ذَاكَ ذُو جَهْلِ فَيَفْتَتِنَا يَا رُبَّ جَوْهَرِ عِلْمٍ لَوْ أَبُوحُ بِهِ لَقِيلَ ذَلِكَ مِمَّنْ يَعْبُدُ الْوَثَنَا وَلا سْتَحَلَّ رِجَالٌ مُسْلِمُونَ دَمِي يَرَوْنَ أَقْبَحَ مَا يَأْتُونَهُ حَسَنَا
When the calamity became great upon Satan, and its duration prolonged for him, wearing out and melting his body, he assaulted us with his cavalry and infantry, and dragged to the gathering from his helpers one who was banished from understanding the truth and from knowledge of its people, and he, along with that, was a compound ignoramus. So he - Allah the Exalted and Almighty is his reckoner - began to transmit [?] from us, according to his crooked understanding and his lame religion, lying words that cause harm in soul and religion. And those like him accept it from him and spread it, among those who did not comply with the saying of Allah the Most High: 'O you who have believed, if a sinner comes to you with information, investigate, lest you harm a people out of ignorance and become repentant over what you have done' [Al-Hujurat: 6]. Allah bless Zayn al-Abidin Ali ibn al-Husayn, may Allah be pleased with them both, when he recited: 'Indeed I conceal the jewels of my knowledge, lest a fool see them and cause tribulation. O how many a jewel of knowledge, if I were to divulge it, would be said: That one worships the idol. And Muslim men would deem my blood lawful, seeing the ugliest of their deeds as good.'
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage continues the narrative. Sanusi describes the intense opposition from Satan and his human followers. When Satan's calamity grew severe, he brought his forces—both cavalry and infantry—to attack Sanusi. Specifically, Satan dragged to the gathering a person who had been banished from understanding truth and knowing its people, and who was a compound ignoramus (ignorant of his own ignorance). This person, relying on his crooked understanding and lame religion, began to transmit lying words from Sanusi that cause harm. Others like him accepted and spread it, ignoring the Quranic verse about verifying news from a sinner (Al-Hujurat:6). Sanusi then quotes a poem attributed to Zayn al-Abidin Ali ibn al-Husayn, in which the poet conceals the jewels of his knowledge to prevent fools from causing tribulation or accusing him of disbelief. The poem illustrates the wisdom of withholding sacred knowledge from those unworthy. Sanusi uses this to show that such opposition is not surprising, especially in the late ninth century when good is seen as evil.

Key Terms
الجاهل المركب
الحجرات: 6
زين العابدين
كتمان العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi is advocating for hiding knowledge entirely from everyone.
Correction: Sanusi is not advocating for hiding knowledge entirely, but for protecting it from those who would misuse it or harm the one who imparts it. The poem illustrates a cautious approach, not a policy of secrecy.

Checkpoint
What Quranic verse does Sanusi cite to criticize those who spread lies without verification?
A) Al-Hujurat 6
B) Al-Baqara 256
C) Al-An'am 50
D) Al-Ahzab 33

Key Takeaway
Opposition is inevitable, but wisdom lies in protecting knowledge from those who would corrupt it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever stayed silent about a truth you knew because you feared how others would react? In light of Zayn al-Abidin's poem, was your silence wisdom or cowardice? Write one specific situation where you will choose to conceal knowledge this week to prevent tribulation.
?
Think of a time you accepted someone's negative report about another person without verifying it yourself. How did that harm both you and the other person? How will you obey verse 49:6 from now on, starting with the next piece of gossip you hear?
?
Sanusi faced slander and false accusations even while teaching the truth. If you were in his place, would you continue teaching or retreat? What is the maximum sacrifice you are currently willing to make for the sake of sharing sacred knowledge?

Precedence of Saints over Scholars in Knowledge of Allah
States the claim of saints' precedence over scholars in knowledge of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic spiritual claim that saints (awliya) are ranked above scholars in knowledge of Allah after the prophets, and how this is supported by reference to al-Qushayri.

Core Idea
Saints surpass scholars in divine knowledge after the prophets.

This passage introduces a key principle in Islamic spirituality regarding the hierarchy of knowledge of Allah. While scholars possess exoteric knowledge, saints are endowed with direct experiential knowledge (ma'rifa). The author states their precedence after the prophets and notes a similar statement in al-Qushayri's Risala.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its English translation. Notice the concise style: a claim followed by a citation.
The passage is very short; read it carefully.
2
Identify the claim
The claim is clearly stated: saints precede scholars in knowledge of Allah after the prophets. No reasons are given here; it is presented as a principle.
The phrase 'بعد الأنبياء' (after the prophets) is crucial for ranking.
3
Note the authority cited
The author cites al-Qushayri's Risala as a source of a similar statement. Reflect on why referencing a well-known Sufi text strengthens the claim.
Al-Qushayri is a respected authority in Islamic spirituality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The precedence of the saints over the scholars in knowledge of Allah Almighty after the prophets, and a similar statement occurs in al-Qushayri's Risala.

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of the superiority of saints (awliya) over scholars (ulama) in knowledge of Allah. It asserts that after the prophets, the awliya hold the highest rank in this knowledge. The reference to al-Ghazali and al-Qushayri provides authoritative backing. The passage does not elaborate further; it simply states the claim and notes that al-Qushayri made a similar statement. This sets up the question that follows in the next lesson.

Correction: The passage specifically refers to knowledge of Allah (ma'rifa), which is a deep experiential knowledge, not the same as academic or juristic knowledge. Scholars are still highly respected, but this passage highlights a special rank for saints.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What concrete step can you take today to combine both paths?
?

Are you more attached to your academic titles and learned status than to genuine closeness to Allah? This lesson is a call to humility. What is one assumption you need to let go of to become a true seeker of Allah?
?
The source cites al-Qushayri's Risala as an authority. Have you ever studied a classical text on spirituality, or do you rely solely on modern scholars? If the greatest knowledge is with the awliya, how will you access their legacy? Commit to reading a few pages from a work like the Risala this week.

The Scholarly Legacy of Abd al-Jalil al-Qarawi
Ibn al-Abbar's biographical entry on Abd al-Jalil al-Qarawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly contributions and historical context of Abd al-Jalil al-Qarawi as recorded by Ibn al-Abbar.

Core Idea
Abd al-Jalil al-Qarawi: a forgotten scholar with lasting works in usul and creed.

This lesson introduces you to a notable but lesser-known figure from the fifth century AH. The historian Ibn al-Abbar provides a concise biographical sketch, listing his teachers, his expertise in usul, and his major writings. The passage serves as a window into the scholarly networks of al-Andalus and North Africa.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage once without analysis to get a sense of its content.
Notice the structure: name, teachers, expertise, works.
2
Identify the key figures mentioned
List the teachers and the author of the source. Note their significance.
Ibn al-Abbar is the historian; the teachers are Abu 'Imran al-Fasi, etc.
3
Analyze the list of works
Consider the titles: a work on usul al-fiqh, an abridgment, and a treatise on beliefs.
These show his specialization in both legal theory and creed.
4
Reflect on his historical context
Think about why such biographies are useful for understanding the transmission of knowledge.
Abd al-Jalil lived in the second half of the 5th century AH, a period of rich intellectual activity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن الأبار البلنسي في التكملة لكتاب الصلة » : ( عبد الجليل بن أبي بكر الربعي القروي ، يعرف بالديباجي وبابن الصابوني ، ويكنى أبا القاسم ، يروي عن أبي عمران الفاسي ، وأبي القاسم الخرقي وأبي عبد الله الأزدي صاحب القاضي أبي بكر بن الطيب ، وكان عالماً بالأصول ، مدرساً لها ، وله فيها تصانيف ، منها كتاب « المستوعب في أصول الفقه » ، ومنها كتاب « الانتصار » ، اختصره من كتاب « الانتصار » لأبي بكر بن الطيب ، وله ( رسالة في الاعتقادات » ) ، فهو من أعيان النصف الثاني من القرن الخامس
The scholar-historian Ibn al-Abbar al-Balansi said in 'al-Takmila li-Kitab al-Sila': (Abd al-Jalil ibn Abi Bakr al-Rib'i al-Qarawi, known as al-Dibaji and Ibn al-Sabuni, and his kunya is Abu al-Qasim. He narrated from Abu 'Imran al-Fasi, and Abu al-Qasim al-Kharqi, and Abu 'Abd Allah al-Azdi, the companion of al-Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib. He was a scholar of usul (principles), a teacher of them, and he had compositions in that field, including the book 'al-Mustaw'ab fi Usul al-Fiqh', and the book 'al-Intisar', which he abridged from the book 'al-Intisar' of Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib. And he has a 'Risala fi al-I'tiqadat'. He is among the notables of the second half of the fifth century.)
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry. The historian Ibn al-Abbar provides details about 'Abd al-Jalil: his full name, lineage, and kunya (Abu al-Qasim). He mentions his teachers: Abu 'Imran al-Fasi, Abu al-Qasim al-Kharqi, and Abu 'Abd Allah al-Azdi (who was a companion of al-Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib). 'Abd al-Jalil was a scholar of usul (principles, i.e., theology and jurisprudence) and a teacher. He authored important books: 'al-Mustaw'ab fi Usul al-Fiqh' (a comprehensive work on legal theory), 'al-Intisar' (an abridgment of Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib's work), and a 'Risala fi al-I'tiqadat' (a treatise on beliefs). He is considered one of the leading figures of the second half of the fifth century AH.

رسالة في الاعتقادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abd al-Jalil al-Qarawi is an obscure figure with no significant scholarly contributions.
Correction: This passage establishes his credentials as a scholar of usul and creed, author of multiple works, and a notable figure of his time.

Key Takeaway
Abd al-Jalil al-Qarawi was a prominent scholar of usul and creed in the 5th century AH, whose works include al-Mustaw'ab and a treatise on beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
He learned from specific teachers and then taught others. Who are the scholars you follow, and are you actively transmitting their knowledge to others, or are you just consuming it passively?
?

Hashwiyya's False Attribution to Imam Ahmad
Sanusi denies the Hashwiyya's false attribution to Imam Ahmad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hashwiyya's claim that Imam Ahmad shared their anthropomorphic beliefs is false and how Sanusi defends Imam Ahmad's orthodoxy in tawhid.

Core Idea
Following an imam in fiqh does not mean following him in creed.

Sanusi addresses a common historical distortion: the Hashwiyya, a group with anthropomorphic tendencies, claimed that Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal agreed with them because they followed his legal school. Sanusi firmly rejects this, asserting Imam Ahmad's unimpeachable orthodoxy in tawhid and his well-known role in refuting innovators. Let's read his defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: Sanusi identifies a false attribution and refutes it.
The passage is a single paragraph.
2
Identify the Hashwiyya's tactic
Notice how the Hashwiyya attempted to associate themselves with Imam Ahmad. They followed him in fiqh (furu') and implied that their creedal views were also his.
3
Understand Sanusi's rebuttal
Sanusi denies the association by stating Imam Ahmad's imamate in tawhid is agreed upon, and his debates with innovators are famous. This shows his beliefs were contrary to the Hashwiyya.
Sanusi uses the phrase 'Hāshā an takūna 'aqā'iduhu...' to express emphatic denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد لطَّخَتِ الحشويَّةُ بهذا المذهب الفاسد بعض أئمة أهل السنَّةِ ، فربَّما نسبوه لأحمد بن حنبل رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه (۲) ؛ إذْ هم مُقلّدونَ لهُ الفروع ، فأوهموا أنَّهم كما تبعوه في الفروع تبعوه في العقائدِ ، وحاشاه أن تكونَ عقائده رضيَ الله تعالى عنه مثل عقائدِهم ؛ إذْ إمامته في علم التوحيد على طريقِ أهلِ السنَّةِ مُجمع عليها ، ومناظرتُه لأهل البدع وامتحانهُ معَهم في ذاتِ اللهِ تعالى مشهور مستفيض رضيَ الله تعالى عنه ، وجزاه عن نفسِهِ وعن المسلمين أفضل الجزاء
And the Hashwiyya have sullied with this corrupt doctrine some of the imams of Ahl al-Sunna, so they sometimes attributed it to Ahmad ibn Hanbal—may Allah be pleased with him. For they are his followers in subsidiary matters, and they gave the impression that just as they followed him in subsidiaries, they followed him in beliefs. But far be it that his beliefs—may Allah be pleased with him—be like their beliefs! For his imamate in the science of tawhid according to the way of Ahl al-Sunna is agreed upon, and his debate with the people of innovation and his testing with them concerning the essence of Allah, exalted, is famous and widespread. May Allah be pleased with him and reward him with the best reward for himself and for the Muslims.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage defends Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal from being associated with the Hashwiyya's anthropomorphic beliefs. The Hashwiyya falsely claimed that Imam Ahmad agreed with them, because they followed him in fiqh (subsidiary matters) and thus implied they also followed him in creed. Sanusi strongly denies this, stating that Imam Ahmad's authority in tawhid according to Ahl al-Sunna is undisputed, and his refutations of innovators are well-known. The passage serves to distance the respected Imam from the corrupt doctrine of direction.

Key Terms

أحمد بن حنبل (Ahmad ibn Hanbal)
فروع (furu')
عقائد ('aqa'id)
توحيد (tawhid)
امتحان (imtihan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Imam Ahmad held anthropomorphic beliefs (like the Hashwiyya) because they followed his legal school.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that Imam Ahmad's beliefs are in line with Ahl al-Sunna, and his debates against innovators show he opposed anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint

A) Because they were his students in fiqh
B) Because they wanted to gain followers
C) Because they misunderstood his writings
D) Because they claimed he was their leader

Key Takeaway
Sanusi defends Imam Ahmad by distinguishing between following in fiqh and following in creed, affirming his orthodoxy in tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you blindly follow a scholar's rulings without verifying their creed? Are you personally accountable for distinguishing between fiqh and aqida in those you follow? What steps will you take to ensure your beliefs are aligned with the Sunni tradition, not merely inherited?
?
The Hashwiyya used their association with Imam Ahmad to justify their false creed. Are you aware of any teachers or groups you respect who might be misrepresenting the true teachings of the scholars they claim to follow? How will you investigate the actual creed of those you learn from?
?
Sanusi defends Imam Ahmad's orthodoxy with evidence. If someone accused a scholar you admire of holding a false belief, would you be able to defend them using textual evidence from their own works? What is one thing you can do this week to study the actual creed of a scholar you follow?

Ash'ari vs. al-Jubba'i on al-aslah
The commentator recounts the famous debate between Ash'ari and al-Jubba'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical background of the argument about children and how al-Ash'ari's response traces back to Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's famous argument was inspired by al-Shafi'i's insight.

This lesson provides the historical context for the theological debate about the fate of children. The commentator recounts an anecdote from Ibn al-Subki's Tabaqat, showing that al-Ash'ari's argument against the Mu'tazilite position was actually derived from a statement of Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this lineage helps appreciate the depth of Sunni theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that it is a report of a debate between two famous theologians.
2
Identify the key figures
Recognize Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu Ali al-Jubba'i, and their significance in Islamic theology.
3
Trace the argument's origin
Note that al-Ash'ari's answer is attributed to al-Shafi'i, demonstrating the continuity of Sunni thought.
The phrase 'if they concede knowledge' refers to God's foreknowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخفى أن أصل هذا الكلام خبر لشيخ السنة أبي الحسن الأشعري مع أبي علي الجبائي ، ذكره الإمام ابن السبكي في «طبقات الشافعية الكبرى » ( ٣٥٦/٣ ) وقال عقبه : ( واعلم : أن جواب شيخنا أبي الحسن مأخوذ من قول إمامنا الشافعي رضي الله عنه : « القدرية إذا سلَّموا العلم خُصِموا ) أي : إذا سلموا علم الله بالعواقب ) .
And it is not hidden that the origin of this statement is a report of the master of the Sunnah, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, with Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i. Imam Ibn al-Subki mentioned it in his 'Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Kubra' (3/356) and said after it: 'Know that the answer of our master Abu al-Hasan is taken from the statement of our Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him: "The Qadariyya, if they concede knowledge, are defeated." That is: if they concede God's knowledge of outcomes.'
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This note provides the historical background to the argument about children. It cites the famous debate between al-Ash'ari and al-Jubba'i recorded by al-Subki. The anecdote shows that al-Ash'ari's argument was inspired by al-Shafi'i's statement that if the Mu'tazilites admit God's foreknowledge, they are refuted.

Key Terms
خبر
شيخ السنة
القدرية
علم الله بالعواقب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari originated the argument himself without precedent.
Correction: The note shows that al-Ash'ari's answer was derived from Imam al-Shafi'i, indicating a chain of scholarly transmission.

Checkpoint

B) Abu Ali al-Jubba'i
C) Imam al-Shafi'i
D) The Quran

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's argument in the debate with al-Jubba'i was rooted in the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, highlighting the continuity of Sunni theological method.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari, a towering figure in Sunni Islam, did not claim originality but traced his argument back to al-Shafi'i. When you defend a belief, do you seek to anchor it in the tradition or do you prefer to invent your own reasoning? Where does pride in 'original thinking' lead you away from humility before the scholars who came before you?
?
The Qadariyya 'conceded' God's foreknowledge yet refused to accept its implications. In your daily life, do you truly live as if God knows every outcome—including your hidden sins and future decisions—or do you functionally deny His knowledge by acting as if your choices are outside His control? What one habit would change if you genuinely believed that God's knowledge governs every consequence?
?
This lesson is a mere footnote in a larger work, yet it preserves a vital chain of transmission. How many of your own beliefs about God and religion can you trace back to a source? If you cannot, are you willing to remain content with hearsay, or will you commit to verifying your religion as al-Ash'ari did by returning to the foundational imams?

The Story of Sawad ibn Qarib and the Jinni's Testimony
Sawad ibn Qarib relates his jinni's poem foretelling the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the testimony of a jinni served as evidence of the Prophet's prophethood and an additional miracle.

Core Idea
The jinn recognized the Prophet before many humans, testifying to his truthfulness.

This lesson recounts a remarkable event from the life of a Companion, Sawad ibn Qarib, who was visited by a jinni foretelling the coming of a prophet from the lineage of Lu'ayy ibn Ghalib. The jinni's poem serves as a unique testimony to the Prophet's mission, demonstrating that even the unseen creation acknowledged his prophethood. This story is a powerful illustration of the miraculous signs surrounding the Prophet's advent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the poetic structure and the narrative flow.
The passage contains two poems: one by Sawad and one by the jinni.
2
Understand the context
Sawad ibn Qarib was a companion who had a jinni (ra'ii) that would visit him. The jinni predicted the advent of a prophet from the Banu Hashim lineage.
This shows that even jinn were aware of the coming of the final prophet.
3
Analyze the jinni's poem
The jinni's poem marvels at the jinn seeking guidance and heading to Mecca. It emphasizes that truthful jinn are distinguished from liars and directs Sawad to go to the chosen one from Hashim.
The phrase 'truthful jinn are not like their liars' is key to the jinni's credibility.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this testimony is considered a miracle. The jinn's recognition of the Prophet before many humans and the preservation of this account in authentic hadith collections strengthen the proof of prophethood.
This story is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and other major hadith collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَتَانِي رَئِي بَعْدَ هُدْءٍ وَرَقْدَةٍ وَلَمْ أَكُ فِيمَا قد بَلَوْتُ بِكَاذِب (۱) ثَلاثَ لَيَالٍ قَوْلُهُ كُلَّ لَيْلَةٍ أَتَاكَ نَبِيٌّ مِنْ لُوَيِّ بْنِ غَالِبٍ (۲) فَرَفَّعْتُ أَذْيَالَ الْإِزَارِ وَشَمَّرَتْ بِيَ الْعِرْمِسُ الْوَجْنَا هَجُولُ السَّبَاسِبِ فَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ اللَّهَ لا شَيْءَ غَيْرُهُ وَأَنَّكَ مَأْمُونٌ عَلَى كُلِّ غَائِبِ وَأَنَّكَ أَدْنَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَسِيلَةٌ إِلَى اللهِ يَا بْنَ الْأَكْرَمِينَ الأَطايب فَمُرْنَا بِمَا يَأْتِيكَ مِنْ وَحْيِ رَبَّنَا وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيمَا جِئْتَ شَيْبُ الذَّوَائِبِ وَكُنْ لِي شَفِيعاً يَوْمَ لا ذُو شَفَاعَةٍ بِمُغْنٍ فَتِيلاً عَنْ سَوَادِ بْنِ قَارِبِ وكانَ رَئيهُ قالَ لهُ أَوَّلَ ليلة : [من السريع] عَجِبْتُ لِلْجِنِّ وَتَطْلابِهَا وَشَدِّهَا الْعِيسَ بِأَقْتَابِهَـا تَهْوِي إِلَى مَكَّةَ تَبْغِي الْهُدَى مَا صَادِقُ الْجِنَّ كَكَذَّابِهَا فَارْحَلْ إِلَى الصَّفْوَةِ مِنْ هَاشِمٍ لَيْسَ قُدَامَاهَا كَأَذْنَابِهَا(۳) حديث سيدنا سواد بن قارب أصله عند البخاري ( ٣٨٦٦ ) من حديث سيدنا ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما ، وهو بما فيه من أشعار رواه الطبراني في « المعجم الكبير ) (۹۲/۷ ) ، والحاكم في « المستدرك » ( ٦٠٨/٣ ) عن محمد بن كعب القرظي رحمه الله تعالى
My jinni came to me after stillness and sleep, and I am not, in what I have tested, a liar. Three nights, saying each night: a prophet from Lu'ayy ibn Ghalib has come to you. So I raised the tails of my garment and the strong, hard she-camel carried me swiftly through the vast desert. So I bear witness that there is nothing other than Allah, and that you are trustworthy over every unseen, and that you are the nearest of the messengers as a means to Allah, O son of the most noble and pure ones. So command us with what comes to you from the revelation of our Lord, even if in what you bring there is greyness of the forelocks. And be an intercessor for me on the Day when no intercessor avails a feather for Sawad ibn Qarib. And his jinni said to him on the first night: [in the meter al-sari']: I marvel at the jinn and their seeking, and their saddling the riding camels with their saddles, hastening to Mecca seeking guidance; the truthful jinn are not like their liars. So travel to the chosen one from Hashim, whose forelocks are not like their tails. (3) The hadith of our master Sawad ibn Qarib originally in al-Bukhari (3866) from the hadith of our master Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with both of them, and it, including the poems, was narrated by al-Tabarani in al-Mu'jam al-Kabir (7/92), and by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak (3/608) from Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage presents a historical account of Sawad ibn Qarib, a companion, who relates how a jinni (referred to as ra'ii) came to him predicting the emergence of a prophet from Lu'ayy ibn Ghalib (the Prophet Muhammad's lineage). The jinni's message is conveyed in a poem. The passage serves as a form of evidence for prophecy from the testimony of the jinn, an additional miracle. The text includes Sawad's own poem of testimony upon meeting the Prophet, affirming his belief in Allah and the Prophet's trustworthiness. The footnote traces the hadith to major collections. This is a biographical illustration of how even the jinn recognized the Prophet before some humans.

Key Terms
رَئِي
لُوَيِّ بْنِ غَالِبٍ
صَادِقُ الْجِنَّ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This story is merely a poetic fable with no evidential value.
Correction: The story is recorded in authentic hadith collections and is considered evidence of the Prophet's prophethood through the testimony of jinn.

Checkpoint
What does Sawad ibn Qarib's jinni tell him about the Prophet?
A) That the Prophet is from Quraysh
B) That a prophet from Lu'ayy ibn Ghalib has come to him
C) That the Prophet will be born soon
D) That the jinn will follow the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The jinn's testimony confirms the Prophet's truthfulness and serves as a miraculous sign of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sawad received a clear, repeated sign from a jinni and acted on it. When the call of Islam reaches you—through the Qur'an, a reminder, or a sermon—do you respond with the same urgency? What stops you from immediately obeying?
?
The truthful jinn recognized the Prophet before many humans. Are you quicker to follow the truth than a jinni? Examine your heart: is there any pride or doubt that delays your submission to what you know is true?
?
Sawad sought the Prophet's intercession on the Day when no intercessor avails. Do you genuinely rely on the Prophet's intercession, or do you assume it without reforming your life? What change must you make today to be worthy of that hope?
